O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, three dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine together with its fulfillment, and I have made the end through its explanations and through its declarations. 
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".  
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fortified in our region and is strange everywhere, so has the science perished and been cut off, and nothing remains of its force except small descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved. 
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this have come error and vanity, and are closed the understandings and is alienated the science.  
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I want to revive it together with the order of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of the other tools of the work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary. 
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason of those that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is elongated. 
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to climb in the science of anatomy, as Galien says, until he knows the judgment of the members, and the forms and conjunctions and separations of joints, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of vessels, and the movement and of moving and resting veins, and their place of exit. 
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this Hippocrates says that the hand with the name is little, and with the work is much; and likewise in the art of the hand. 
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the things said before, if he guards himself so that he does not fall into error and that he does not harm men; even as I have often seen many of those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and without experiment.  
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a fool who cut an abscess of scrophules or neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; for that so much blood issued out that the woman fell dead in his hands. 
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And behold another case who treated a stone from a man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he carried away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.  
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called for this treatment, and I see the disposition of the patient and the size of the stone, and well if one cut it they would die. 
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And look at another case that happened to the duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the fracture there was a wound; and the doctor full of ignorance put the fracture on the wound with strong ligatures, and did not let any ointment go onto the wound, and left it thus; and he commanded him that he not untie it at all; and remained thus that the leg was completely swollen and the foot and came to ruin. 
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come to untie the leg; and when I moved it out of place, he was in peace and felt no pain. 
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all ways the corruption was already confirmed or member, and it could not heal it; and did not cease the corruption to go through the member as long as the members were throughout lost.  
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another kind which breaks open the abscess and then inflames by the evil of its lordship.  
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a sore, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it is not proper that one touch it with iron unless in such a place where one can remove all that is corrupted. 
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that the work of the hands is divided into II divisions: that is to say, work where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger. 
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For that reason it is necessary that you guard yourselves so that foolish people cannot speak badly of you. 
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galens says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a bad illness unless you are called a fool by the wise.  
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.  
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are of fire cauteries and of medicinal cauteries, and the chapter is ordered from the head to the feet; and the forms of the instruments, and the making of cautery irons, and of all that is necessary in the work. 
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and examining, and of leeches and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and is the chapter ordered and the forms of the instruments. 
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is to restore dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered of the head just as far as the feet, and forms of the instruments. 
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus as we remember from the work, it is necessary that I say the quality of the aid and of the annoyance of each complexion.  
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of help, and of nuisance, are the longest discourse and most subtle science, and the secrets replied; and of this speak the most sages, and agree to this; and I suffice them little words, because I fear the length. 
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery helps universally to all complexion or it has matter, except for two complexions: that is to say hot complexion without matter, and dry complexion without matter.  
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together matter, some said that cautery is great help; and the others said the opposite: that cautery is not good for illness that comes from heat and dryness. 
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and it should not be treated for a hot disease by heat, nor by dryness; and he who says the contrary that cauterization does great help to a hot and dry disease that comes in the bodies of men.  
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you examine the body of man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold. 
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree to this word. 
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never by experiment.  
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in every way, let no one interfere except he who has experienced it and knows by long usage the chapter of cauteries, and the variety of complexions of men, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and the space of time; of other complexions we have no more fear, even in cold and moist diseases. 
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the masters assembled and agreed on the cautery.  
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, sons, that fire cautery together with secrets of the treatments and more good than cautery of burning medicine. 
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the heat is simple, and does not come forth except to the member which is burnt, and does not harm another member besides that one. 
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The hot medicines come from member to member in separating, and bring to the member diseases of grief healing; and by chance kills the patient The fire because of his height and for the goodness of his substance does not do this, if there is not superfluity. 
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And these things I have found by experiment and by the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it was on the truth of things; and for this I excuse myself from the length of speech, because it does not please me that I would steal from you the secret which is contained in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; or receive it in your thoughts. 
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that it is agreed upon in what time cauteries should be made, and how long they are to be applied. 
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is suitable in all times, because the harms occurring are reduced with the help of cautery; and even if the cauterization is for necessary pains before and until they cannot wait for the time when greater evil may come to the member. 
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear child, like the fools do; for a sickness which is healed by cautery has no return; and they say so; but it is not as they believe, because cauteries are only medicine that changes complexion, and dries up humors which are the cause of pain, and is worth more than medicine for the speed of its value, and for the virtue of its work and of its authority. 
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the most important thing is that the patient comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the sickness and its virtue; and superfluities are assembled in him by the acquisition of meats and similar things, if it isn't cauteries administered in their place where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries of teeth for pain, and similar things, and this pain does not return; but this happens little.  
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worth after medicine, but their understanding is false, and it is cautery the last of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any disease and they are not worth it, then we administer the cautery, and it is worth.  
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish people. 
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cautery instruments of gold are better than those of iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and the height of its substance; and they said that the cautery wounds do not cause rotting, but this is not true because I have tried it, and found that it is true in some people; and gold cautery is worth more than iron, as they say.  
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And nevertheless when you heat instrument of gold, you do not know well when it is heated by the color of the gold, and if it cools too quickly; and if one heats it too much; so it is done at the fire; and thus there is enough hindrance. 
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use our fire cautery which we have seen useful in our work.  
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or I have ordered this chapter of the head down to the feet, so that the path may be easier to find. 
dou cautere olivaire	of the olive cautery 
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and there are two ways to make it by reason of a disease called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head as the eyes, and ears, and because of a multitude of dreams and toothache and sore throat, and also all diseases that come from cold such as paralysis and stroke and apoplexy and similar diseases.  
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a medicine solutive softening the head III or IV, according to what the virtue and age and habit of the patient can endure; and then make rear the head of the patient. 
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on your feet; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his neck between his two eyes; and where your two fingers will come, if it bleeds then cauterize with the cautery called "olivare", because of this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, and do in descending and pulling your hand back and forth while turning it; then gently lift your hand, and look at the place if you see the bone I told you; and if you do not see it, begin the cautery again until you see the bone as I told you; after take a piece of wool, and put in soft cotton inside, and put on the spot, and let it be for III days; after put on a moist cloth in butter; and leave it on until the burn is gone; after cure the wound with the ointment which is called «tetrafarmaçon», until it is healed. 
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said the ancients, that when a wound stays open longer, it purges more; and for that reason, they helped it to heal. 
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said any of these that one must let the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then sew up what is burned of the bone, and be cured. 
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that one must leave the cautery thus, and push so strongly that it lowers the bone as wide as the whorl that women put in their spindles for that the humors may come out more; and one must leave the wound long open; after which one must cure and soothe. 
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two manners of cauteries do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the head the is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more safe and sure for me, and of this I work therefore altogether salvation.  
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of the ancient pain of the head 
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head comes chronic pain, and lasting long, the patient must use herbs and pills that are called 'cochie,' and of purgation of head and oils and plasters; and if one makes him the cautery that we have said before, and it does not work.  
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the shoulder of the patient is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; therefore cauterize it under that cautery a little as we have said above. 
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After do cautery on each horn of the head until the bone, as we have said before, and do the cautery where they are called "vasselz"; and it is there that one puts suction cups; and align your hand so that you do not see until the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it later; and it behooves the cauteries of the horns to be more subtle than those with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form: 
dou cautere dou chief	of cautery of the head 
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain, and it is extended to the eye, and the neck is purified by softening medicines, and one has done the other cures that I have said in the division of maladies, and all this does not profit: therefore I make cauteries according to II manners, that is to say of medicine sharp and of fire.  
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine cautery is this that you take a piece of alum, and remove the bark and cut it in two pieces, and then make the place where the pain holds in such a manner that you can put the piece of alum under the skin; and when it will be placed so put it together and hold it tightly and let it for XII hours; and then untie it and take away the piece of alum, and let the wound like this II days or III; then put on top ointment in butter as long as it endures. 
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of ointment until it is healed; and if you see so do any of some medicines burning that I have written or in a tenth treatise of burning medicines.  
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done this way. 
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery of which here is the form: 
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And is called "closed" because the head is made in the shape of a clo, where it has I the point of curvature, and in the middle a small appearance; and place it on the painful place, and hold your hand and move the fire a little lightly, until the half of the thickness of the spear of heart is burned; and raise your hand that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and run an abundance of blood. 
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in awe of silk, and put on the place for III days; then put cotton moistened with butter, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery that is called "cultellare," at all the tip, and keep from covering the artery in this migraine which is not ancient. 
de emigraine	of migraine 
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure migraine as we have said before in divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit, and see that the cauteries before said of medicine and of iron do not help him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called «cultellare» until it is white; and reign thus on the painful place a line of half a palm long, and withdraw your hand once, and restrain yourself so that you do not cut the artery and that you do not come close to the bone; and guard yourself from the jawbone that moves when one pushes, and the nerve does not feel that it is moved and that spasm does not come to the patient, and guard yourself from bleeding of the artery when it will be cut, or cutting has great fear and especially for the one who does not know it, and who is not studying and experienced; and leave the work in mid-way; but I will tell you how to restrain blood when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it is discussed in this book. 
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice to the malady, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him in the middle of the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or chapter of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has II knives; and this cautery is better than that one and more helpful. 
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and one puts there opening of medicines solutives and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not change, then take this cautery which is called "point," for this is the form. 
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After pricking all around the ear of the sick person, or where the pain holds in both, and you move away a little upward from the root of the ear once you have marked the place to cut; and make X prickings around each ear; after cure the place until it is healed. 
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth's torture 
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torment which must be cured by cautery are not others than those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses; and do not make cautery on resemblances that come from dryness and sprain of nerves. 
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this likeness of torture which weeps with phlegm from the eyes and expulsions from the head and gargles, and that does not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with III cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and the other a point fire on the temple, and the third at the adjustment of the two lips; and put the cautery in the part which opens healthy, and make cautery toward the top of the ear above a point below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cautery so long that the middle of the heart is burned; and this is the shape of the cautery: 
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And is the likeness of the scalpel that we have put before, but it is a little more subtle and it is fitting that the knife be a little larger; after curing its place as I have said before, until it is healed. 
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then I make IIII cauteries: II on the II horns of the head, and I in the middle of the head, and I at the place which is called "vessels" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and be cured as we have said before. 
de litargie	of lethargy 
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	To this illness it behooves to give the patient large potions and pills that mollify the brain; after which raise the head of the sick person completely, and place on the occiput the plaster of mustard which is written or treated in plasters; and this is the manner of the cautery: if you do so as I have said. 
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy thus, well; and if it is not, make III cauteries of the middle from the head descending to the neck, and have a space between each cautery I finger thick; and cure it as the others, and if you see it joined again, and the patient suffers, make I cautery in the middle; and if necessary II others on the II horns, and cure it until it is healthy; and let the cauteries be called "olivare," as I have said before. 
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head 
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of herbs and of what we have said before; after this cleanse the head of the patient, then make a cautery on the head and on each corner, and I behind and III on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the illness is gone, make IV cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it until the most of the heart is burned, and raise your hand; after this care as long as it is healed, and the cauteries which are called «olivare» that we have said before. 
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy 
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic ones should not use fire cautery except that one who is phlegmatic, and it conviene first to modify the brain of herbs and other cures that we have said in the division when the patient is great and suffers from bad medicine.  
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot suffer it, make gargarisms and mastication modifying the brain often with good meats; after the king of his head in the middle, and I do cautery according to what we have said before, and the cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is for and suffering, I do cauteries as I said to the one who has paralysis and softening of body, on the spine of the back and neck, and be the cauteries olive according to the manner that I have said.  
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, do the cautery subtly according to this manner. 
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When by reason of melancholy are the superfluities or humors corrupted and phlegm thick, then one cauterizes with those cautery as we have said to him who has paralysis. 
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if by reason of melancholy the superfluities are declining to melancholy, and the body of the sick man is moistened, then give him to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to that which is before in the division. 
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After raise the head of the patient; after make I torteil of linen well made, as well as the circle, so it put in between the head; and the patient sit crossed, and be well held on all sides; after present the liniment, and worth moves of butter of sheep old; and the heat to fire temperately, so that the two should suffer if he put it; after empty the circle from inside in the head, and let it cool; and make this to the patient each week once with other good governance, until it be healthy. 
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you see cauterize him by making more points all over the cautery. 
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery moistens the brain; and then puts on cotton moistened in butter and fat of lard. 
de l’awe des eulz	of the awing of the eyes 
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes first to the eyes by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do drink to the patient a thing purifying the head, and keep him from all moisture, and let him sweat or bathe more times fasting.  
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he commands to rear his head, and he makes a cautery in the middle of the head, and he makes II cauteries on the II temples if the descent of the awe is at the II eyes together, or in I if the descent is in I; and cut with all the cauteries all the veins and arteries that are below the heart, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against the loss of blood, and if you see too much blood issue, so restrain it with as much power as you have. 
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I shall teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision, the precaution how to stop it; and sometimes one does cauterize or burn beneath the two bones behind.  
dou cors des larmes	of the body of tears 
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that these are cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then I make the cautery as I said at the beginning of this work, descending to the eyes: I cauterize the top, and II cauterizes on the two temples, and II cauterizes under the two bones; and if there is need for more, then one cauterizes carefully above the eyebrow with all small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Tears from within the eyes 
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not profit at all, then give the patient III nuts of cochineal; after which rub the head, and make a cautery or middle of the olive cautery; and make II cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" on the II wrists, one under the cheekbones; and beware of the artery that you do not cover it. 
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis": 
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the parchment of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then the cauterization of this cautery which is called “olivare”. 
de coi ci est li forme:	of this is the form: 
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see so do it II cautery on the II eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and let not the hand off except until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said. 
dou poil qui point l’oil	The hair that pricks the eye 
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are converted to the eyelid and prick the eye, and one does cautery according to II manners: that is to say of fire or of burning medicine. 
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.  
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are equal, then put the patient in your healthy; after mark on the paper of the eyes a figure that be as the leaf of myrtle, and be the beginning of the sign beside the hairs; then i put cotton moistened in the white of an egg and mash of persil on the eye, then heat the cautery of this which is the form: 
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterize upon the figure that you have signed point and point many times, that the hairs be burned at the place; and the signs of the health of the work is that you see the paper retreated, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave thus III days, then put cotton moistened in butter until the burn is removed; after the cure of ointment until it be healed. 
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And after this, if the hairs come and the paper is softened, then begin the cautery again on that same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are outward, cauterize them until the paper is raised to its natural place, and is even, and do not prick the hairs with the eye. 
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauteries of medicine burning is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make of parchment the form of the leaf of myrtle; then take of French soap and live coals, of each one part, and grind together well; and do it hastily, so that it does not cool, then spread on the form that you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and put under the eyes; and if the patient holds in the eye only, so must one operate in it, and if in both; and put under the eye cotton moistened in a broth of egg; and the head of the patient be in your lap and put your hand showing on the medicine, and press it and squeeze every time that the patient feels burning from the medicine, for he feels burning as with fire. 
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine to your place.  
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the cautery shall have passed, lift the place of awe, and look if you see the paper raised as if it were raised by constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is well. 
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If this is not the case, then put back on the medicine where it did not open, until your works are equal, and your eyes are set; then put on moist cotton in butter until the burn is cooled, after cure the place of the ointment which is called "diaphines" and another, until it is healed. 
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary that you guard well your work with great care so that no medicine falls into the eyes. 
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then resume the medicine on that part which is softened by the paper properly, as you have done before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the form of the myrtle leaf: 
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to these be your constraints; and let not the right way be returned to him whose is the study of this art. 
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the cure of fistula by cautery 
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you cure a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your cures do not benefit, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner. 
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy one; and hold his head between your hands in such a manner that he does not move or lower his head; after putting moistened cotton in the bin of an egg or in the juice of parsley on the eye; after heating the cautery which is this: and it is placed on the head as if it were the shape of a goose feather, together with the quill being the cautery; if you see, so it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, so it be like a tent; but nonetheless, this which is placed is worth for your work. 
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After the fistula is opened, treat the pus and dryness; and if it is closed, open it again, and treat it from within; after put the hot cautery on top, and hold your hand on the cautery to the part above the eye, so that your hands do not make a mistake; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it. 
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.  
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If this is not done, if the cautery must be started again once, and another one if you need it, and leave it for III days; after that put cotton moistened in butter on top, and cure with drying ointment until it is healed, and if XL days pass and it is not healed, then put medicine corrosive on it as long as the bone is uncovered; and the king according to what comes up in his chapter. 
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said. 
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Attend to the fistula, and cut it open; after put into the fissure the most subtle camphor of which this is the form: 
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the quantity of one [third] of plumb; and hold your hand or hammer firmly, and let the patient not move at all so that the melted lead doesn't run into his eye; and it is necessary to put on the eye of the patient cotton moistened in wine of rue or in eyewash: the lead sits in its place of fistula, and the healthy by miraculous health. 
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.  
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If this is not the case, it is necessary to administer purging to the nostril and bring the fistula back to the body of the nostril according to what is proper in its own place. 
des crevaices en levres	of the openings in lips 
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times there are wounds in lips which are called “hair”, and even in children’s lips. 
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these wounds with those that we have said in the divisions, and the treatment is not beneficial, then use this small scalpel cautery according to this form. 
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it carefully into those crevices until it comes to the font; after care for the place with cerote until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat 
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or the cheek, or palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it makes rot and swelling, and is evacuated, and becomes a fistula; and you cure it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit; then it is necessary that you have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after the bottom or opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron touches the bottom of it, and at its last place; and do thus once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, that is good; and if this one, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to those that you will find in its chapter. 
dou movement des dens	of the movement of the teeth 
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and this is not worth it, then put the head of the patient in your own; after heat the cautery whose form will come here afterwards in such a manner that you put a chain over the tooth; and put inside the cautery hot as much as possible, and hold so long that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after release your hand and restart the cautery according to your will; after fill the mouth of the patient with salt water, and keep it for an hour and pull out strongly. 
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such manner the tooth that was moving is thus confirmed, and the softened gum restrained, and the moisture corrupted dry. 
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of teeth 
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold or dampness, and the cures of medicine are not worth it, then there is need for cautery in two ways: cautery of butter and cautery of fire.  
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	A cautery of butter is such that you take butter of the vat and put the end in a spoon of iron or brass; after take cotton and wrap it over the point of a tent, and moisten it in the melted butter, and place it on the aching tooth gently and hold until it is cooled; and so often do this until its virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that wool and cotton are cold and wet in butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and put on the hot iron until the fire comes to the summit of the tooth.  
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery with fire is such that you prick a piece of iron or steel, and it should be thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after warming the cautery, which will come in form later, put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be removed the same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the haste of this cautery, and then the root be heated; and this is the form of the cautery: 
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery where you want, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the caine: 
des scrophules	of the scrofulas 
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrophules are of phlegm and cold moisture, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then cauterize with a heated iron as is explained after, and have it have openings for the fumes to issue from the cautery on the other side; and put the hot cautery upon the abscess once, where it is necessary, until it comes to the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it so for III days; and put upon cotton moistened in butter as long as the burn is removed; after cure the place with ointments and tents until it is healed. 
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the dog: 
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the humors overcome in the channels of the pharynx, and also when this comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first emptied by laxative medicines; after that you make cautery at the root of the throat, and keep that you do not come even up to the throat, and do not burn more than a point. 
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the fire cautery to the joint of the neck at the head of the spine, and let the cauteries which is called "clavicle" for that we have the form before; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healed. 
de la toust	of the boil 
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and diseases of the body are from cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the disease is old, if you make two cautery on the forcele in their veins; and the other cautery removes the pit between II breasts; and be the cautery that is called «clavile» according to the shape which is before said. 
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cautery in pricking all the cautery that is called "points" because its form is before in the illness of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or wherever it reaches. 
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After curing the place according to what is said before, and let the cautery be at III reins according to this form: 
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cauteries are lighter, for you make three cuts with it. 
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder 
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then it befits you to reset the dislocation first. 
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After be made to lie the patient on his back and on his sides; after lift the heart which is within the tittle to the two of your left hand; and if the jointure is dislocated within, so sear the cautery that has II ners douqueil ci est li forme: 
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	And cauterize the liver as much as it pierces to the ribs, and come the figure of the cautery along with IIII cauteries; and for this cautery is made with the cautery that has III nerves, so that the figure of cauterization are sis cauteries; and are the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has III nerves. 
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes is adjusted upon this nerve for which there are VIII cauteries. 
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After put on the cautery points ground with silk; after let rest the patient, and be not moved his limbs for long time until it be well fortified.  
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated upwards, which thing happens rarely, then make cautery on the thickened part of the clavicle cautery, or many cauteries by pricking. 
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.  
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come coldness and much moisture until it becomes altered to its complexion, and many catarrhs multiply in him, and the usual methods of treatment do not help, then it is necessary that the patient be treated on his back, and extend his legs and hands. 
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From this then the III cauteries I below the shoulder bone by the quantity of a dime, to all the clavical cautery, and II cauteries fires the II ribs as long as the figure of the cauteries is at III angles, and have such space between one and the other that they are not joined together when they will rot; and be the cauteries so deep that they penetrate the II parts of the heart, and be the figure of the cauteries according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who will have fear of this cautery, cauterize pricking and reigning on the stomach at a point according to the quantity that you see of it; then cauterize all the cautery which is called «poins». 
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure of the cure we have had before, as long as it is healed.  
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes pain from cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is far from its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is cured of those that we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him, so it is necessary that the patient be treated on his bed; and sign of enche III cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, away from the hypochondria, where the ribs of the man come; and have spacing between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be long throughout the body, and do not press your hand too much on all the cautery; and let it burn only half of the heart, and let the patient be straight on his feet; and if he cannot, let him lie down, and extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form: 
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if you desire it, cauterize these cauteries with the knife, if you are skillful and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all of the heart, for you would make the whole body dry; and that it does not come to boiling, because the hearts are very subtle there, and you know how to see. 
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels pain fiercely. 
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure does the work, it behooves that the patient be soothed upon his head; and then place a poultice on the spot where the abscess is, and then warm the cautery which is similar to the sun's ray, of which here is the form: 
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with the fire cautery until the hairs are burned, and come to the skin, until the root is all strong; after the cure according to the cure of wounds until it is healed; and it should not be used by this cautery by anyone except those who have studied long in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured many times.  
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore he can boldly work, and it seems to me always better to leave it. 
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the cautery of pleurisy 
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one must make to pleuresin cauteries of roots of aristologe, and in this manner: take a root of aristologe long, the largest that you will be able to find, and be dry, and be as thick and as long as your fingers; and the moisten in oil, and the press on the fire, and cauterize the cautery between the shoulder and the neck, and II make little cauteries one by one going down in the part which is below the beard; and II cauterizes between the fifth rib and the sixth, declining back a bit; and I cauterize above the hip, and I other on the stomach, and I between the shoulders, and II as II ribs of the hip from behind the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but make openly as if you were smelling. 
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said that any old man who uses cautery of fire resembling the razor, and heat it up and put it between the ribs, until it comes to that abscess; and leaps pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. 
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear where the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed. 
de la mice	of the mouse 
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of the mouse of that which we have said as divisions of cures, and it does not benefit, then there are III ways of cautery that all are good.
