Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in the ancient days "cure contused," and is that you do to the patient who has this malady the hairs that he has or on his forehead, then make III incisions or forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as II should all remove the forehead down until the end, and the other II as II ribs above the cheekbones, and keep yourself from the incision of the arteries which are as II ribs above the cheekbones; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the II jawbones, and let each wound the quantity of III does across joints; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much of cloth for wiping the blood, then put the spatula acute of II parts as this is the form: 
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is from the temple to the second incision; and scrape all the marrow that is between the two cuts at all the surface that is on the bone, then make another cut from the middle incision to the other second, and then extract forth this spatula.  
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If in the first incision you put the instrument called "cultellaire," and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is blunt, not sharp, and this is its form: 
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And put the rib cutting towards the flesh to the heart, and the rib bottom toward the bone, and the point until it comes to the middle joint. 
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head as the eyes until the incision is continuous to the one that opens from the heart, and then another part make in the middle split until the other end; and then extract the blood evenly, and press the place for the taken blood; then put in each slit a tent of old cotton, and put on cloths moistened in wine and oil and aesil, and keep that an abscess does not come; and on the third day untie the bandage, and there administer great planty of warm water, then the cure of basil ointment with rose oil, and other cures which one cures wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the closing of the eyes 
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When a certain catarrh comes on acutely, and you see the eyes watery and small, and weakening of sight, and the nostrils burned; and the hairs fall out, and when he touches his head there is sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; therefore know by these accidents that this matter and this catarrh come from many veins, and the cure which is in it, this is it. 
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to raise their forehead, then make a great cut in between the brow, and another one wide in the cheekbone. 
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begins from the fissure of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision be until the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move at the meal; and when the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, and then sew between the two lips of the fissure and put old cotton there, and linen bandages; then tie above with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and keep yourself from a hot abscess; when it is removed, it is necessary that you rub the bone until cartilage begins to grow there, then cure it with drying things, which cause cartilage. 
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take II parts of flower of wheat, and of colocoline IV parts, and make a plaster from it; and administer it on these wounds to prevent flesh growing throughout.  
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping of ears 
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that falls into the ears is one of four things: or grains, or beasts, or stones from the mine or similar things like iron; or seeds, such as beans, lentils, peas; or flowing things such as water and oil and similar things. 
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or any other kind of thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, put the ear to the sun. 
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if there distills any drop of violet oil or sesame oil, then administer extraction; and have him sneeze from the condiment, and stop his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and elevate the ear upwards. 
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often comes force with this treatment; and if it does not come forth, administer the extraction with subtle pincers, which is the form: 
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pliers, that is good; if those do not come out, then administer extraction to the needle with a small doubler; and if it does not come out with those, make a caine of iron and put the head of the caine or hole of the ear strong, and stop what is around the caine with soft wax so that the blood cannot enter with the caine; then the tract should be formed, because many times it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take a glint of that which birds take, and put in on any instrument that is sharp for doing that, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the glint on the stone or whatever it may be, and extract. 
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not follow all these things that we have said, then hasten to cut the ear so that an abscess comes out, and spasm; and the manner of the cutting is that you first make the patient bleed from the cephalic vein, and extract blood according to the measure of his virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear to the fat or place where it depends; and let the cut be as a moon, as long as you come to the bone, then follow the bone according to your power, and suck it diligently with your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain that is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot be issued, then administer the spatula thin according to this form. 
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision to that grain. 
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grain is moist because of the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract with fine pincers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be aligned. 
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the earache therefore that falls in the ear it is necessary that the patient uses a first external of condiment, and opens the ear with old cotton. 
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And lie lying on that same ear where the water is.  
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it has leaped forward because of this, it is good. 
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not so, take many stones according to the length of your thumb, light and easy, and heat them a little in the fire; and put it in the patient's ear where it hurts, and raise it up from his feet on the other side, and place one stone upon the stone that is in the ear; and do not cease doing this of stones until the water comes out entirely, and thus will it all be drained; and if you see it, take a piece of reed, and put one end in the ear, and the other end catch on fire until the tip of the reed is burned; then redo another piece of reeds until the water comes out entirely, as we have said in the stone. 
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small in size, such as a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, administer an extraction with tweezers; and this is the easiest thing to remove that is in the ear. 
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	When extracting worms in your ears, when you treat them like we said in the division and where we treated distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear in the sun: if you see any worms there, treat them with small pincers, and if you do not see them, take the chain of which this is the form. 
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it should be narrow below and wide above. 
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And put the most subtle head in the ear according to the quantity of the suffering of the patient, then suck them form to all the chain; make this often as long as all the worms come out. 
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not obey this instruction, suffocate them around the cotton ear as I have said in the stone; and if they do not come out further as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven in the incision of worms, and you will find how to treat with distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines in the ear with all this instrument, for this is the form as you see. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And be it of silver or of iron, the small opening is below and above for distillation; and to press inside the distillation with the instrument of iron well made for this purpose, and if you see take the razor and wrap around the point conveniently cotton; then put your oil or your juice, and that which you see of your medicines in the ear canal, and the canal be in the ear; then put inside the razor all the cotton, and press your hand moderately until the oil is distilled or finished at the ear; and feel the sensation of the patient within, and let the distillations be a little warmed by the fire so as it distills in the ear; and guard that it not be too cold for the medicine would not be so good. 
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of the ears 
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a hole in their ears; and this same thing happens to men by blockage of a wound, or of flesh born inside the ear, and these blockages come sometimes from within the ear, if one cannot see them; and sometimes it comes from outside the ear, and one sees it well.  
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That one which comes in by fashioning, if it cannot be seen, is of grievous healing in many dispositions, and in this one it is seen that you should put the ear of the patient to the sun; and look inside: If you see the apparent opilation, so the work has all this spatulum of this form: 
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it sharp and trenchant before and behind all plain, so that it does not whiten the ear; if the opilation is of flesh or of the body of the ear, then hold it with subtle pincers, and cut it lightly, until that flesh be entirely removed.  
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the operation is done in the ear, then take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly at the fire, then put it on the body of the ear.  
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the swelling that the patient feels in the ear, pierce lightly, and be careful not to injure the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment. 
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this none day until the wound is healed, or you take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder with powdered vitriol; and if you see the ear inflamed, then it is necessary that you pull out the tent and move another tent soaked in cerote which should be made of rose oil and wax, until the inflammation is gone; then cure it until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, then dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop bleeding which are or treated with distillations. 
de la char des papieres	of the skin of paper  
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This ointment that comes on paper for the eyes when they are moist and dry, so you must stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off a spatula of its roots; then put on top of it powdered vitriol. 
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without it being decorticated, so the one cauterizes with the lentil-shaped cautery subtle, and the cauterizer after the incision worth moves; and many times they repair, since no thing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, so are those roots burned and do not return any. 
de la gresle	of the ankle 
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come in papers of the eyes things that seem brittle in their shape and in their hardness, and for this reason this illness is called "grainy," and it is a gathering of moisture thick in the paper above and below; the work is such: take warning if the grainy moves from one part and another, and it's a light thing to know; then make the wide, then the scrape of each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and the cut. 
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cover it without feeling a little the paper, do not grieve the patient; and if the opening is large, assemble it with a suture, and care for it until it is healed; and if it is small, do not make any force, because the flesh restores it soon and prevents scarring. 
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the grain is descending into the ear towards the upper part, then turn the paper over, and hold the grain with pincers, and cover and press it on both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the incision, it grieves nothing; and when the grain is cut, let the eye of salt water flow, and cure the place from that which causes flesh until the patient is healed.  
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes 
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is ingrained in the fabrics of the papers above, and this happens more to children than to other people, and it grieves their eyes greatly, and they come with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears hasten to their eyes; and because of this they lie down on their faces upwards, and sleep on them, and are their fabrics below their eyebrows moistened that the swelling and appearance have covered with exinach which opens in the eye.  
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your two hands and feel the snapping between them. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient puts his head in your hand; and then takes linen cloth, and prepares a tent in the manner of a circle according to the quantity that contains each side, then places it upon him; and presses with your feet on one side and the other, so that the sides are assembled within the circle; then makes in the middle of the moistor with a sharp blade trenching a fissure as wide, and no more than the wound made in the vein opening; and make the skin apart until you come to the exirnach; and in more preparations comes exirnach from the fissure, according to the shape of a piece of white fat. 
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract then with one piece of cloth stretched between your two fingers at the outside, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and guard that you do not bring in the fissure, that you come to all the spatula up to the eye, that you do not blind it. 
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the opening does not open at the beginning of the fissure, so carefully widen the fissure slightly until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then moisten bandages in hot and cold water, and put them on top, and bind with bandages. 
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind herbs and put them on to corrupt the moisture which is lingering.  
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure until it is healed.  
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the place hot, then its treatment with plasters soothing until it is healed. 
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of the papers 
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When in papers hairs are born adjusted other than the natural, and are weakened, they harm the eyes, and bring many kinds of diseases as tears accustomed and softenings of the papers and albuginea, until it is cause of the destruction of the eyes; and is the cure according to IV manners: either by cautery together fire, or by medicine acute according to that which is before or chapter of cautery, and is done or by incision and stitching or by chains, according to what I shall say. 
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the head of the patient in your well, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, put a needle at all the thread above; and be it below the edge of the paper where the hair grows near these hairs, and draw the thread upwards to all the paper, and turn it to the razor; then make in the part below the paper, below the hairs adjusted, to all the spatula cutting, from the large tear to the small one; then extract the thread, and put below the paper a small tent of cotton and drapelet, then place on the paper a figure of an enclosure, like the leaf of myrtle, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity that you see elevate the paper which is divided to all.  
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if to one who has need one cuts a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is soft; then making at all the spatula upon the II lines that you have signed, and commencing from large tear up to small; and let one of the clefts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the incisions in one of the II angles where the heart is, then peel it entirely; then assemble the II lips at a suture of a needle with all I thread of fine wool, and wipe the blood, and make air the superfluity of the threads upon the II eyebrows to any sticky things, if you wish to do this; and if not, take no care, then leave the suture and the threads up to III days or IIII; then cure the wound without a suture with dry and constricting things, for the paper revives at the bonding of the wound and the assembly of it, but the suture is mutated (as the ancients say), and this work without fear; and if in another manner: and that you sign the paper of a figure which is as the leaf of myrtle, as we have contained, to III incisions separated according to the form that is here: 
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then treat those who are sore with little force equally according to the form which is here: 
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have power to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, take a needle where it has I thread, and put it in the figure; and put the other thread alongside the large tear, and the second thread alongside the small one, and assemble between your two threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have signed, as we have counted, then assemble the II lips of the wound by stitching, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment; and sometimes it happens that the hair of the paper are converted: so it is necessary that you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitch in one and the other is more artificial. 
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the splints is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the felt inside according to what I have said, and then make II splints by art, and II subtle ties as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and cut the II ends of II parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of that which is above the paper of the eye, and strain the II splints of the II parts formed; and leave it so for some days, and the skin which is strained will die and become necrotic and form, until it falls off by itself. 
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has some forces, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn together, and if the paper is lifted, and they will no longer prick the hairs; and this is the form of the two canines that you shall make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide. 
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you prick a fine needle and put in the thread of silk soft and fine; then assemble the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then order in the chase the other fine thread of silk briefly, and tie the chief of the thread; then put the patient's head on your healthy; and be near the sun so that the work is clarified, for this is a subtle and small work; then put the needle to all the chase in the root of the hair joined, and make it pierce the paper carefully until you draw it up above the natural hair; then extract the hair until above the chase, and put in the chase that hair, if there are one or two or three or more; then extract your hand until the hairs come out all the chase in the paper with the natural hair. 
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, you will draw the hunt to the outside along the whole length that you have ordered it, until the hunt comes forth through the hole above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you will draw the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair hardens in its place and the flesh grows; and if the hairs are small, accompany the long hair of the natural horses, and raise it with that one or you leave it, as long as it is lengthened and then lift it. 
de la porriture de l’oil	of the rot of the eye 
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this sickness which is called "aleacrati" or the rot comes in the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.  
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens by a sudden blow from a wound or incision or cautery, and by similar things. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut that suture, and separate the lips of it, and put inside tents of linen, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not fitting that you use in the cure of it things that dry and restrain. 
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but there are works of softening things, such as fennel; and the rose of water or wine, and linseed seeds cooked, and oil of aqua dillon melted in any of the oils, and surround a tent, and treat with this. 
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure is that you take care that it does not fuse according to the form that it was before; and this work that we have said is nothing but addresses of this disease, that it does not return according to the form that it was before. 
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the shard which comes in the eye 
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This illness which is dislocation is truly called "axacrati", and is both natural and accidental. 
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the way of the work in them is that you prick a needle, in which it has a double thread, and place it in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear to the right, so that the thread comes into the two shoulders of the flesh; then is the flesh above all the needle, and the cup at the spatula wide. 
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns according to what is right, it is good; if not, then take a razor and put it in the fissure, and turn the paper, and make II fissures where it costs inside the paper; and let the heads of the II fissures be at the II angles of the incision that you have cut, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, that the figure is as the figure of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then take away that flesh, according to the quantity that its costs are aged below, of what follows the paper, then adjust the II parts separated, and their seams with a thread of wool; then cure with what we have said of softening medicines, and bandages, until it is healed. 
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the malady comes from a split or suture or cautery, it is necessary that you make a plain incision under the hairs of the papery skin, and according to what is said before; then sew between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the malady, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare anything of all their power how it makes return the figure to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs of work and instruments in more dispositions. 
dou soudement de la papiere	of the pressing of the paper  
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this soldering happens to the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is soldered with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural works, then it behooves you to put the point of a razor under the paper, and lift it up; and the extent as pinches, as long as you cut what is attached to the spatula subtle, which is neither too thick nor too sharp, so that the patient may not suffer that the spatula is too thick nor bleaches the eye; and let your incision be, with which you scrape the assembled one, lightly, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and it is healed all that assembly, and do no times in the eye saline water, and the lift of fresh water, and of collyrium; then put between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye wool moistened in an abundance of egg yolk; and after the third day use the collyrium and things boiling so long as it is healed. 
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the angle of the eye 
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the eye is in two manners: one is nervous and similar to hard wood; and another which is not nervous but is similar to white, frozen moisture, that when one touches it with iron and cures it with pincers, it cannot be done; and both appearances begin towards the great tear, and cross little by little until it covers all the view and all the light and movement of the eye. 
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient puts his head in your hand, then opens the eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then coil the angle with pincers of small thickness, and the raise it up; then take a needle, and put into it hair of horse, or of goat, or of ox, and the thread strong; and double the point of the needle one prick and put it into the angle, and pierce it all the way through with the needle, and tie the angle with a thread and raise it up, and rasp all the hair along the side of the angle which follows the root and the silk to the head, then cut the remaining in the root of the tear all over the little spatula and with small forces, and leave the natural flesh or tear, so that by the incision does not come the body of the tears customarily; and sometimes raise the angle only on the thread, as we have said; then rasp on all the little spatula beneath which is the form:  
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And guard that the spatula does not touch the fleshy cloth and break it, and that the needle be not pierced; and after the incision put in the eye a bit of silk ground, and from the collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it as much as it is needed until it is healed. 
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not feverish, and you cannot insert the needle, and the awl cannot enter, many times this appearance of a nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it covered, so work the eye of the patient, and take the spatula light point sharp according to this form: 
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And place the eye gently back into its socket, and if you see that it does not lessen and the reasoning speeds up, then distill from your mouth into the eye collar made of litargire and of red collar and a bit crushed, and stop the eye until the other day; then begin again the other work according to this same work, as long as it is completely removed.  
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the eye, such as a boil, then treat the boil first and cure it well until it is healed, then begin the work again as before, until it is healed. 
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of flesh from the tear harms the eye by great nuisance, then suspend it to the one and a half part, that body of tears does not come; then distill in the oil red collyrium which is made of litharge. 
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh which rises upon the pupil 
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The eyes of some men are born red sometimes and cover the eyelid and restrain over the papers and turn them to the fire, and seem like a rose of balustrade; and the work is that the patient puts his head in the healthy one, then the one works the eyes, and coil all that flesh with suitable needles for those eyes, and the sustain with force; then cut the first flesh, and go on cutting until the end, and guard yourself that you do not blind the eye during the operation; and let the incision be with a spatula like we have said in the incision of the angle and small forces of which one removes the sebum, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all flesh is removed, then employ the oil of silk or you distill red coral and similar medicines corrosive, and put on the eye fire cotton with egg white, so that it may be assured of a hot abscess; and if there remains nothing, and the blood clot rises, and you doubt a hot abscess, so leave the eye and cure the abscess with things calming a hot abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do as many times as flesh is adjusted in the eye by this manner. 
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nonetheless it behooves you to apply the cure of each weak point of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member suffers from that work. 
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes 
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Bloody veins are visible that are covered over the eye, and they take away from its work and weaken the eye all days. 
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary for the first that you look at if the eye, where it is, and whether it is not, and there is no other disease except the white of the eye; therefore the coil in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head on your healthy one, then suspend those veins to all the body according to his wisdom, and let the veins be fine and double according to this form. 
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And they shall be two ounces by degrees in the body according to this form:  
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then one should carefully apply those veins and wipe the blood hour after hour until you see remove those veins from the eye; and keep that you do not prick the eye with the points of spatulas, and make this work at midday before the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you will have done this, then distill into the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt what is left of the pus. 
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have power to collect all this in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye of things calming the pain of the eyes, and let it for some days until the pain is calmed and is assured of a hot abscess, then begin again according to this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of forces. 
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye 
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula is called "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is something in it that you should cut into the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is uncovered.  
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and blackness, then the king has all the instrument of this which is the form; and it is called «aspre chief», and be made of fire iron at the head rent, and be pointed like a file as it is in the present form: 
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put on the place of the bone corrupted, then turn it between your two, and press your hand a little while until you know that that corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the place with medicinal drying agents.  
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is fused, and flesh grows there, and the bow's body is fused, and it remains so for forty days, and it does not renew and is not an abscess, know that it is healthy; if not, there is no other way but to return the fistula to its opening according to this form: and that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, take the iron according to this form, and let the shoulder of iron be at three angles, and the shaft be thinned out until the head as you see here: 
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little, then turn the entire forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through what comes in this if he keeps his hand on his cheek; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens, the matter will go to the cheek; it is lighter for the patient. 
de l’issue de l’oil	Of the issue of the eye 
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is open entirely and does not come to disturb the nave nor diminish, then it behooves you to bind the patient; then the salve, then put on suction cups or a leech without wounding so as to draw forth; then put upon the eye the liniment made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolla, and then strain the eye, and the pad above with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths soft enough, and double each one into four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then strain it from above with a hard bandage, and repeat the suction cups to draw forth without wounding; then remove the suction cups and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the liniment softens, then it behooves you to strain it much; then remove the liniment after the day and night, and if you see the eye repairing, that is good; if not; then repeat the liniment and the bandages and the liniment and the suction cups until it be healed.  
dou derrompement de toile uvee	of the derangement of web woven 
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a disruption comes in the web covered, then open, and comes out of the papers like I grain of resin, and is easy to see; therefore if you see it covered, the work is such that you put a needle in the root of the lower part until the upper one, then put another needle where it has the double thread of the tear; and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the disposition; then cut the place of the double thread and tie one part of the grape around, and restrain it well, then extract the needle and put on the other oil half in the shape of an egg; and let it be until the threads fall with the grape, then cure the eye with comforting things as long as the wound is healed; and at times the wound is restrained by the grape on each side by a circle of cloth, as long as it is healed. 
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes have a great appearance, pierce them with a fine spatula which comes from the eye, and correct the albuminous moisture and lower the eyes, and put them in right away; then extract them as long as they are sound. 
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bowl of the eye 
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This sickness which is called «alcunnati» is nothing other than a bow which is assembled in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of the work is that you make the patient sit on the properly equipped and straight seat, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move it as much as you see the bow come up to your eyes; then be sure, and do not descend and let the light be dispersed, and have the patient see things as he usually does; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not properly arranged as we have said.  
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sharp spatula and make on the cornea tissue a point along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, as long as the bubble is there; and when it is out, distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek boiled and honey, then be cured with another cure until it is healed. 
des aigues de l’oil	of the eyes 
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of fish in dissection, and what is necessary to discern; so in work according to health. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from the light of the sun, and tie his healthy eye and hold it very tight; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left, or in your right hand if the eyes are right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called “almagda”, or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then put the point of the instrument beside the crown by the width of a fingernail in that whiteness of the eye to the part of the less tear, then thrust the instrument which is called “almagda” virtuously, and return your hand until it pierces into the whiteness of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the perfect measure of the space which is from the pimple to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; so you will see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cornea, and then put the instrument up to where the liquid is, then squeeze it below one way after another.  
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the water descends now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye. 
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After repose I little, and if the water returns up the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is ens fichie and she does not go up, extract gently by turning your hand poc and poc; and then put back in water a poc of seil gemme, and leave of this the oil inside. 
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by way of defense the eye plugged with a cloth or felt moistened in rose oil and honey, and tie it with the healthy eye.  
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top a common broth with abundance of egg. 
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter into the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, so it is necessary that you prick the instrument which is called "alberit", for this is its form: 
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce therefore the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep in it, but make it subtle, then put almagda, as we have said; and at the completion of the work, equip the patient with the sleeping place beforehand, so that he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be careful from all movements, and eat light meats, and do not move your head neither to the right nor to the left, and be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in the same dark room, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then put him back in a tie until the seventh day; and it is not appropriate that you do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you do this, because the water rises quickly.  
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess comes, that you untie the eye before the seventh day, and the address of those who soothe abscesses; and when it is appeased, then untie the view and put upon its face a border to cover for any day, and be in that dark house. 
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then he goes out of the house, to and fro, and turns in his case; and know that none of disciples should interfere in this case.  
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who told us that in his country they made a kind of almond paste, with which they sweetened water, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I ever read about it in books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing. 
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of the almond, for those who do not know them they see them; and be from a proper grain.  
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of each of this same subtlety, and the last in three angles acute. 
de la char sor le neis	of the bone upon the knee 
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes birth or are joined differently, so some seem like scorpions with many feet; and if there is such a one, and the flesh has a bad color, and if the flesh has a good color.  
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these carts which is puffed, and not cracked, it behooves you to make the patient sit between your hands opposite the sun; and open his nostrils, and throw the ointment on those carts, and the trai outwards; then cut what you can hold with the sharp subtil spatumile of one part, until you know that that cart is entirely removed. 
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if any thing remains that cannot be covered, one opens it completely with all the instruments subtle and lightly, so that nothing remains; and if there is no swelling or abscess, you secure it as is fitting; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hasten and cauterize it until the blood is staunched and are removed all the humors, then pour on it either boiling water or wine. 
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose works, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not pierce as it should, know that there is new flesh in the bone above, so that the instruments do not come to cut; therefore it is necessary that you put in a linen thread a little thick, and be knotted with hands ours, and have between each knot a space of less; and put the patient's elbow on the thread in his nose at its end, and pull by pulling until it comes out through the nose inside the mouth; and many times do children do this in schools, and it is an easy thing to him who wants to do it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and feel each one after the other, being attentive to those that are or thread. 
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make this as long as you know that the new ones have corrupted that flesh, then treat the child, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back straight to the wound as before; do this III days or more, until the ointment corrodes all that remains of flesh; and then put on the wound a bandage of felt for several days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which one distills the oils and medicines into the wound:  
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be it of silver or of iron, resembling a lamp open, as a funnel, and lead it thus; and if you see fit, make a closed funnel, and let the instruments be full to cleanse the head; and have the handle at the head for holding it when one heats the oil or any other liquid. 
de la char sor le neis	of the bone on the birth 
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.
