Many times is born at the head of new a sickness that is called «telul», and grows and becomes great enough, to the point where it is a visible thing to look at; and for this reason it behooves you to cut it at the beginning, and remove all the bone, then put upon its place the cautery or the burning medicine; and if one delays to cut it until it is large, one must take care if it is hard, of a dark color, of poor feeling: so do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanced abscess, for when one cuts it any time, there comes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touching, not of dark color, and you see that one can cut all of it, then empty the patient and cut it without fear, and cure the place with dry and restraining things. 
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn 
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuation comes in one of these works cartilages, it profits little, because in some men. 
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary when this happens to anyone, that you see if the wound is fresh in all its blood; and then adjust the two lips to a suture, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of their core as long as they bleed, then assemble the two lips to a suture, and hold them together, and put powder on powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and place above the powders a piece of strong ointment or another healing ointment, and leave it until it dries by itself, then treat it with ointment until it is healed. 
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or by thread, as I have let you know. 
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of the lips 
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	To men's mouths happen inside the lips abscesses hard, seeming like grains of peas, and smaller and larger; therefore it befits that you turn the lips, and fends on each one, and take with pliers and cut in each part; then apply in place after incision vitriol ground, until the blood is stopped; and then the ointment of oil, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed. 
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums 
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times pus arises on the gums attached flesh which the ancients call «albulus»; so it behooves you to hold it with forceps, and cut it at its root, and let the wound dry out or blood; then put on the place vitriol ground, or other powders astringent and desiccant; and if that flesh returns after the incision, and many times happens, so cut it a second time, and cauterize it: so it does not return after the cautery; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.  
des sordens	of deafness 
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scales that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and green, as long as the corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; so it is necessary that you make sit the patient between your hands, and his cheeks be in your saint, and pull out the teeth or the scales until nothing remains; and thus do of the blackness and greenness, and jaundice and other spots, as long as they are world; and if one removes those that are at the first reason, it is good; if these not, so begin again the second day and the third, until you have all pulled out; and know that the teeth have need of various forms of instruments to pull, according to what the work demonstrates, because the razor which one pulls out outside the teeth have other forms than those which one pulls between the teeth; and these forms and others be with you equipped. 
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you take time to drain as much as you can, because it should not be done; because it is a very high substance until we have no excuse to remove. 
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore when the patient is constrained to endure pain, it is necessary that you are certain about the tooth aching.  
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain annoys the patient, and thinks that it is in a holy tooth, and makes milk the good tooth; and however the pain does not depart for him, as long as the evil remains, because we have already wanted to do this to his saints; and when you are well certain of the tooth hurting, then it befits you that you scrape around the tooth to all i. spatula strong in order to guard the gums from all sides; then you move it with your two or with pincers subtle at the first prick and prick, until it is well loosened, then you firmly affirm the pliers; and let the head of the patient in your saint between your knees, and hold him well so that he does not move.  
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After you have pulled the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take one of these instruments and push it gently inside from each side, and move it as you did at first. 
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and damaged, then it is necessary to fill it with bandages where the holes are; and gently hold it with tweezers so that it does not break when being held; and it is necessary to work very carefully around the gums to dislodge the tooth.  
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And therefore take good care that you do not break it, and remain a part of it, and return to the patient through the wickedness of the root greater pains than the first. 
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And guard yourself that you do not act as the ignorant healers who by their haste and their boldness sometimes break the bone, and they bring it no help which we have recounted; but often they bring with questioning of those great illnesses for the roots which remain there, or for the bone that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is drawn, wash its place with wine or oil and salt; and if bleeding comes, which often happens, then apply the place with powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it. 
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, as to which one moves the teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms: 
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be thick members so that they do not bend when pulled, and let them be of well-made iron, and let them be toothed to hold the parts. 
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth 
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the breast, it is fitting that you put on it cotton moistened in butter for one or two days. 
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the eyes are closed shut, then put the pliers called “algebri” inside, so that the head looks like a beak of a bird; and be made inside as well as a file, and this is the shape 
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to issue with all these pincers, then it is necessary that you uncover the flesh around the root, and put there the instrument which is called "althali", that is to say, a spatula, because of this is its form. 
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root falls out with this, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all tools, of which the forms come after here: 
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument which has II reins, of this is the form: 
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments which are in front in the order of teeth, and of this instrument which resembles great pliers, whose form is here: 
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this instrument so that it may not break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not mentioned; and the wise masters subtle find by himself his instrument, according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are such maladies where the ancients do not teach any instrument for the diversity of others; and if one does not break the bone or other bones, where it may be permitted, then seek the instruments that are necessary, which I have told you, and help yourself with gestures, of this is the form: 
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then return it to its place with medicines suitable for this, and if it has in the bone rot, and it is small, then the queen has all this instrument:  
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural body, and the form is ugly, and even in maidens, it behooves you to know if the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and one cannot file or trim it; therefore, the ridge; and if it is next to the tooth, take this instrument whose form is here, and it is similar to a small beak, and it is made of sharp iron on its tip: 
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cope a little and little with hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a tool like this is its form. 
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file of which one makes needles; and in filing its tooth point by point gently for several days, so that it does not move until it falls; then the plane at the end has no trace at all, and if the teeth are too sharp and it bites the tongue, then it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not bite the tongue nor corrupt speech. 
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth loosens 
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front is loosened, either by percussion or by falling, and the patient cannot press on it so that it moves without it falling out, and you have treated it with restrictive medicines, and this does not work; if it needs to be restrained with a thread of gold, because the silver threads become green and rotten, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of the space between the teeth; and if you see the need to align the teeth, take the thread and bring it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the head between the teeth, if there is one or more, until you arrive skillfully to the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again the coverture up to the part where you began, and strain your hand subtly and skillfully, so that it does not move at all; and let your thread be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.  
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the broken jaw with pliers, and join them, and put them between the healthy tooth, and place it so that it does not touch the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it loosens or the wires break, bind it with another wire; let it remain and serve thus throughout its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two broken ones, as you see: 
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls, one puts it back in its place, piece by piece, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and suffering, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from bone of calf, and one puts it in the place where there is a lack, and one holds it as we have said, and it stays and serves so long a time. 
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the vein of the tongue 
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At no time is this ligament which comes from under the tongue or nature that one is born thus; or by accident of a suture wound; and the work is such that you operate on the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your hand, and raise the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament of the wide part, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from a suture wound, so put the needle and cut with the wide one that ligament; and guard that the cut be not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done, lift the area of rose water and of oil, or of cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen; and bandage the patient each night, that the wounds may not join. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding comes, put on the place vitriol ground; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize it with the fine cautery, which is good for this; then cure it with another cure until it be healed. 
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it of fire color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining to whiteness, and there is moisture, then put on an ointment, and make it with a subtle spatula, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if the sans te goes well in your work, then put on powdered vitriol until it is stained, then return to your work as long as you extract everything; then raise the place of the aisil and seil, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.  
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses of the throat 
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come into the throat sores that are called "godath," and they are properly called the II almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is abscesses hard of small sense and of fusse color, then do not touch them with iron.  
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also to avoid blood loss; but leave it until it is mature, and then you will cut it off, where it would break on its own; and if it is of white color, and the root is fine, have your instrument prepared to cover it, but first look whether the abscess warms and is calmed. 
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his chin be on your hand, and open the mouth and place the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, because this is the form; and let it be of silver or fine iron as well as a knife: 
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Since you presses the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the probe and put it in the midst, and drive it upwards as much as you can; and do not move anything with the cloths, then grasp the instrument by its form, which seems like forces; and nonetheless the head are bent, and one place the other, and they are very sharp, and is made of iron or bronze:  
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use tongs for this is its form: 
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be trenchant on one side, and on the other side no; and when you have cut one of the almonds, cut the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and lukewarm, and if there is a flow of blood, gargle the patient with water, or cooked pomegranate rinds, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the wound is cleansed; then cure it until it is healed; and any time other abscesses arise in the throat than the II almonds, then cut them as you did the II almonds.  
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicined a woman of an abscess that was near inside the throat, that is to say the abscess of small size; and I had well nearly closed all the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the conduit which was stopped up, and could not eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained thus one day or two.  
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high raised that it had to have been put II reigns by the II openings of the two. 
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore did then, and put one in the one opening, then I drove the thread outwards, and in a great portion of bowel; then I refixed the other half in the other opening of the two, and worked the mouth and pressed the tongue; after which I put the needle in these abscesses, and in one part, and there came out only a little blood; and thus was the woman’s throat unstopped, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not cease to cut this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew back again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; therefore I grasped it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I departed from these parts, and only know that God did what he wanted to with her after me. 
de l’uve	of the grape 
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the grape comes to maturity and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is small and round, it is called "grape". 
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the chapped abscesses are calmed, and it is subtle, then it behooves you to cut it; and the one which is rounded assembled and is not long; and it is sanguine or of fusse color or black, then it behooves you to eschew the incision of it. 
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril for the patient. 
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is therefore necessary, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, that you make the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue to the instrument which we have mentioned before; then insert the needle into the eye, and move it below, and the cup to the II instruments that I have said in the incision of the II almonds. 
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut more than the superfluity which is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the II almonds, and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid to have it cut, then you must use something to lessen the fear of cutting. 
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp acute. 
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or chapter of cautery, and confides with quick lime shoes, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and using the point of this instrument, from which comes this form:  
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have or chief a tuft of wool where one puts the medicine, like the hair of a spoon, and put the instrument on all the medicine above the eye; and let the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and the muscles pull from his mouth the medicine within, so that it does not descend to the throat, and the windpipe; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press on the eye, the quantity of half an hour, until you see it burn and the bites of the medicine be appeased; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument to all the cotton in the canal above, until the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and lie afterwards IIII days or V And if you have need to recommence the cautery of the medicine, begin it again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye, with cotton smeared in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and be cured with gargles until it is healed. 
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, nor the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calament and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble them all or any of them in a pot, and put it inside, and boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have the instrument. 
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be it silver or iron, and let one of the heads be put in the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor rises to the uvula through the vein, until the uvula is mortified; afterward, it restarts often, until the uvula dries, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, because many things happen; and do not make this except at the declination of the hot abscess. 
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put inside its head a staff of beef, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the staff of beef does not allow the vapor to weigh down the mouth, and it is good cure altogether salvation. 
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fishbone or spine or any thing lodges in the throat, therefore it behooves you to draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all your instrument so that you see move the thing; and what does not appear to you and is put back into the throat, it behoove you to make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if this will draw out the thing through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or I morceil of dry bread; and tie to the sponge the thread, and then swallow it again; and when it comes to the place, it will lodge, and then you will draw out further; and if she does not come out further of what we have said, then take the instrument of bronze according to this form: 
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it may more easily enter into the throat, and have the head raised high; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest it come to him or close his windpipe; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument forward because he knows whether the thing is easy; if he pushes down, or draws it out fully with the entire instrument equally.  
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the throat cutting 
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	At no time is medicine given to the bloodless, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when those do not help, then look at the throat of the sick person in the sun, then that you press the tongue with the instrument that I have told you. 
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the wound, treat it with all small instruments, or subtle tweezers that are fit for this purpose. 
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a horsehair and put it in the throat of the patient, then put the end of the horsehair into the fire hot, and do this often. 
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And the patient remains with a fever every day.  
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full the glass of cold water, and work the mouth, and the put it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the patient feels the water, he falls. 
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the grape; do this many times, because it will fall without pain. 
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you light a pot where there are embers, and let the base be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in that one put the head of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up to the snout; and the snout will now fall, and if it does not fall, then begin the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and chew salty things and others, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for it to be purged by this government. 
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the hemorrhage, is, when it can be seen, similar to curved pliers in order to enter into the throat; and has a resemblance to the beak of a bird, and it has asperities of lime, so that those whom it takes, it cannot let go; and see here the shape: 
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses 
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are, according to what memory comes here after from one and the other in this book, and are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in II manners, whereof one is in its own semblance, and of that which it holds moisture.  
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the eyes where they are on the body. 
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are other than those of the base, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are other than those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work. 
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if to abscesses one must not prick, as long as the boil is ripe according to its completion; and if to such ones that it is necessary to prick when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses which are near joints. 
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and it is left as long as it is rotten and swollen, by chance the tendons and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb. 
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Ou the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is mature, it will harm the principal limb; where it is near the foundation, pierce it so that it is mature; and it is not proper that you pierce an abscess without complete digestion, except for the one which is near the foundation, so that it may not burst forth, and be lengthened within, and there comes a fistula; and it cannot heal in a great time.  
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess which is ripe according to accomplishment, and this is when the pain is appeased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and of the swelling and the softening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where more dependent place of the abscess, and where it appears to open; and be the perforation long in the body, and if the abscesses are at the hands or at the feet, or in joints and in nerves and in arteries, and in all their equals where there is no plying. 
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these that are dislocated, according to which limb. 
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is worth while that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. 
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce him in front of those, his body will be lengthened by the venom from within, and it will be full of much dirt; and perhaps the lips and the depths of him will harden. 
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is perceived according to the width of the body, according to what the members have need. 
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the semblance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, and cover; when it is become as a flap, and is softened, it is necessary to do as one does with boils: and if there are such that are cut into three angles, and if there are such that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the anger; and if there are such where one makes a round size, and other sizes and semblance cuts.  
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial abscess, you must pierce it fully; and when the abscess is large, and it has accumulated much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus in that hour, but drain part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then drain nothing directly; do this many times from great to great, until the pus is gone; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an old man decrepit. 
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes trembles with the issue of the bowels, that perchance the patient dies, and you do not lose yourself. 
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the abscess wound is small. And if it is a flat cut, administer pads of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, it is necessary that you put one pad in each so that they come against each other; and if you have pierced part of the skin in the abscess and have covered it inward, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day. Then open it, and care for it with ointment until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, then administer cold water and ice, and moisten the cloth, and put it on the bleeding area many times.  
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the flow of blood persists, administer government and care, and the powders that I have said in this book, and if it is during winter, and the abscesses are very nervous, then it is necessary that you put on tents and drapes moistened in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the wound is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on moist bandages in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess, wipe it, and cure it, as necessary, until it is healed. 
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in the treatments of abscesses: as I have said how one must proceed before the treatments of abscesses, and see here the chapter. 
des soros	Of sores 
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When the heart of the head comes little abscesses, and are manners of ours that are in webs, just like the braiding of a tunic, and there are many resemblances. 
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and such that have moisture like the arms; and there are some that are hard and stony at the waist, and there is no doubt if the artery does not do the opposite. 
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of the waist are that you experience to all instrument which is called "entromissoire", from what the form comes after, what thing it contains. 
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then lift it up by the long end. 
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is dried, carefully scrape away without leaving the hair that contains that moisture, because it returns if you leave it alone; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; otherwise, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and pick out what is left of the pus.  
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain at all of the wound; then cure the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is healed. 
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in the fat, then cut according to this form, long; and place your linens there, and the skin from all parts, and put all your care into drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, then do what I have told you afterwards. 
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do for an abscess if it is foul, and how to cut and cure as I have told you. 
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the boil on the abscess festering and moist, it is lighter because they are of little blood. 
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in some of these abscesses or chief where it has no moisture, and of these abscesses that I treated or chief of an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot be broken; and if one had done any of them, one would have done to it just as well as a wound from a stone. 
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come or chief, for those who come near the head of children and at the roots of the ears, let the opening always be at the lowest point, in order to make it easier to drain pus; and treat them as appropriate. 
des scrophules	of scrofulous  
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses happen in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere on the body, and are bad, and are intertwined with each other. 
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofulous is properly within its side, as the boil and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulous are many. 
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some who contain moisture, and there are some who do not want to obey health. 
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in that which you see of good disposition at the touching and seeming to the color of the body, and mute from each part and is not much troubled by the nerves of the neck nor by the artery nor by the conduit, and is not too deep; so it befits that you cut it from above, and the skin from each part, and extend the two lips of the heart as incisions, if you have need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve nor the vein, and not be the spatula too wide nor trenching, that the hand escapes, and see not too far forward, that you do not cut what you should not.  
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put in the wound powdered vitriol, or some powders that restrain blood, and hold tight the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot. 
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is stitched up, return to your work, until you have finished it; then examine with your index finger if there remain any small pustules, and cut them out and cauterize them. 
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has in the root of the scrofula a great vein, it is not fitting that you cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by it, without hurting it; then apply the wound to old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cover it. 
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the whole scrophula, it is necessary that you assemble the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, since there is no remaining superfluity for the size of the scrophula. 
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	So it is necessary that you understand to cover the root of it, and milk forth, and the count as we have said. 
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophules that hold superfluity, pierce there where it opens better; and pierce thus as the one said before, in depending, then administer tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, the ointment cure enjaring flesh, until it is healed. 
de squinance	of squinting 
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients said and spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I never saw in our land who did it, and this is the writing of their word. 
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the slit of the throat which is called "epiglottis" be escaped; and one does not help with these, because all the veins and the pores of the patient are to those who have abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in II amandres.  
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the channel of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation. 
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary when we want to cut the epiglottis that we cut it below III circles or IV a small incision through the center between the II circles or by the quantity of the incision of the syfac, not in the cartilage; and these are so suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no char, and the vessels are long from within. 
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to all its extent, then split the keel as long as it comes to the cartilage; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see nothing, and then cut the syfac, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm of the cartilage that it flows out from the place which is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a piece. 
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour is passed because one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound to the heart, and stitch together solely along the cartilage; then administer medicines that make flesh grow, until it is healed. 
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says one does not do this until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault lies with the wing.  
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore cover the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and for this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in III days or in IIII. And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and care for it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.  
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took the knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels of the pharynx; and I was called by her to cure her, and I found her as dead. 
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had come from it, and I see well that it had not struck a vein nor led further than the throat, and the veins were coming out through the wound. 
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I bound it up, and thus I dressed the wound, and I treated it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the maiden except that she was hoarse of voice, and afterward returned to her disposition; for this reason I say that in cutting into the epiglottis there should be no fear. 
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat 
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess in the color of a boil, and is most common in women; and it is according to II manners: natural, and accidental; where natural has no instrument.  
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat in us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it does not behoove to work to make outwards except in this which is small, and proves and searches all the introduction: if you find it as I fatty, and cannot to any vein, so cut it, as one cuts the fat, and treat it with its whole top, if there is any; and enclose well soon, and cure it as it befits, until it is perfectly healthy. 
des nous	of us  
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to us, of which I will say all the appearances; and now it befits me to say all the difference that is between us and the outcome.  
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is sometimes accompanied by fever, as long as the boiling is not passed, and the putrefaction is accomplished; therefore rest the fever and the heat. 
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the new one there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains I syfac, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as well as a pimple, and becomes large; and they are according to two resemblances, or thick, or moist, and much of color are as I said in the division. 
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the cure of the new, that you try and inquire first to all the instrument which is called « entromissoire », according to what its form will come or chapter which is afterwards.  
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of incision of abscesses from us is that you prick or more moist place than you find in the abscess, and turn your two points and points, until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess; then remove the introducer, and take care in those that jump may be. 
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes running short, whatever its color, treat it as I have said about other abscesses; and if after the introduction of pus, there is no more moisture, know that it is fatty, so treat it in a cross, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape it on each side and guard the tunic where it lies so that you draw it out healthy with the needle; and if you cannot draw it out healthy, then drain it by pieces so that nothing remains. 
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	Car if it remains there nothing, it returns to us many times; and if it remains a little, and the wound does not grieve him, then apply to the wound some sharp corrosive powders, and tighten the wound, and put on top soothing things, an abscess hot, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if the wound is large, then stitch the two lips of the wound, and cure it from that which generates flesh. 
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beating is contrary to you or otherwise hurry and apply the place of vitriol ground, and let it lie II days or III, as long as the wound rotts, and rests the boiling of blood; then return to cover what remains of the new. 
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the introducing instruments, and they are in three manners: large and medium and small; and there are three squares that are called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and there are also in three manners: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula; and they are also like needles with which one sews the sorceresses, and they are of citrine iron, or iron, or silver, and most valuable are those that are yellow, and they are more proven of black pitch to surround the fistulas; and they are in three manners: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the openings. 
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the forceps are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are forceps that have II curves in III ways also; and there are forceps that have III curves, and they are also in III ways; and there are forceps that have II curves, and forceps of one curve only, and they are in III ways; and all these are necessary in their place. 
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these are cutting instruments, and there are some which do not cut more than one side, of which we remove the skin so that one does not cut a vein nor a nerve; and among these intruments are the alemeles put into handles so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in their fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and groins, and similar places; and sometimes one makes a smaller instrument resembling the strips of fistulas, according to this form, for which one lances blood. 
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it once in its place which is wholesome to cutting of veins, and arteries, and never again according to this great form: 
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain disfigured and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form from this line .b. up to .g. 
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat, and apply medicine to the wound preventing flesh, then assemble the two lips of the wound with stitching, and care for it until it is healed; and if it swells downward, and becomes softened like women have, make two grooves above, by two similar slits; so that one holds onto the other at the end of one and the other, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to the line .g.; then scrape the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and there administer what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the care, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or because of the bleeding, then it is necessary that you fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it softens the remaining flesh and fat, then care for it until it is healed. 
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits 
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the arms are kinds of hard scrofulas which have edges, and some contain moisture. 
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line .b. to the line .g..
