Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the matter that is in the abscess is emptied, put the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and care with ointment after this as long as it is healing. 
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of the appearance of scrofulas, then cut it as we have said for incisions into scrofulas, and if the wound is bowed inward, then administer cautery as we have said before. 
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery 
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is cut, and the skin is sewn that is on top, then often come abscesses, and just as it happens to the vein inflamed and abscess; and if the one who knows this is for the artery, then the abscess is long drawn out; and when you feel it at your fingers, you feel a tightening; and when it is for the vein, then it appears swollen red with fever; and it is folly to cover this abscess, and even though it is under the armpits and the groin and neck and in many other places, and it is very large. 
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the treatment of iron, and that which is in chief, it is necessary to avoid also, and in that which is inflamed by artery making from above the skin long; then operate the waist as incisions, and depart beautifully the artery from the fabrics, until it is discovered; then put below one needle, and let it pierce until the other side, and restrain the artery with a double thread in II leagues, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the II arteries that are in temples; then point the place which is between the II links of an intromissoire as long as the pus comes out from there, and be cleaned the abscess; then administer the cure that enjanre bowe, until the ligament hangs; then cure those with ointment coming to these, until it is healed; and if the abscess is for the size of the vein, then it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can of the abscess to all the skin, then put the needle below the place that you hold in your hand, and let it pierce, and there have I double thread, so that you draw it from the other side; then tie the abscess, as I have told you, or ligament of one of II parts as II chiés of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads are not issued, so put another needle to all I thread below all the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and restrain the threads in IIII leagues; then cut the abscess as long as the superfluities come out from there, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave what is tied; then put above I drapeil moilliet in wine and oil, then administer to them cures of tents and ointments until it is healed. 
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves 
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses come to the nerves when they are burned or by too much work, and similar things.  
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the shoulders and hips and in all the places where there are joints, and it is the grief abscesses, and its color resembles the color of the body, and is in more dispositions without pain; and when one confines it strongly, the patient feels pain, and is not at all within the body, but below the heart; and moves well in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor down nor up, and that which is in the joints should not be covered with iron: for fear it would contract; and that which is on the head or forehead, it raises the skin to the spatula.  
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a thread, and peel it, then extract it and stitch the wound together, and treat it until it is healed. 
des grosses boces pendans	of large bladders hanging 
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else; and is a disease that is called “fungus” because of its appearance; and are the roots subtle, and the head large; and there are some small and very large; and I saw the man who had II in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a fine root, and were just split open, and from them flowed moisture. 
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI З., and the work in the incision is that you see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of fine root; if the cope to the spatumile large, and be in your presence the cautery to the fire. 
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the hip often come too great bleedings, and if it does not stop, therefore hasten to cauterize it; and if you see the patient fearful and afraid of the incision of iron, then take a thread of strong wool well made, and tie the limb as we have said, and let him leave it for days; and then restrain it, and do not cease restraining the wool thread until it closes the limb, and heals by itself; and if the roots are thick, be afraid to cut them all at once because of the belly, but you may well cut half, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and guard that you do not cut the tissue which is of pale color and poor sense and of milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess encrusted, and I will come to the cure of ulcers after. 
quant li boude ist fuer	when the head is carried 
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the swelling comes from cautery of wound or tear of the flesh, and is on the belly and in some of the parts, as they have in other wounds, or of blood which flows from veins or arteries according to what is above, or of windiness; and if it is from the rupture of the flesh and the exit of pus, then the color of the abscess appears like the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and opens of various exits. 
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it to its sides it returns, and then returns again, and perhaps it is seized, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and for heavy work. 
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, not constraining it; and if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs the abscesses thick and hard, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, it is soft to the touch, and the work is that you look at whether its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or wind. 
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	So you must leave the cure. 
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in it, as I have said to you in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and for the vein. 
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bowel, then you must command the patient to hold his arm, and be stretched straight, then grasp around the belly; then command him to grasp his body between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked with all the spatula, then extend half of the abscess above to the whole great incision; then tie it around with a strong thread, or a very strong silk cord firmly, and let them be bound to each other's ends; then operate on half of the abscess extended over the linen, and put your index finger in, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the linen, then untie it, and put the intestine out of the belly; and if you find the bowel, then take it at the incision, and cut off the superfluity; and if the artery makes you go against, or the vein, then go well around, then return to your work and take II needles, and put II strong threads in them, and put the II needles around that which you have made in cross that you make perce; then strain the abscess in IV leagues on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it can rot, and let the dead flesh fall by itself; or you cut it when it is subtle and rotten, then cure it as much as necessary, and heal the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as necessary, and solder the place. 
dou chancre	of the ulcer 
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the resemblances of chancre, and how one must work it with medicines, and how one must shun the cure of iron; and let us say the chancre is engendered in the marshes, and great caution in its cure, and they said the ancients that when the chancre is in a place where one can shave it as much as a chancre that is on the nipples, and in the buttock, and in similar places, and one must remove it all when it is at the beginning; and when it is large and old, it does not behoove you to approach it, because I have never healed any of them; nor has anyone ever healed any before me. 
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the work, when it is in place where one can remove it, as we have said, is that you purge at any time the patient of black bile; then make him bleed if he has a manifest repletion, then put the patient in the good place to do the work; then wipe your incisions or chancre, and shave the head from all parts, and the bone from all parts without leaving anything; and let the blood flow entirely out, and firmly press the place with your hand or any thing, and if the bleeding from the incision of the artery or vein goes against you, cauterize it as long as the blood is extinguished; then cure him with another cure until he is healed. 
de ydropisie	of dropsy 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what way the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron; so it is only lit; and one must not touch iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarche, because it is a mortal thing; therefore when you medicine this semblance of dropsy which is called «eclytes» by medicines, and the cure does not benefit, see if the patient is weak, or if he has another disease besides dropsy, such as cough and solution of the belly and similar things; if you do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great strength, and he has no other disease than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you must act thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the ministers press the belly by pushing the water to the lowest part of the pelvis, then take the spathule espinous according to this form: 
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And shall be sharp of II parts. 
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	to the point, and nonetheless let it not be so inserted that it could come up to the intestine when you insert it, and do not let it bleed; then see if the dropsy is occurring towards the intestines: if so, you should cut into above the bulge III two inches below the armpit; and if the dropsy is due to the liver disease, then make your incision on the left side of the bulge III two; and if it is due to the spleen, then it should be on the right, and it is not proper that the patient lie down on the incision so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and put it in, and lift your hand over the whole spatula between the skin and the syfac as much as when you are lancing a quantity of an inch or more; then pierce the syfac until the spatula comes to the point eight, and this is the place of the water, then the water flows out, and put that instrument back in there because this is how it is formed: 
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a fine silver coin, and it is of iron or bronze light, and in the lower part there is I small hole; and on one side, III holes; and II on the other side, and I on the other; and the head is cut like a feather, and this is the form of the incision with which scribes cut the pen: 
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the head above is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the liquid, it draws now on the instrument; empty therefore half or a third part, for if you empty more than is due in this hour, by adventure the patient dies because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of his virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then treat the instrument and hold the liquid, and it is held now for the heart which stops the hole which is on the syfac, of this I have spoken, that you pierce according to this manner; then begin the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering from it, and treat of the liquid a small quantity; do this any day, and guard yourself from foiling as long as there remains but one drop of liquid. 
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and give him much water, so cure him with burial or hot sand, and with much sweat or bath and in the sun, and let him drink; and cure him with drying medicines until he is cured, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before. 
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the stoppage of the penis 
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At times children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its place. 
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary, then he must see to every little detail very carefully according to this form: 
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then put or through the clo subtle of plank, and bind it and keep it so III days or IIII and when he wants to urinate, let the clo be removed, and make urine, and then put it back; and by adventure, it is not necessary, because the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed. 
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose hole is small, if he is medicated with the clove of plantain, as we have said, it will widen. 
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the glans in its place are pale, because none are born with the glans at the head of the penis, which is why they cannot urinate until they lift their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot come as far as the urethra, and this is a serious illness. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is that the patient lies supine on his back, and place the head of the rod and the cup as well as the waist of a feather, so that the hole falls in the middle, as it is proper; and guard against bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, with the sponge of those who staunch blood, and cure the wound until it is healed. 
des pustules de la verge	of the blisters of the penis 
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this boil comes in the shaft, and it is a hideous appearance of flesh; and there are malicious ones and non-malicious ones; so it behooves you to pluck them at the root with a subtle needle, and the cut and clean all, then put on soft cotton with Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed. 
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the boil is malignant, of bad color and pus, then you must apply a cautery to it. 
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have captured it, and if the bandage is in the body on one end, and part inside the skin and part outside, then it behooves you to remove the bandage that is inside first; and when it is joined, then care for the one outside. 
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if the head of the staff is not assured that it is pierced, and black and corruption comes in its staff and at the root; so it is necessary to remove all that is black and corrupted, then put on it a plaster of honey and flour made from the bark of pomegranates and quince, then cure it with other cures until it is healed. 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, administer the lunar cautery according to this form: 
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery helps with two things: that is to say, bloodletting and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary for you to put or lead a chain of wood on the penis, and piss the patient among; and when the hair is raw at the head of the penis which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you scrape it with a sharp instrument until the bonds are loosened, and the head of the penis is delivered on all sides; and if this thing is difficult to discuss, it is necessary that you scrape it with a spatula a little bit from the head of the penis and the hair; then loosen carefully between the two, and put between them the fine linen cloth soaked in cold water so that it does not dry. 
de la circoncision	Of circumcision 
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a wound like the others; nevertheless, when we do this work of our will, and especially on children, it is necessary that we do the best work and the lightest to salvation. 
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not say the circumcision of their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we have no more than what we have acquired by experience. 
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and surgeons who made circumcision in Dal, and with forces, and a whole novacule; so they fled because there are two blades, and by chance if one cuts above and stays below. 
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it must be covered, and the pain is doubled, and in the purification which is of the bone, the point of the limb is not assured; and in the purification of the joint by chance the iron escapes, and the work runs, and many times they are born as if they don't need purification and I wanted it.  
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the modification that is made by force to all the linen thread I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces cut equally well above and below. 
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, so that it is equal in all parts of the soul; but let the hair be well straight around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be as you make the child think, if he understands, that you only tie the hair around the rod just, and then allow him to rejoice in every way that you can; then make it stay between your hands straight, and place the forces between your hands or below your feet so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the rod and breathe or heart, and bring it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the dirt which is assembled there, then tie the place sign with a double thread, then tie it below I poc to the other lien; and hold it as II does by the second lieeure at the pouch and to the index finger, and cut between the II liens, then lift the heart up gently and bring the head of the rod; then let the blood run drop by drop, for that is the muedres; and put powder on and above the powder I drapeil glued with a half of an egg cooked tempered with rose water, mixed with fine and fresh rose oil, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with another cure until it is healed. 
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for purification is this: the two shoulders are held and are pointed, and the shoulders are also as large as the arms equally.  
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the purification is when the kernel inside is at the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your finger, so that the pus makes an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, then hold it with pliers, and then cut it. 
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed III days, and that which is below the member is swollen, let it be left until the abscess has subsided, and lightly scrape it; then cut it as you can move it, and guard yourself from the part of the member, it will harm him nothing. 
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the place with things soft wound of powder, that we have said or treated of powders, and if one strikes too much at the heart, and it goes upwards, it will do no harm; cure therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.  
dou retenement de l’urine	holding back of urine 
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is from a stone in the bladder, or blood congealed, or bowel, or new flesh, or similar things that we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to the stone which is at the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees; and their feet should be placed on the back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient's legs as much as he can; and thus the neck of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the stone upward, so that the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then it is necessary for you to administer an extraction with every instrument that is called a "syringe," from which this is the form: and be of fine silver, light-headed, like the feather of a bird; and be the shaft a palm long and half, and be fine at the tip. 
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issuing of urine is that you take I double thread, and tie it to the head I wool ball or cotton, and put the head dou thread inside the syringe; and cut the superfluity of the wool and put it until the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and aubin of egg, and make the patient sit on I seat, and lift his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently put the syringe into the penis, until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis from above towards the bud; then put the syringe forward until the bladder, and the patient feels coming until the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order for those who lead or where it goes is twisted; then stretch the thread to all the wool ball and ball, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make correct the urine; and re-begin the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is aligned. 
des maladies de la vessie	of bladder ailments 
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When sores or blood come in the bladder, or rot is assembled there, and you see them distilling sharp waters and medicines, do as to all the instrument that is called “clepsedre,” and this is its form: 
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III perforations: II on one side, and I on the other, as you see; and the leus chevez because of which the medicine should be such that it stops well the verge without addition, if one can drain the moisture, and put out when necessary; and when you see putting your medicines in the bladder, put the chief dou keusteur in the moisture, and pull with the pulling string which is inside; if you will pull the moisture to the kesteur, and then firmly reinsert the pulling string inside; so will enter the moisture inside, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder: this is it.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And is of silver or of gold, and is the head higher; and below to the breast where the cords fall; then take a sheep bladder and put in it the moisture which you see clisterize the bladder, then tie it between the two breasts forming with a good double thread, and heat the point of the clyster on the fire; then put the head of the clyster into the rod, then strain your hand on the bladder to all the moisture happening, until the patient feels that that moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don’t have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it in a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then put the strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles the dal, and put inside what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder. 
de la piere	of the stone 
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in the division the manners of stone, and the extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between the stone formed as rains, and all the signs, and in what stone one must work to cut; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and briefly.  
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is lodged in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder seeming like water in its subtleness; and it opens harengues, and hardens the patient's penis, and he feels many times, and then retracts; and with many of these jumps the foundations are destroyed; and it is light for the healing of children until they have four years, and it is very grievous in old men, and is as much in-between between young and old; and the cure is lighter from those who have large stones, than from those who have them small. 
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the cure, it is necessary first to purify the patient by clyster, in order to draw out all the phlegm that is in the intestines. 
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it often hinders seeking the stone.  
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and dislocate them and move them downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and emerges occasionally from its high place; then make him sit between your hands properly, and his hands be below his thighs, so that the bladder be all declining downwards; then touch the urethra and feel inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut into the stone. 
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not fall to the touch of all, then moisten your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it into its base, and feel the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your finger, and put it outwards where you want to cut. 
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister that he presses the bladder with his hand, and he commands him to extend with his right hand the testicles upward, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the testicles in the part where one makes the incision; then he puts the spatula cutting, from which this is the form: 
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make between those which are between the buttocks and the foundation, neither in the middle but at the side of the left hip; and be straight on the stone, and the two sides be either foundation or above, and let the waist be like a traverse so that it is wide outward and inward narrow, according to the quantity of the stone, nor too great; perhaps the press that which is the foundation, that she leaps out without work; and know that there are such stones that have angles, and margins: so is grieved to pass; and if there is one that is submerged, like a lump, and round, whose issue is light. 
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	To him then where he has angles and margins, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, it is necessary that you pull with tongs which are like a file at the head, in order to extract the stone so that it does not escape; or you put below the subtle curved instrument at the head; and if you cannot manage it thus, then enlarge the hole of the opening, and if the stone does not come out, restrain it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stones, put the largest first at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then the tail forward, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.  
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be cauterized, and make a larger wound.  
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For the two things happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes back through where the legs cannot close; but nonetheless, you force to treat it, or to debride it with forceps, until you draw it in pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and restrain it, and put over it a bandage moistened in oil and wine, or in rose water and cold water, to appease the hot abscess; then re-stitch the patient on his collar, and do not untie the bond until the third day.  
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you set it, so well raised its place with oil and water, then the cure of ointment diaphicon and ointment basilcon, until it be healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes in the wound and corrosions, and blood clots in the bladder, and because of this urine is retained, which is known in such a manner that without jumping with the urine: therefore put in the wound all those things, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and burn it; then raise the wound from water and air and wool, and help him in every way that you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that all the hours that you cure him, you tie his two thighs together, and assemble the medicines on the place. 
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is where the urethra passes, and it is stuck there, and urine cannot issue; so the cure of those I say, that you should cut it many times, is excused from the cutting by this cure. 
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this thus. 
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I a piece of iron according to this form and let it be three-angled shaped in one stick. 
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a thread and tie it around the edge below the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then thrust the forest into the edge lightly, until it comes to the stone; and turn the forest in your hand at the stone point and point, as long as you can feel the stone from the other side; then the urine will soon come, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the edge. 
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is at once broken, and jump out with the urine, and it is healed for the patient; and if you cannot do this for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and the other above, then make the rod go straight into the stone between the two threads, then extract it further, and untie the thread, and clean up the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed. 
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women 
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that a stone is lodged in women, and if it happens at any time, the cure is grievous, and it is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-knowing who uncovers herself to midwives, even when she is chaste. 
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well-knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is more hidden than the stone of the man, which is why it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear. And if necessity arises for this, it is necessary that you choose a midwife well-knowing, and with pains find one, and if you cannot find one, then do not seek one; I cast mire subtil; and present her a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command of the inquiry of the stone; and look well whether the woman is a virgin: therefore it is necessary to put her down or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, constrain her below her down, and recommend her that she put her down or con with the patient, and seeks and presses her left hand upon the bladder forming.  
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it is necessary that she move it from side to side from the entrance of the bladder until below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh opposite the middle of the cone, where it appears to be emerging, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move its tail upwards or downwards, and let the incision be small at first; then insert the point into the waist, if you feel the stone so close to the wound as much as the stone can emerge further, and know that many types of stones are: namely, small and large and rough and smooth, long and round, and those that have ribs. 
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the likenesses to know the outcome. 
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the vein does not bleed, put on it powdered vitriol and hold it for an hour until the vein is stopped; then return to your work, as long as the stone is hard, and have the instruments that I told you in the extraction of stones to help you in your work; and if the vein does not bleed, and it is the artery that has been cut, put the powder on the place and strain it with bandages and bands, and do not begin again with this, and leave the stone and do not touch it, lest the patient die; then cure the wound. 
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is appeased, and the eyes are closed, then return to your work, as long as the stone is firm. 
de hernie carnouse	Of flesh hernia 
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquatic ramice is nothing else than an assembly of moisture or white syfac, which is the discharge from the heart of the testicles, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac," and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it to be another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac that we have said; and these do not have this point no.  
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this root is of weakness that comes to the testicles, and that matter is spread. 
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the joints, and this moisture has many colors: either declining to jaundice, or without red, or black, or aqueous white, and so on; and these are the signs to know this assembly, because if it is white as we have said, then the abscess reopens, like a long as the figure of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around. 
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, then the abscesses are redden with a part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white syfac, then one feels it well; therefore when you see to know the color of the moisture, it believes all the intromission quarreit, of which its form is before. 
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what then comes after the introducer, judge of what is inside. 
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the fullness of his body; then he lies on his back, on something a little high, and puts many cloths underneath him; then he sits on his left side, and commands the minister to sit on his right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs near the heart of the collarbones; then take the spatula, and cut the skin of the collarbone among them, long up to near the elbow, and let your incision be straight, dividing the skin of the collarbone until the white flesh, and scar it gently according to your power; then pierce the white flesh full of water through the wide opening, and extract all the water, and then put your bandages, and cover the white flesh upwards; and do not touch the heart of the collarbone, but only the white flesh; cut thoroughly or in pieces, the same way, the bone beneath it, that if you do not cut it wisely, the water will return; and if the knife has made its way through your work, put it back in place when you have finished the work of the white flesh; then assemble the two leaves of the collarbone with a suture, then cure it like other wounds, until it is healed.  
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cut the cord to the entire suspender, and remove the egg, and cure it as we have said. 
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the water is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you have done with the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put in the wound linen swabbed in rose oil; and put outside another swab soaked in wine and oil, and put on top of the two swabs, and put above double cloths, and bind it above all the linen according to this form: 
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two drapes, and employ them of wool padding according to this semblance and be assembled by stitch in the groin of the breeches, and one of the arms presses upon the foundation up to the back, and the other at the part of the armpit; and the other two chief above the two elbows, and be all assembled the restraint in the loop of the brazier; and sometimes is medicine this ramice of cautery in place of a size of iron, and it is that you prick the cautery cultellar subtil, and cut the skin of the stones, and be heated as we have said, so that the white sap that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that sap at once, and the scorch at this subtle hot cautery: 
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cope in all the ways that you can, as long as you scrape everything; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and moves keeping from loss of blood, and moves that the works of size; and if any thing makes you contrary, or abscess or discharge of blood or other thing, so cure what makes you contrary, according to what is said before. 
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to endure this work because of its horror, so administer a perforation as I tell you, and it is that when you are well certain by the meanings that we have said that the watery root is there, then make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the part below throughout the whole spatula wide, and put the perforation deep into the body; and let the opening be wide so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave for the remaining water to drain, then cure it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to flow out of the mouth of the wound, then you must pour into it a pen or the instrument with which one treats the water of the hydrophics, of which the form is previously given; and enlarge the hole of the wound, and know that the water returns, and is assembled after six months or whenever it enters, and when it is assembled as before, then the patient will pass his days. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the genitals 
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this member, there is fear in many positions, for which it seems to me that it is better to leave it; and I will tell you the work and appearances of the abscess. 
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come to the body, and even to the genitals; and this is by many causes.  
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to know by superfluity sour and ague, which is spread as boils, or from percussion; and is the color of the abscess according to the color of the body; and finds no pain, and is a grave abscess; and by chance are some abscesses grisly, fearful, and stony, and of a dull color, and sometimes comes from out of an artery, or from inflammation of a vein. 
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When this is by means of an artery, then it is known by the arrangement of a hot abscess, when you press it to your fingers; and it is not appropriate that you touch it. 
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made of the inflation of vein is known by his disposition to the expression of the touch of the two, and he can well do the cutting on this semblance, and on the other carts; and it is that you chop the core of the cones, then the egg being on top, and the track of the white there, and deliver the suspender from all parts of the egg. 
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the eye has already been joined with these threads, then you should pull out the eye, and cut it; and if it is trapped in the sac, or in those things that are inside the vessels, then you should deliver all of that space, and cut it roundly. 
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the cartilage is or its rear, then it is necessary that you cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said. 
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your works are accomplished, then use the wound of wool moistened in rose oil and wine, then care for it with other cares until it is healed. 
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the genitals 
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a boil wrapped in a wrapping resembling a bladder, with the softening of the cones, and the patient cries out when it moves; and the cure of this illness is as frightening as the one before, but nonetheless we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancients did. 
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It behooves you to make the patient sit on the elevated seat, then he binds the suspender of the groin down to your two hands, to all the vessels that are near the penis, and the masters cover them, and extend them; then cut with the sharp spatula wide through the middle of the vessels, as long as they are discovered, and then scrape from each side, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then put a needle where the vis is come, and bind it to the first place where the vis came, and bind it straight to the other end; then cut them in the middle directly, according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as the others where one enjures a bow, so that no vessel is cut which nourishes one of the testicles; for by these there comes no harm, and if to all the vessels comes vis, it behooves to drain the testicles to all the vessels; so that the testes do not lose their nourishment because of the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot be helped. 
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the hip 
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events of this branch are by the section that comes or there ifac, or the extension on the belly in the part of the angles, for which the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the corners; and this rupture is either at the dou syfac, or from the extension of it, and come these two manners of mouth of causes: either by percussion, or jump, or braire, or raising of heavy loads, and by similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension dou syfac, it is that it happens poc and poc, in long time, and does not come suddenly; and are the abscesses equal up to the parfont, for that the syfac hastens the intestines. 
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is of the section of the skin, that it brings at the beginning a sudden pain, and there are diverse appearances of abscesses, under the skin near, and this is for the issue of the intestine and the body to the outside of the skin. 
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the intestines are drawn into the wound, and are held in there, and cause great pain to suffer the patient, even when it is pressed.
