Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron there is fear, for which it behoves one to shun. 
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command the patient to bring the intestine in his hand inside the wound, if it can enter; then hold it on its neck between your hands, and lift the hips; then have the heart above, and cut all the skin of the groin long; then put inside the loin folds needles according to what you need to open the wound, and be such that the eyes may issue; then peel the syfac which is below the skin of the groin, until the white syfac is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger into what follows the groin, in what is between the white syfac which is below the skin of the eye, and between the second syfac, and depart from what is behind the eye, and between the second syfac; and then move with the right hand inside the heart of the groin, and hold the white syfac on high to your left hand, and raise the eye to all the syfac towards the waist; and command the minister that he stretch the eye upward, and untie what is behind the ligament; and seek with your fingers if there is any intestine enveloped or white syfac hard, and if you find any of these things, put it into the belly below; then take a needle which has a thick thread made of X threads, and put it in the back part of the syfac, which is after the skin of the groin; after the waist, then cut the hairs that appear from the threads, as long as there are IV threads; then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and tie the syfac, about which we have said it is below the skin of the groin, with a strong thread of II parts; then envelop the hairs of the threads, and tie them forming of II parts, so that none of the vessels that nourish them can enter into, but that the abscess may not come; and put the thread straight according to the first long thread II times of that one, and after these II threads leave the syfac which is below the heart of the groin the size of a finger; and after all the others according to the roundness that the eye carries; then cut in the part which is below the skin of the groin, as long as the without correction, and the bow, as we have said before; then administer wool soaked in oil, and put it into the wounds, and put in the thread that we have said. 
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes is cauterized the whites as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of a decrease in blood. 
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the ligature remain as long as it sticks to itself; and if it delays at falling away, be raised by hot water, and put upon it that which we have said, until it falls off; then cure the wound with other remedies, until it is perfectly healed. 
de hernie carnouse	of fleshy hernia 
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.  
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like a branch that is assembled with the veins, in such a manner that you bind the vessels, after the cut above or lightly below; then cut it in half, and treat the abscess of those who operate, until the vessels bleed; and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy. 
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture occurs in the bowels, as we have said, and it opens them; and do not insert any of the intestines into the anus, and if any are inserted there, it is little, and repairs all hours; and nonetheless if it remains too long in this place, then the wound or abscess increases, as much as the intestine is inserted; and this happens by the extension of the abscess which is in the bowels, as we have said, because it is extended, then it is softened and swollen the bowels and opened; and the cure is thus by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner: and that is that the patient lies down completely on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the rupture open widely according to the quantity of III fingers; and then extract the abscess which is below the skin that follows it, then take the rait and put it on the place appearing of the abscess; and press it to the bottom of the belly, then sew the II places appearing of the abscess onto the top of the rait, and sew one and the other; then extract the top of the rait, and do not cut any of the abscess nor extend the skin or anything else, as I have made you know in the cure of the ramice of the intestines; then cure by the cure of the wounds. 
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, if it is defaced and care for the wound, until it is healed.  
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The suture is constrained, and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cautery is moved in this place, and closer to salvation. 
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening of the skin of the genitals 
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles in certain men softens, because the bags that are within them are softened, and it is easy to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the sick man lie on his back, and one cuts the skin that is softened on the natural skin; then assemble the II lips to a stitch, and if you see, first sew the superfluity of the softened skin to III stitches or IIII firmly; then cut between the stitches, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.  
dou chastrement	Through chastisement 
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that cauterization is common in our law, and for this reason I would like not to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: one of which is that the reader may be able to respond when asked about it, and know the cure; and the other, because we often have need of cauterization of some animals to aid us, such as goats and sheep and oxen, and other beasts. 
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that a cauterization is done in two ways: either by attraction or by fending. 
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water, until the hooves are softened and pliable; then taking them with your hand, as long as they are put back and you no longer feel them.  
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of tail: it is necessary that you hold the beast and press the skin of the scrotum with your left hand, then tie the suspensory, and cut on each testicle with a blow, when you will have well scraped them; and leave no point where there is itching and the subtle itch which is on the vessels; and this manner of chastisement is better than that done by attraction, because in attraction it happens that nothing remains from the scrotum, by which the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
des hermofrodites	Of the hermaphrodites 
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is according to II ways as men: one if it is that between the II sexes opens as the figure of nature of a woman, where it has hair, and sometimes in short the urine.  
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and about the nipple as well as a staff and they copulate. 
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is that you cauterize all the warts, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine leaps through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.  
de la tentigene	of the tenting 
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tumor is a growth attached to the natural part, as long as it is too unsightly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and that is the cure. 
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the tendon to your hand or with tweezers, and lightly cut it; and do not go too deeply, so that bleeding does not come, then treat it with another cure until it is healed; and for one other sore that is born at the mouth of the margin, and the limb, and by chance may be said to have been bitten, and according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called it by the ancients “disease of the cow”.   
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cover it, as we have said the tendon, and the care until it is healed. 
de erratique	of erratic 
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by illness that comes to it; or it is by a char joined, or by subtle or thick syfac, and is made in the marrow, or in ribs, or below, or wherever; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the gaze of the bailey. 
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the stop is near appearing, then to the two or to the rail.  
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is painful subtly, and it is close to the two livers, then hurry, and do this: put your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then hold the two livers, so that the subtle syfac is round, and covered with the swelling; then take wool, and soak it in oil, and place it on the spot, and lay the woman down at home every day, so she cannot move. 
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the sty is hard and thick, then it is necessary that you cut it with a spatula seeming like a myrtle leaf. 
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh, then suspend it with a bandage and cover it; and take the medicines that staunch blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and an equal amount of egg white; then apply a poultice of wool wide enough so that the wound may not close; and thus let it remain long, and administer a tent of dry linen; then be cured with other dressings until it is healed. 
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh comes new clay, then it should be covered in this manner, if it is not abscesses suppurating. 
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is in the flesh one must not touch with fire. 
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids 
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without usual custom and when hemorrhoids become old they become hard; and we have said in the division the resemblances of them, and the signs, and I will say here those which resolve cure.  
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the boils, when they are brought in the marsh, and they do not appear to the touch, unless it is cured by iron. 
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, one can feel them, those who can be healed. 
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then estent the altul as tongs, and the cope at its roots, then powder above medicines restraining blood, such as acaice and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then place her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is a bleeding, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confection it with honey and aisil, and apply it as a poultice on her back. 
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stays put, it is good. 
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If this is not the case, apply to the back and breasts with suction cups without piercing; then take linen and moisten it in juice of plantain or in elderberry juice with old wine, and apply it to the place. 
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, care for its place with ointment until it is healed; and the one that is called "albathir" is red, and is similar to the sharp chief, so it should be covered as I have said in the previous text; and then care for it until it is healed. 
des apostemes de la marris	of the abscesses of the marsh 
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of abscess come in the flesh, such as cancer and festering abscess and herpes and boils and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and more other diseases that I have said in the division. 
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the marshes, which is not like the abscesses that swell; and if you want to know the work of iron, then look at whether the abscess is thick at the beginning of its arrival, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red if you can see it. 
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not hasten to pierce, but let him rest until the pain is calmed; and then make the patient sit on a seat, and have small seats or he may lean, and support his back and bring together his legs at the outer part of the leg; and let his thighs be spread, and put his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good band; then turn him towards the right side, and administer there the instrument by which one works on the mouth of the ear, because after that comes the form; and it is necessary when you see administering this instrument, that you put the tip first in order to know the depth of the ear, so that what enters inside the instrument does not come more deep than it should, and that it does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the ear with cloths, so that the instrument does not grieve him; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and that he hold the instrument. 
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens and one moistens it with the hand, then it is proper to cover it at the chief, to the spatula of lead; and when the boil is emptied, then it is proper that you put into the wound wet tents in rose oil, or in green oil dry; and put the tent further from the wound to the edge of the marsh, and put outside on the marsh and on the linen cloth clean moistened in water or malves are cooked; then cure after II days of ointment before this, until it is healed; and sometimes one raises the marsh and the wound by enema of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lilies and aristeologe long are cooked; then return to the ointment.  
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is put back in the flesh, then you must guard yourself from cauterizing with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division. 
de l’enfantement	of the birth 
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The first job is to the midwife that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and signs so are when you see the woman press down below, and desire to smell: therefore hurry the child out by force; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the head first, and the buttocks with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press lightly her belly, so that the child issues quickly; for when it comes up on its head, then the buttocks come with it, and is cleansed the mother of her superfluities by good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. 
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes sometimes upon his feet, and comes to the force of the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes upon his belly, or groin, and is turned by chance onto his neck, and by other bad figures; so it is necessary that the bailiff be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help him. 
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural birth, and the woman cries in childbirth, and the strength of her is feeble, then have her sit upon a saddle, or the women hold her; and rose her nature of oil or fenugreek be cooked, and then put the baile between her two thighs with the small spatula whose form is here: 
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cleave the secondine, and cut to its nail until the moisture that is within is gone; and hold the belly of the woman as long as the child descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to clysterize the woman with fenugrec husk with sesame oil; then have her suck and sneeze with condiment, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus the child will now be extracted. 
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands issue forth, it is necessary that you set them lightly back and forth; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman upon the seat, and lift her feet up high; then overturn the seat to the ground, and hold the woman, so that she does not fall during the overthrowing; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife which is placed before, and extract the child, and reset them equally. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child on its feet 
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up on his feet, it is necessary to push upwards; and then turn back and forth, until it is equal; then seize the feet and extend back and forth. 
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	He jumps until his hips, if he is commanded to take, and makes him sneeze from condition; if he will, God help him. 
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it back and forth, until it is according to the natural shape.  
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore, there must be treated lightly. 
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come forth as we have said, then take muscle-meat of the arm, and sesame oil, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit upright up to below the ribs; and when she is softened below, make her wear the collar of myrrh, and put it below, and let her remain one hour; then make her sit upon the seat, then make her sneeze and restrain her mouth and nose, and take hold of her belly gently, for the child now jumps. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue of the child on his knees 
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, he puts his hands up and down; then it is laid on its neck, and the legs hang down, and lying on the bed; and bends his hands up and down, and then he takes the hands on the belly, and removes the pillows below, until she is prepared down; and if the child does not jump, he takes its feet and moves them gently, then moves the belly up, then puts his hands; and holds the child up and down; and commands the woman to keep it still as long as the child will.  
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child who comes out by a wide hand during 
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to devise a way to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand up and go; if she cannot go, make her lie on the bed and spread her legs apart; then administer the poultice that I have described; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then try to bring back the hand; and place the child according to its natural form, and make her sneeze, and command her to press down as long as the child is issuing. 
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the issue of the child on its neck, and have spread its hands, and its face turned toward the back of its mother 
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bailiff hold his hand, then turn it little by little, and lightly; and when it is equal, he puts on the nature muscillage of altitude and oil, as we have said, then he commands her to move little by little; and when you will have done this, he makes her sit on the seat, and commands her to stretch; and she sneezes. 
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all of the spine 
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for the whole secondine, so strike the secondine with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child can rest on its face and on its neck, so strike from under the bud that it be not held back, and kill the child; then put the child inside, as long as you have placed it as it should be, and command the woman to refrain from any time: therefore it will go more easily.  
de l’issue des gemelz	of the separation of the twins 
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens often. 
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and do not live well, if they have no name; I know them, that they are multiplied, and are separated by the  sheath which divides them, which is tied to the bud; and sometimes they come out as naturally as all under, as we have said. 
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they raise violently, so the cure as we have said, and be the treatment subtle, and make quickly and lightly what she does; and make thus as it is worth moves to salvation.  
de plusors enfans	of many children 
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the marshes I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of their glorious sage, and it is necessary that the bail knows all these, because by chance something seems to happen; so it is done according to what is necessary.  
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child 
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are constrained to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no accident or she has fear of death; then it is necessary that the woman be laid on her back, and her hips inclined down, and her legs raised; and the minister hold the groin from II parts, or she is bound to the bed so that she is not moved by the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the vagina with moist oils with a wash of alfalfa and fenugreek and flax seed, then oil the belly of her hands with these oils and washes; then put them into the vagina lightly, then desire the place where she puts the pins that are suitable to those, and take ward if the child is appearing that it descends on its head; then put the pins in her eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the chin or in the throat or near the ribs, and if the descent is on the feet, then put them or prickle and at the sides of the ribs; and it is necessary that he holds the pin with his right hand, and puts the curve between his two fingers of the left hand, and puts it all over his hand lightly, and puts the pin in any of these places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the pin:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then place one against the other one, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are equal; and then move them equally in both directions, to let it pass smoothly, and let the incisions be toothed to hold it as this is the form: 
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part of it, he anoints the bail with some of his oil, and puts them in that part, and draws the other part; and if none remain, he puts this onchine or higher up, and does this until it comes out entirely. 
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you should wrap it in the drape until it is whole; then cut in the joint of the foot or at the ankle, and in this way you should do in the other hand, and as to the feet. 
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is stuck in the issue, where there is or chief aigue assembled, then it is necessary that you put the spatulum spinous between your two, and make the chief and extract the aigue; or you turn it with the instrument that is called "almidach," so that the form comes with the instruments or chapter which is after this one; and in the same way do if the infant has a large head naturally; and then draw out the bones with pliers, and if the head jumps out and it is restrained by force, then cut it, as much as the moisture that is or worse issue; and if it cannot issue, so cut it by pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then it is necessary that you pierce it until the moisture runs. 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the addressing to the mouth of the shaft is light.  
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is in the belly or breast, then it is necessary that you draw it out to the drape enveloped upon the hand; and make the belly or breast, until the moistures which are there cure; and if the other members are ossified, and the head remains, then put the bath your hand into of the marrow; and it draws until the mouth of the marrow; then put in the needle or II, and it draws forth; and if the mouth of the marrow is contracted for a boil which has come there, then it is not necessary to work on it, but it is necessary to administer moist and fatty things; and administer poultices, and sieves in softened and moisturizing water. 
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on his side, and you can put him even, administer what we have said in the living child; and if one has no power, so that it be treated by pieces, and leave nothing of the secondary. 
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if he is given the things that we have said about abscesses that come in the marsh; and if bleeding comes out, it should be put in a sharp restricting bandage, and given other treatments. 
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly one child had been dead, then she conceived another on top of that one, and refused to give birth to the other.  
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time there came an abscess in the buttock, and it swelled so much that it opened, and began to great purulence. 
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought long about it, and could not suture the wound.  
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a plaster of strong attraction, and from it emerged one bone, and after some days another. 
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly astonished because this belly has no bones.  
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought that it was the bones of a dead child. 
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I looked at the wound, and in between my hands bones, until the woman was in a better state; and I saw the woman long time like this, and she had there a little bit of bowe from that place; and I don't remember this chapter further because for that reason, when masters find a strange thing, they know how to put help. 
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place 
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the presser, which is found in the books; and to its two shoulders, the two limbs. 
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle of the restrictor, and made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the shaft I must be wide, and the edges of the trees I must, and long one palm and a half; and between the two limbs they should be two adjustments of this same shaft, which are fastened in one and the other, of half a palm long or a point more; and these two adjustments are put into the mouth of the marris to open when one turns the two horns. 
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	One other form, in its semblance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of pliers; and it has two jaws with adjustments, as you see, a palm's length long, and two fingerbreadths wide; and when you see opening the vagina with the whole instrument, so make the woman lie on her bed, her feet apart and legs open, then put the two clamps together in the vagina, and hold the head of the instrument below between her thighs; then work your hand on the whole instrument, as you have done with pliers equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the vagina, until the girl does what she wants.  
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument are all surmounted, and they multiply their likenesses; and when the mirror has shown them well, then is the work more hasty, and higher to men for their quantity. 
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument, so long as it is well equipped, because its necessity is not excusable.  
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is held back during childbirth, it is necessary that you command the woman to retain her arm, and then make her sneeze with condisi, and restrain her hands at her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, well is. 
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If it is not the case, if you take a pot, and make it perforated or covered, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, whether cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put one end of a cord or perforated pot into it, and the other end in the mouth of the marsh, and tie it so that the vapors come inside the marsh; then make it sneeze, as we have said. 
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If you jump the second joint violently. 
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this cure, and there is no more force, command the midwife to moisten her left hand in oil of sesame or in muscus of altea, and then put it into the nature, and seeks the secondine; and when she has found it, she grips it and extends it point by point directly, so that the marri[s] does not fall to the extraction; but it is necessary to move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come and disengage.  
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the marsh is tightly closed, we have said the cure of sneezing, and fumigation of herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, so guard that you do not use milk; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marsh, that you tie it to the hip of the woman, then cl isterize with ointment tetrafarmaçon; if she will bear and return, and come forth; but nevertheless, when she bears, if evil odor comes to the stomach and head, and pales the patient. 
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is fitting therefore fumigation suitable to these: none of the ancients have experimented fumigation of cress and dried figs. 
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument for which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the second is this: 
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And is to see semblance to a hound, and puts one the head subtle in the nature, and the shoulders wide above the fire; and be the fumigation above the coals, and the rag until it is burned out, and begins another. 
de percier lou fondement	To examine the foundation 
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but it is stopped by a subtle syfac: so it behooves the midwife that she pierce that syfac to its due, and does not pierce it with a sharp spatumile, and guard the lacement so that she does not touch it; then put above a cloth soaked in wine and oil, then the cure of ointment until it is healed. 
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not reset, put in a splint of wood, and leave it for several days, and remove it when the child wants to go to bed. 
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this stopping of pain comes from the hardening of a wound or an abscess; so it is necessary to cover that hardened part; if it be cured, as we have said of the cauterization of lead. 
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula of the foundation 
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the foundation are nodules, and larger than those that come near the foundation outside, or in the space of the two parts, if there is a fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and encore moisture arises white or subtle bows, and sometimes these fistulas pierce; and they are known by those who have them or ejection or windiness when the patient makes an expulsion, and perhaps in jumps one.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if to fistulas that pierce up to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and reach up to the junction of the hip, and to the knee of the thigh. 
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing at the foundation, and not passing; and it is that you put your right index or foundation, and put a needle subtle of iron or of steel in the fistula when there is no tortuosity. 
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, then put a tent of fine wool or horse hair in until you feel the tent or hair at its point; and if you do not feel it, and there comes no outward discharge nor swelling nor blister, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; so hasten to cure. 
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced up to the bladder or to the urinary tract, then the urine leaks out, and cannot be healed by medicines. 
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the juncture of the hip, then the tendon coming up to its place; if there is no twisting and the invention of pain around, then it is that there is a bow in it, and there is no medicine or healing by ointment; and in these piercing fistulas there is no cure other than labor, and vanity of fools who intervene. 
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one who is neither too young nor too old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have proven, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and you lift his legs up to his hips, and let his hips incline to his belly; then put a tent of iron, or of lead if there is tortuosity, as long as you know where the tent comes. 
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it near the foundation, then you should put your index finger there, so feel as if it is being pulled by it; and be uncovered or you feel between your finger the skin or the flesh, then you know that it is pierced; if you don't work on it much it cannot be healed.  
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One says forthwith it can be well cured some, but that happens little; and the aid one makes, if is one carefully heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it was said before; and puts it all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the foundation; and do this II times or III, as long as you know that these chars are burned, which are seeming like a feather of an eye; and then cure with tampons moistened in butter, as long as those chars issue, then cure with ointment enjuring char and soldering. 
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healthy, then well. 
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this, otherwise cannot be healed; and if it is caught in between, and does not pierce to the root which is the foundation, and between your tooth and the tent a thick covering of flesh or of syfac, and you see the fistula following the covering of the heart; so cut from the beginning of the fistula, and push forward past the tent, and then cauterize afterwards, as long as it reaches to the head of the tent; and will be delivered the tent, and fall; then mold those flesh-covered things that resemble a bird's feather, and none remain. 
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound gets worse, and goes between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine. 
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cautery of fire assembles II good things: that is to say, the burning of these joined bones, and the stopping of blood and the drying of moisture; then the cure of wounds moistened in butter or in crushed herbs, as long as the flesh lies low, and if the bones are burned in the hollow; then cure the wound of sores with hard dried substances, and they are dry medicines. 
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return. 
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the very bottom of the foundation, and is separated from the body, then you should probe its opening and examine it carefully.  
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between it is the canvas or the syfac or carts, where it is close to piercing, if there is no other way except that of faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it to the bottom, or if you can put tents and care as before; and do not go too deep in so far that you do not cut the tenement that holds the foundation, and come the evacuations by lay sense volenteit; then cure, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and the wound once it is cut from below its foundation, or by tent or by another appointed instrument; then define that char fautree which is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to remain the fistula in the part outside the foundation: so it will be a lighter thing for the patient. 
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this manner: and when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side of the bottom near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form: 
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts the thread twisted in it, and puts the tent to all the thread into the fistula until it is at the head.  
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation within, then extract the thread of that which is pierced, as you would put your finger or foundation; and treat the head of the thread, and assemble the two heads together, and restrain one to the other, and leave it for a day or two; and restrain it no time, until the threads join those which are between two, and stick; then cure the wound until it is soldered and healed. 
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, make it pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deeply embedded. 
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make a ligature cover so when it is made, and then cure it as we have said, until it is healed. 
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spittle spine from which one makes a fistula is very thin on one side and trenches; and on the other side no, because we do not cut what we do not need to cut, as you see here: 
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids 
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhages are according to II manners: or they are within the foundation, as grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and in short added blood, and there are one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are outside have little moisture, and in short or a little of citrine water or a little of blood, and they have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them within the foundation, is that you command the patient to strain to go into rooms, as long as the foundations are healed, and the threads appear; then hasten, and you can take it with tweezers, or you hold it with your finger, then cut it at its roots; and if the needle cannot hold it because of its moisture, then take it with the cloth, or cotton, or a piece of chamois; and extract it to your fingers, then cut it, and powder above some hot powders that are in their place of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said or chapter of cautery, then cure the other cures until he is healed; and if the foundation cannot issue, then enema the patient with a biting and sharp enema to wash what is at the foundation, so that it can issue openly; when the patient strains, and if the threads are outside the foundation, then the cure is light; and is that you take them with your finger or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until he is healed, and that he fears the incision by iron.  
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you administer the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread and put it through a needle, and then draw the thread upwards and make the needle pass through from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and so be wide; and tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave one to correct the superfluity of blood; then place on the foundation a thin cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate, and place it on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then leave him until they are dry, and when they are dry, cure them with ointment and other cures, until he is healed. 
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of drying of the veins or foundation 
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there happens drying of humors in the intestine, and by constriction of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine no longer works there.  
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you scrape to the point of a spatula or with your fingernail the bark above, which does not leave it moist; then cure it until it is healed as it should; and if it cannot heal, begin the scraping again more strongly than before, until it heals well, and is scraped; then cure it until it is healed.  
dou fremit	from shaking  
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants is a little appearance false before the body, and goes much in by force; and sometimes it finds the cold, and feels it also like dead of fever, and comes in all the body, and more to the hands than other part.  
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a caine of a goose feather, or a vulture feather strong, and put that caine on the fremit, until the circles prickle the fremit all around; then turn your hand to the whole caine until you cut all around the fremit, and put it in its entirety, and scrape the fremit from its roots. 
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so do this of a serpent of iron or steel according to this form, and be subtle below and trailing above: 
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not feel it, to hold on to the two, and squeeze them together, and if you see it, then cauterize the furrow as it is in the chapter of cautery. 
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the clyster 
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes a clyster of silver or of archaut, or of lead melted or woven; and sometimes one makes these instruments small and large, according to those to whom they are administered. 
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those therefore who are administered to in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small. 
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clyster small and great is above wide, where the belly is tied in this manner: 
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a severance where the abdomen is tied, as you see, and the shoulder is pierced inside; and on one side II is pierced, and on the other I; and the abdomen where one puts the medicines of a bladder of beast or parchment, and is pierced all around with small punctures, and has between each puncture I space; then put in these punctures I strong thread of thread twisted like X or as it goes around, and assemble the abdomen like a kid; and when the medicine is inside, tie the lie to the instrument before with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle: 
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the chief of the rectum with oil or egg yolk, or something similar, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes it with his two hands together, until it is all covered, then remove the clyster, and lift the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to issue, let it come as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night on top of it, then it is greater help.   
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you treat it with a disorder of the belly and the medicine hastily issues from there, repeat it until it is cured. 
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the base or abscess, so is the clyster as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin should be strained. 
des plaies	of wounds 
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will say the treatments of hands and medicine, according to accomplishment. 
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of what they are made. 
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the cutting of stone, and sword and knife, or spear or staff or sickle, or similar things; which are done according to their places on the body, as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and begin with the simplest wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
