Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or on the head, and the bone is not broken, so take care if it is of a stone or similar things, and the skin is readily torn and is the wound large, and you doubt heavily of an abscess hot: so do immediately bleed from the cephalic same as if it comes little blood from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the affected part; and avoid the patient repletion of wine and thick meats. 
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat be lessened, and drink no wine, nor eat any meat; and put on the wound, if there comes an abscess, moistened cotton in rose oil only, or in styptic wine; and if there is no abscess hot, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if it has been moved by the air, put on some ointment, until he is healed. 
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by tents, then bring them together by suture, as I will say for wounds of the belly, of the suture. 
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is open to the bone, and hanging, and only holds by a bit, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as beef and cooked grain, also beans, and similar things. 
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a rotten skin and it does not reach the bone, so cut out all the rot and throw it away, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be stopped without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then cauterize the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it. 
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light: and it is that you put in this powder which solidifies as soon as the fire has touched them. 
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take frankincense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it dries well and joins with all its blood; and then bandage it well, and leave it untied if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed. 
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And no times is this done with just chalks, when one does not have incense nor the blood of dragon, but that the fire has closed the wound. 
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has been cleansed properly and is still open, then do not put on this powder but apply some boiled cloths or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey until it softens. Then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.  
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with a wound, and it is small, then I will extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you later about fractures of the head.  
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck 
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this one and the other of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.  
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerve, there is no other thing to do than leave the cure, and put nothing restraining, because it harms the nerves and makes them retreat; and do not put on the wound anything cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation of them is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as calx washed in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cupped wash also in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments. 
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, so the side and tie with bandages, then care until it is healed. 
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and he is covered and full of bowel, pierce or lower them; and if the artery is cut, and there is bleeding, then cauterize it, and tie it, and this is what you must do; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the vein, and the conduit is kept, because the flesh goes in, so sew the heart on the chain of the throat, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural figure; and then restrain it well and leave it for some days, then cure it with ointments until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then set it; and if there are pieces of bone, take them out all that you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them as long as the wound suppurates, and be cleared and aligned the issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said. 
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in my chapter. 
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of lance or knife  
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, see if from the wound there escapes windiness as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put any powder at first hour, nor bind it so that the blood does not remain deep, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there comes no spasm, nor bad tremor of heart, nor strangling of the breath; and when you see the good dispositions, know that the wound is saved. 
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure then with tents and other dressings, as long as it is healing; and if it cannot heal and work, know that there is a fistula; and treat it as one should. 
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or deeper or on the back, so cure that which is in front; if it is large, suture it; and if it is small, with powder; and if it is embedded in bone, and has broken pieces, so clean the wound, and pull out the fragments if they are loose; and if they are not loose, so leave it to rot, so that it will alleviate the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said. 
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the displacement of the belly 
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; sometimes a large wound causes an intestine or nerve of the intestines to protrude, which is why the introduction of something happens; and sewing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one, because one returns the intestines inside, unless they are put in warm by warm; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, so they enter more tightly, and that's why the middle wound is worse, because of this we reset the intestine to its place like the others. And know that the rupture of the belly is in four ways: the two common seams happen in the seam of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body and two other particular sutures are common with other wounds; and nonetheless they are more proper with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and declare. 
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestine is outside, and it is a thing to be put back, this is done by one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen because of the cold. 
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or soft cloth with hot water only, or you boil the water, straining and adding juniper and pepper, and apply to the intestine until the swelling is removed; and sometimes do this restraining, and then it can be moved that it alone deflates. 
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling departing, moisten the intestine with water or ale and mallows be cooked, because by these is aligned the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a hole in the wound with the instrument by which one cuts hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to moisten that tail, that no one should cut it except great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting it: so trench inside in the curve and outside no, and see here the form. 
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have jumped out, put them back in their natural form in their proper place if you are able, for this is valuable to heal.  
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, put the head and buttocks higher than the parts below, and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to that the wounded part be higher than the other; and thus you must administer what I say in large and medium wounds. 
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Small wounds put what you have appeared, then take between your hands I minister piteous who holds all the rupture in its hand, and assemble the lips; and this is the common way of sutures, and is that you prick a needle or more, according to the quantity of the breadth of the wound, then leave from the chief of the wound I doi of space, and there put a needle where it has I good strong thread; and pierce the II chiés dou cuir with the II chiés dou siphac, which is desoz le cuir dedens, as long as you make it pierced on that side, and assemble the II chief dou siphac the IIII ensamble; then the strain of a double thread around the needle of II parts, then assemble the II chiés de la plaie avenanment, and then leave I doi d’espaice, and there put another needle; then the tie the thread as you have done the first needle, and do not cease to do so according to what you need needles, until the whole wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, because the subtle needles cut all the flesh, and the too thick ones can't enter well: therefore it is necessary that they be medium; and it is not necessary to put the needles too outside the flesh and leather, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; and then cut the points of the needles so that they do not prick the patient while sleeping, and I put tents or drapes on the points of the needles for them to hold, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this way of suturing with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because it suffices a needle or II Li second suture if it is common, and is that you assemble the II chiés dou cuir and the II chiés dou syfac together on a needle where it has I medium strong thread; and when you have pierced these points all IIII ensamble, then turn the needle to the part where you have begun, in the manner in which one sews clothes; and put space between each suture the thickness of a minor doe; this suture serves the man, and I sewed a wound on a man's belly who had been cut by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines were well II palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly. 
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for XXIV hours, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and I cured him, and he was healthy. 
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mire had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, because I was in the place where one could find none, nor any medicine; and I put more than once a day cotton old on top of the wound, and I washed it with honey water until it was healed. 
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing: take the needle, and put it from the outside part to the inside; when it has pierced the heart straight in a straight line, you leave the tip above the skin where you have put in the needle, and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside; and the meaning of this sewing is that you sew as the furrier sews furs, and that you leave one end of the thread on one side, and take it back on the other, until the sewing is complete. 
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of sewing, which the Gauls call properly, is like any font, which bring together the two parts naturally and apply one chief to the other chief, in this manner: prick a needle or chief of mirach near, and make it pierce that place alone, and leave the two chiefs of the syfac; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part until the inside, at the two chiefs of the syfac; then make it pierce both from the outside to the inside, in two other chiefs of mirach which are on the other side; and this is the middle manner of sewing and the most common. 
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galians says this word, and no one testifies to it, one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one must push one needle on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew ropes; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is more grievous than the other parts of the belly.  
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are like those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh in all its blood, so that the poultice has moved it, then put back the intestine, and the outer part; then put on powder enclosing flesh, and if the poultice has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound bows; and sew the edges, and suture the sides, and the mirach; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healthy; and if you have no medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to get bowed, old cotton, and move it II times a day until it is healthy. 
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in more cases than wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make community with the principal members, it is necessary that you moisten the linen light in oil of temperate heat, or in rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or rot in bowels, and many times happens, then the clysters of black wine are given to them, and even if the rot comes up to the intestine; and pierce it inside, and know that when this is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.  
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is pierced, and this is because of the proximity of the veins, and for the subtlety of the whole body, and the approximation of its nature to the nerves. 
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the worm jumps out of the wound, put it back in as with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned to black, then you must tie the place that is black so that bleeding does not come from it, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the two parts, and put the two heads hanging from the side below the wound until outside to align the extraction when the worm falls, and the wound bows.  
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel 
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is pierced, and the wound is small, in some men it can be restored because I saw a man who was wounded or belly of a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became inflamed and became a fistula, and into it came the excrement and the windiness; I put care according to what I could, and did not cease to treat until it was healed, and the ends joined. 
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him weld, I doubted that the patient had evil in his belly; and he had no evil, but remained in better dispositions, and eating and drinking; and some experimentors said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such a manner: take threads with large heads, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the thread covers its mouth, put it on top of the two lips, so that it strains its mouth upwards; and then cut the head, and this stays so that it cannot untie, then put the other thread afterward in the same manner as before, until the wound is entirely closed; and sew the wound. 
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is burned in the intestine and there comes no nuisance to the patient, and one can tie the intestine of a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the head of this thread of intestine that is well-cleaned, and then tie to the head of this thread the thread of fine linen twisted, then put the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back in the rupture; and this manner of sewing of threads is not worse than according to the way of marriage and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is nothing else or saneness, except subtlety. 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be 
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is universally called "fistula," and also when it is healed and turned inwards. 
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the truth a knot false and white, where one does not feel pain, and it is also covered like the feather of a bird; and sometimes in clear bowe, and other times thick; sometimes thin, and other times enough; and I have spoken of it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh, it is only by one of the IX causes: that is to know, by the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside, and on the lips, that does not let flesh be born; or there is too much bowe; or the leus is rotten, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is a manner of pestilence; or because the property in the region is late digestion, and slow healing, and swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and cures of medicines in the division. 
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary for me to tell you the cure of a fistula which is done by the work of hands. 
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come to the large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the liver, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the ribs, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so that it comes to the property of the principal member, and to the similar ones. 
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of grief healing, and there is only labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you want to know it, then take a tent of lead or iron, if the fistula is straight, so if it is twisted; and if the fistula is twisted, then surround it with a subtle tent of lead, because the lead bends well around the twisting; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well surround it by tents, then cauterize it through one of the openings, because the moisture goes from one opening to another, and it cleanses it; then surround it carefully as much as you can, so that you know if there are bones or nerves, and is pierced in depth, and ask the patient about the pain that he feels when pressing with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you will truly know the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the foul matter and corrupt flesh that are inside; and then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is well deep, straight place, then you must cut as deeply as possible, then put moist tents in a medicinal glue, and push them until the chief of the fistula, so long as the medicine corrodes the superfluity that is at the bottom; and then put ointments healing good flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerves do not trouble or principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so cleanse as long as the corruption is all removed, then cure of things happening flesh until it is sound; and if it is not sound, and returns bowed as before, know that you are not well gone to the bottom: so uncover and go as far as you can, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus sound, it is good. 
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If that is not the case, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot reach it; if there is nothing else but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small bone corrupted, and you can extract it with tweezers, if it must be extracted with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, then extract them all, do not leave even one; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, then cut through both moisture and flesh, and deliver the bones. 
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, put on the wound a thing hindering rot, and let it remain as long as the flesh is rotting around the bones, and then they will have more easily the bones; and if it is large bones, such as of leg or thigh, so leave only the corruption as long as the blackness is entirely removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption, and comes up to the marrow of the bone; then it is necessary to be and cover all up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is joined; and I will tell you of a fistula that happened to the man in his leg, so that you take example from it and help in your work. 
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about XXX years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body, so much that the materials came to the leg, and he became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no external cause to open; but the midwives out of their folly opened it so much that the abscess opened, and they corroded a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and many openings came that all oozed pus and moisture from the body; and many midwives treated him for about II years, and there was no sage in the art of hands, until I was called to him, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and what corroded through the openings a great deal; and the young man’s body became red, and had a yellow color.  
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these pits, and then searched all the pits, and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg. 
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I therefore began and pricked in one of the holes until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption came to the inside bone; I saw what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for that which I had removed; and began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, and could not solder; and then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I saw it, and then removed it, and decided to solder the place; but I was not able, as long as I pricked around a palm of the bone, and the wound appeared throughout its whole length, then I restored it with medicines; and it became healthy and soldered quickly, and did not need to begin the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who cannot bear, and for the fear of death that I had of him. 
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but it was cured completely, and in place of the bone grew a hard cartilage, and it was well-disposed and did not have any inconvenience or contrary at all, neither going nor coming. 
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner: take I linen and restrain it at the head of the bone that is open, and command anyone that he extend it upward; and put another linen band thicker than the first linen, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone, and keep the head so that you draw the corrupted flesh downward, and uncover the flesh on the place where you wish to be, that the bone may not break the flesh; and put tinder or a board under the bone so as to cover the corrupted flesh; and it must be treated as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and be treated again another time. 
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is rotten and does not open, and the rot is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh entirely; then put a piece of wood beneath, and then with silk thread from one side to the other bring the rot together, and let the silk thread be as long as the length of the rot, as we have said; and if the rot is in the joint, cut the rotten joint, and thread silk between the bones on either side; and if the rot is in the continuation of the two joints, there is nothing else to do but to cut it; and if the rot is in the finger of the hand or in the finger of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must examine that rot, how it opens for you; and cleanse it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not oppose you; and know that the instruments and threads to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to equip each kind of work with its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; so think about the instrument which you need according to what is right. 
dou feu	of fire 
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joint can be affected either from within or from outside; and when you have medicated that corrosion by the treatment of medicines, and they do not profit, then it is necessary to cover that limb until the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes through this from death, or from the malice, which is greater, of the fault of the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and then after the blackness, that corrosion of the limb goes from limb to limb, and takes over the whole body; therefore hasten to cover, and if it is from the percussion of some venomous beasts, such as scorpions of the sea and viper and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the thigh, then cover it, and do not give it any space to come as far as the hand. 
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes to the hand, cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no other remedy but the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut the whole foot; and if it goes up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or cauterizing the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one minister below the one lien, and another minister the other lien upwards, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two liens to a spatula wide, until the bone is uncovered; then cut or cauterize, and put on each side a piece of linen cloth, so that the cautery does not touch the healthy part, and comes to the patient another lesion and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you are working, cauterize the place carefully, or put some powders on it that restrain the flow; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a blackness that seemed burned by fire, and this corrosion first came in his heel of his foot, until it consumed the whole foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover his foot, and it was healed; and long after that the corrosion returned in his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things that are effective after the purification of the body, and it could not cease the corrosion; and he begged that I would cut off his hand, and I refused, because I had hope of treating the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he would die, because the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired of everything, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and it was healed; and I have recounted this story only for this reason, so that one can do otherwise if they need to. 
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess comes to a head and stays so long that it causes a great gathering of pus; then it ruptures and bursts, and the pus flows out like from a vessel; and the skin above is as fine as delicate cloth, and it does not reach the bone or the nerve, and such disease is called “boil,” and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it reaches the bone itself, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin of this is that you cut all around that skin, even when it is fine as cloth; and it does not heal because of its corruption. 
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you know that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not in perfect, and the skin is thick with flesh, so treat it with clysters as follows: look if the breast is large, and the bow which is in it is of foul odor, then clysterize with Egyptian medicine which is made thus: take a part [of] oil, and litharge, equally, and put the cure into a vessel over fire until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; and then take of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and restrain the opening; and let the medicine remain for II hours, then extract it by pressing; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the evil is removed; and at one time clysterize with water of ashes, when this medicine is not present, and that is that you take ashes from grapevine wood, and pour water upon them, then filter it, and clysterize, until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot suffer either the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then clysterize with water and honey or with a bit of ground litharge; or you clysterize with honey and sweet wine, for that honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine dries the flesh; and when you have done this, and you know that the breast is well cleansed, then clysterize with that which makes flesh grow in it, and that is that you take diaphinit plaster, and make it with rose oil and wine; or clysterize it with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treatments of the ointments; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the cannula of the clyster cannot enter it, then enlarge it with iron a bit, and put inside a tent of Egyptian ointment, or Basil ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then sew it and leave only the place where the clyster can enter, and if the opening that gives off odor is above, then cut or make the lower point where it is. 
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bow is in place, let nothing be put on it and if you can not cover the breast below as you want, then prepare it so that the bow goes to the lowest place that it is, because when the bow is in place, let nothing be put on it and if you can not cover the breast below as you want, then prepare it so that the bow goes easily down, and do not leave anything of the bow; and take strengthening medicines to put on the wound, and be above the linen drape covering the whole wound; then cut as forcefully in the spot of the breast a little wider than before, then put ointment beneath the other drape according to the quantity of the wound, and put it on the wound so that the bow aligns, and do not remove the larger drape except after many days once; and the one who is on the spot of the breast, often removes to remove the bow, and know what comes from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or indigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that goes on the wound, then know that the breasts are already healing, and approaching health; and then untie it in the morning, or the third day, and when you open the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.  
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast lies bowed undigested after many days, know that the breast does not heal well. 
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after a long time, if it does not make you despair of health, for the cure is approaching.  
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose healing of flesh in their wounds is slow, and those who do the opposite; and if a boiled indigestible thing goes from the chest after many days, know that the breasts do not heal well; and if the breasts take long to heal and are drawn out, then apply medicines drying moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as diaphinit ointment, because it contains much vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take diaphinit ointment, and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine equal in substance; then congeal it and use it; and the same thing made honey-cooked, when diaphinit ointment is not present, or take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them on the honey when it is over the fire; and then glue it onto the breast, and apply the one who has administered a long lance, and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour of rice and centaury; and use of simples or composites: grind them, and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has gone deep, and made an impression in the bone, or in the hard members, or in the limbs; so treat the cure of the fistula, as we have said before. 
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the angle 
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the hand, or the foot, or by chance in other places; and when it is neglected, and one does not take care of it, then it comes I to the abscess boils, and runs and bleeds so much that it runs to the root of the nail, and by chance it runs all of it; and the corrosion comes to the bone, so much that it comes painful, and the limb of the foot is wide, and the color is flushed. 
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary that you cut away all the superfluity which is remaining from the bone, then cauterize the wound afterward.  
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses against the flesh, and it begins to prick and become blue, then it is necessary that you put a little underneath the nail so that it does not touch the flesh, and put it up, and cut that flesh subtly and lightly, and put on the remaining flesh medicine burning and corrosive to remove all; then cure the wound until it is healed. 
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, so you cut it and treat it because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see that it should be corrupted, then you cut it in I like as it has been said before, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is broken, and thrust, and he feels great pain, so you must heal him first; then cut the angle of the spatula sharp by cutting across above, and guard that the cut does not come to the flesh which is below the angle because the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top which soothes. 
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the shoulder
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two joints that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is where it has bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and none of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us of the two. 
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any knot of the thigh does not move, and he who is born at the joint of the thigh, by chance moves; the size of the one who is fleshy is so light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a wide spatula. 
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is grievous to cure: so keep it from being cut.  
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or must at the back of our, it is fitting that you cut first the flesh roundabout until the bone, then cut the bone to a suitable length for him, then cure it until it is healed.  
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The blows that come to two joined together come by birth, or by binding of a wound, or by burn of fire, or by similar things.  
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If it is necessary that you join that suture, so that the parts return according to their natural forms; then put between two tents or cloths moistened in rose oil, so that they do not stick together; or you put between two pieces of subtle plank, as long as the joints are joined, as it is fitting. 
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If it happens to come together with the palm of any of its hands, bind that suture as is fitting. 
des vils	of villages 
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are thick envelopes full of melancholic superfluities, that come in more members of the body; and more happen in legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry, than to others.  
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to him once purging of col, and then the health of the basilica. 
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two ways: one is to cut them, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open the vein, and treat it entirely. 
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The waist is thus treated in this manner: first arise the leg with hot water very strong, until the groin is softened, then strain the leg of the patient from above the hip to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide incision; and suck out and pull forth the black blood from one end to the other, as much as the strength of the patient can bear; and then dress it, and command him to stay with meat abstaining from black coles; and repeat the evacuation and salving when the veins are full, and hurt the patient. 
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the leg is according to this manner: place the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in the bath, and raise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut above the vein from the long one at the top of the knee, or in the part below to the ankle; then open the skin with the needle, and scrape the vein on each side, until it appears when felt; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters into the skin, it seems like a white cord; then put the point below, until it is raised from the skin, and then put it to the needle lightly, then cut it in another place above three fingers; then scrape the skin above the vein until it appears, then lift it to the root, as you did, and put it to another needle, as you did first; then cut another size, or more if you have need, then lift it, and cut at the bottom of the foot, then pull and lift until the second size; then extract from size to size, until it is all pulled out, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, put a needle with very strong double thread, and tie it and pull it, and put it below the point, and turn your hand on one side and the other, until it comes out; and keep it from cutting, for if it cuts, one cannot pull nor lift it, and it brings great annoyance to the patient; and when you have treated it entirely, put wool moistened in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and cure it until it is healed. 
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it twisted, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before. 
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which one cauterizes is curved, and does not cut, so that it only sears the vein; and it is of great curvature, for if it were fine, it would pierce the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form: 
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein 
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in legs, in warm places where no herbs or trees are born, and in soil that has no moisture; and by chance it is born elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the rot that comes under the skin, as it comes from inside the body serpents and worms, enclosed between skin and flesh. 
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then it changes its color, and the vein begins to burst forth, as if a root of a plant. 
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.
