When the shoulder is dislocated, it is necessary that you wrap around one piece of wool from 3 to 4 inches long, and tie it, and leave the wool on the leg, and all times that there is a point at the end, wrap around the wool, and tie it; and if it is too long, cut a part, and wrap the remaining, and do not cut it at its root, until it is completely out; because if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh, and brings an abscess and rot there, and bad sickness; for this reason it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the top, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein when it is treated of 5 palms long, or of 10, and a certain man came to me once, whose vein was 10 palms long, and when you cut it, it puts the root out through, and pierces it to the bottom, so that everything comes out; and be empty the matter that is inside, and administer at the place medicines that prevent rot any day, then cure it as abscesses.  
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes at this vein main pains, and even when it opens in the joint of the foot, or foot, and there comes much pain, and from which it jumps pains; cure therefore as we have said before.  
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that are born between skin and flesh 
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This sickness is called in our land "ox disease," because it often happens to oxen, and is a small worm which is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body going up and down, and one feels it well at the end of limb in limb, as long as it reaches the skin where it goes, and leaps further; and is engendered from corruption of certain humors, such as come worms and serpents and filth and roundworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it goes up to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times. 
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see him being cured and treated, it can only be done when he is going: therefore, it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong linen band very tightly, then cut on top and treat the wound further, and if the worm enters deeply into the flesh, and you do not find it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrodes the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the eye, then restrain below him the eyebrow forming, then cut on top, and treat the wound further; and it is necessary for the patient to use purification of the body of medicines soluble for the harmful humors poured, and avoid meat causing putrefaction. 
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain which comes from windiness  
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This sickness is called in our land “vakirir,” and is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those that I tell you. 
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as a worm towards the shoulder, faster than anything, as if living silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and went into the shoulder, and then shortly after it spread throughout the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that she was turning back around her body, as I saw her. 
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly how she moved thus from limb to limb, for I never had seen this illness in this manner. 
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I have seen many who well wanted to move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it so, as I saw it in the woman; and I thought that it was for this reason that the woman had dry body, and veins uncovered, and for this appeared that constraint of windiness; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who are delicious, and who have moist bodies and covered veins. 
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then lie above and below carefully, and then cut above as much as that windiness constrained in its place is; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure by those who remove windinesses, such as fetid pills, and seraphim pills, and similar others. 
des saiettes	of arrows 
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places of the body where they strike. 
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them is that there are some which have large points, and small, and hairy, and soldered; and those which have II angles, and those which have tongues, and those where there are pieces; and the one which falls in any limb so it falls according to II manners: or in a principal member such as brain, heart, liver, stomach, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members. 
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death, that I will tell you later, appear to you: then it is fitting that you desist from the extraction of this arrow, for death comes afterward in many dispositions; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not yet deeply embedded, then treat it, and cure the wound. 
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and jumps the soft tissue that is on the brain, is when it is dark, and hard, and twisted, and red in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and mixing of understanding, and vomiting of phlegm; and perhaps without blood from the nostrils, or ears; and perhaps loses the speech and voice; and jumps out of the wound white moisture seeming to poultice, and jumps also like burned flesh; and if this sign appears to you, hold yourself back from treatment, and treat the arrow if it is not inside. 
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the seventh when it falls or heart, are that she is near the left breast, and feels as if it were tied in something hard, not empty; and by chance the seventh moves also like the arm, and in short black blood, and comes coldness and sweat cold, and syncope: know then without doubt that death is coming. 
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that does not come out is that without plains of foam jumping from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and sighs high and seeks the cold air.  
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the covering of the hip, it is near the ribs; and throws great pain and great sorrow and sighing; and moves all the members of the shoulders.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls or stomach, perchance it leaps from the wound any thing of the undigested flesh. 
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls into the belly, and in a no point of fiber by the intestine route, then there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow. 
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine flows out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal. 
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the arms and necks and throat and shoulder and helper and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs, and similar members, are safe according to more dispositions. 
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you that it happened to me, for that you may do otherwise. 
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man with an arrow that lodged in the root of his nose: I touched it, and pulled it out from the other side under the ear fat, and it was healed without feeling at all. 
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And in the course of one game a javelin fell into the fat of the eye under the paper, and the javelin was returned, and he could only touch the tip towards the shaft, and the javelin was as large as a Turkish bow, with all the iron light without ears; the player was safe, and did not suffer any bad accidents.  
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I treated an arrow in the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I removed the barbs, and carefully extracted it as much as I could, and the Christian was healed. 
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And treated an arrow in a man who had it in his chest or belly, and thought he would die; and then after thirty days had passed, it did not change its position; I cut above the arrow, and tightened it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.  
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man who has an arrow in his back or side, and the wound is closed on top; and the arrow remains inside him, and does not change its natural position, nor finds annoyance in any of its natural works. 
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And behold another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn shut; and he remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar things. 
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And treated an arrow in the man of the princes the king, that it was stuck in mid his knee, and was slightly declining to the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded I was called to the cure after those three days. 
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow. 
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I touched her with a whole subtle tent, and felt nothing; and she felt a pricking and pain behind her right ear. 
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow 
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the splint on his hand for a few days, and sutured the wound directly, and kept the patient like that for a long time until he felt the arrow one day inside his joint; and he told me this. 
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the wound medicine corrosive and sharp for many days, until it was open, and I touched it, and felt the head of the arrow that was hardening in place; then I adjusted in the opening of the wound with that medicine corrosive, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly to me; and it remained well for IIII months, and then expanded so much the wound that I put pliers on it, and squeezed it on one side and the other, and it could not come out; therefore I did not cease to be subtle and to devise ways of instruments, until I took I day the pliers well made, according to those which its form will come in the end of this chapter, as long as I treated it, and restored the wound. 
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I therefore restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient became completely healthy.  
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on those things that I do not say, for the books cannot comprehend all; but the wise masters compare well with a small thing, and with what is present and failing, find new work, and new instruments, at the descent of strange things which happen in this art.  
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are not from the limbs where they are fixed except according to II manners: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and the one that is because of the place where it enters, it's an arrow entering into the flesh, and there being none at all now. 
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump now, let it be left until the root is carried outside, and let the opening be calmed; and also if it is fixed in the bone, and it cannot come out, let it be left for several days, and move it each day; and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around to all I forest subtle, as long as the root around is enlarged, and then treat it. 
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have said appear to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it there until it is healed after a few days, for if the arrow comes to this place, it is death. 
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only lodged in the bone and does not come up to the surface, and the patient remains for some days without ill effect, then the instrument of extraction. 
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very tightly packed this way and cannot be moved further, then administer poultices around it, as I have told you; then care for the area until it is healed.  
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is put back in its place in the body and it cannot be seen, then seek it with all your efforts; and if you feel it, treat it with any suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then cut as long as the wound is large; and treat the arrow if you can, and if it has ears in the arrow with which it holds on, then remove the flesh that is stuck from the two parts until you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can extract it; and take care that you do not break the arrow, so that you may draw it more easily. 
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, then let him lay until his leg is soft, then treat it, because the extraction is painful.  
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the flow of blood makes it contrary, then administer those that we have said about the cure in his chapter; and guard against the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put everything as well as you can draw out the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form that he was when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help that it be, and if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you.  
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, where one sees or feels nothing of it, or the skin is swollen in place if it can be seen or felt: cut then, as far as the forceps can take hold, and then extract it; if it jumps now. 
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held within the bone, then turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then treat it. 
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be pulled out, leave it still, and then begin the extraction again until it comes out; and if the shaft is in it, thrust it out completely; and if the shaft has fallen, and you see to administer a thrust, administer the instrument with its point entering the handle of the instrument; and then thrust, and if the arrow is capped, thrust the instrument back with its point entering within, in order to facilitate the extraction. 
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the wound is surrounded, then it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as it is proper.  
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or weight or to the belly or to the bladder or to the ribs, and it is close, and you can cover it up, then cover it; and guard yourself from covering the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then stitch the wound, if necessary is; and cure until it is healed.  
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of pliers used to treat arrows resembles an eye's beak, and see here the shape: 
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.  
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the pointed arrow is like the feather of a bird, to put at the tip of the shaft, as this is the shape: 
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape of the pliers to push and to know if it is here. 
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the body common 
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one is cured, of which sixteen are at the head, that is to say: two veins that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries that are in the two temples appearing; and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and the two veins that are on the collarbone; and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue. 
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins by which one commonly heals are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilica, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilica is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is on the bone, and it is the one by which one heals, which opens manifestly above the pouch. 
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the ring finger and the little finger, and it has two [veins]; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: the first one is below the curve of the pouch of the left side, and the second is superficial which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "saphenous", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.  
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears so helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the quality of the bloodletting, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in their two places depending on the head: then put your hand there, and where you feel the pulse below your hip, so prick it; then take the lancet, and push it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all over the vein above, and cut through both the skin and the vein well two fingers deep, and make blood flow out as much as you see; then tighten it and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book. 
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bloodletting of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is good for old migraine, and sore, and customary blepharitis, and to the body of the tears sharp to the eyes; and the qualities of the bleeding si est as I say: and is that the patient strains his neck, until the two veins appear openly; and feel the pulses below your right, and then he rules by enche; then lift the heart above the vein on your right index, and put the lancet under, and lift the vein up, and the cup, as you have done in the other two veins, and do correction of blood according to your need; then untie the patient, and put your right over the vein for an hour, then put cotton on top; and then the lie is formed, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them and their cup and their extraction, how the beginning of the book. 
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The vein of the forehead is as valuable as the cephalic vein for old facial ailments, and for migraine, and for redness; and its quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "digger", whose form is: 
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and hold firm with your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then bind the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and never once open it with a wide flame. 
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not proper that the flames be too large; and the healthy from the side, because the bone is near, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle. 
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The vein of the two veins that are in the two tear ducts helps the eyes, and to the nose, and to the ear, and to the inside of the eye, and to diseases of the face; and the qualities of their blood is that the patient straitens his neck by twisting with any linen, as before; then the vein is pricked, and be it the vein of traversal, a little prick of the long or flame a little wide, because there is no flesh. 
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perchance it breaks; then make a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then tie it up with cloth, and tie it well. 
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood from the vein of the nose is worth for fever, and for sore throat, and for diseases of the face, such as migraine and rubor that comes in the face, and even when it is old; and the qualities of the blood are that the patient tightens his neck, then strains his nose to your left hand, and takes a fine thin flame, and inserts it into the space which is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to come; and do not go too far in depth, and make a correction of blood according to your need, then bind it for one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:  
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bloodletting of the two veins helps in the treatment of ailments, and the beginning of measles, and many diseases, and leprosy, and corrosions, and herpes, and boils; and the qualities of the bloodletting are that the patient strains his neck under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master stand above the head of the patient, and the patient sit on the seat, then bleed the vein on the long one a little wide, then drain the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then make another incision in the other vein, then untie the linen, and restrain both veins moderately, that the patient does not strangle; and let him rest until morning, that the wound be healed. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the veins of the books 
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins above the lips helps in healing wounds inside the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and to sores and inflammation.  
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are to make the patient sit in front of you, and restrain his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by those that are black, and by those that around them have small black veins: cut therefore both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and also make of the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner. 
de la sainie desoz la lengue	from the vein under the tongue 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bloodletting of the veins that are below the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic, and it is at the stricture of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the vein are that the patient sits between your hands before the sun, and he lifts the tongue, and looks below on each side a black vein: bleed then one and the other, and do not go too deep because below are the arteries.  
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the cut from which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways: either by pricking them all with a flame cutting very wide, or with a subtle olive tree as the trenchant cuts, and it is called "anel"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins. 
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame martin is very well known, and it is wide as you see. 
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And there is a need to open the prominent veins full of thick blood that is apparent, and which contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive flame.  
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtly pointed, and is for bleeding the veins subtly, where there is subtle yellow blood. 
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so helps in the illnesses that are below the throat and neck and chest and belly; and it behooves the physician that he wounds wisely and that he withdraw from the artery which is below. 
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it cuts the ground, and blood flow comes, then it is necessary to stitch it up, as I have said; and it must not be a prickling flame, but cutting like an anvil. 
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, then it is necessary that you restrain it, and change another; or you want any vein of it, or you heal in its place the vein removing from the arm: it opens manifestly; and the cope to the flame anesil, as we have said. 
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you see to know the place of the vein, then so it is necessary that you extract the arm, that you touch the place until you know the pulse; then mark the place with an incision, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein of the flame's vessel; and guard that you do not wound the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is of the artery: avoid therefore.  
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it protrude upward like the urine of a child, and the skin is red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: hasten therefore, and place your hand lengthwise on it, then remove your hand if the bleeding stops; if the wound is in his arm, bind it up and leave it so, and do not move it. Let him be fearful, and do not move it until it is healed. 
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the vein is not cleansed and it bleeds, and the medicine is not present, then close the artery if it opens, because the head of the retraction; and cleanse the wound. 
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a rind of fig, and cut it, and take one half and tie it well until the other day; if it does not ache, it is good; if not, cure it, as we have said, with powders that staunch blood; and the styptics are not grieves in more dispositions for the small wound site, and the tension of the arm's band. 
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle helps that it treats blood from the top and bottom of the body because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the vein to lay itself near the nerve that is below, and if it isn't too much in sight, and it finds the nerve, and it swells and the saints be grieved, and by chance it cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it doesn't open in any man for its subtlety, then it behoves you to feel its instrument anesil; and avoid the nerve at your power. 
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if he has a vein between the two nerves, then make it long. 
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps because it draws blood from the head, and it helps the eyes; and you should bleed by pricking it with the olive flame or the myrtle flame, because that is the safest of all veins, because it does not have nerves or arteries. 
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest place, and it does not harm if it must be done the first time, and one begins again; and by chance swells the joints in some men, when one tries the first time, but it does not harm. 
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts. 
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing that you must know about bleeding, is that bloodletting is only administered to keep health, and to avoid future diseases; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins that are or cut: namely, cephalic, femoral, and basilica; and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent on Monday, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two hours or three days.  
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bloodletting which is administered to the sick has no set time, but when need is of day or of night, at all hours and at all times; and it does not behoove to bleed children until XIV years, nor woman carrying fruit from the fourth month until the seventh. 
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not bleed those who have passed sixty years old. 
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when some one wants to bleed, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that he purge the intestines with a light clyster, if he has much filth retained, so that the veins do not attract the superfluities harmful to the principal members; nor should anyone who is too full of meats be bled, nor who is drunk, as long as it is in him, nor dropsy; and worse to bleed after colic passion, and vomiting, and diarrhea, and multiplication of labor in a woman, and childbirth, of vigil and fasting, and that which all virtue, or by thing of the arm or of the body; then subtilize the humors, if his blood is thick, by meats and by drinks and by medicines, if you have the power; then enter into a bath, if nothing hinders you, to subtilize the blood, and bleed from the vein of the wrist, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, and from pain, and from lust, and similar things; and be quiet and joyful, and let the one bleeding be higher than the one who is bled, and rub his arm two or three times, then restrain the linen above halfway, because when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the place with your hands until the veins swell, and you feel them; then moisten the bleeding person's flame with a little bit of old oil, then put his finger of his left hand over that vein below the wrist one measure where he wants to bleed, so that the vein does not fail and break when it is pierced. 
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that are as thick as cords in the body, and some that are filled with wind, so that when one puts fire upon them, they recoil from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus it is with these; and if one works on the vein, the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary for the surgeons to be wary of these things. 
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; if not, start again a little below that same place where it was last attempted, if the wound is not swollen. 
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient fears, let him leave it for a day or two, and not bind his arm: by chance there may come boils; nor enter into a bath, then restart the bleeding if he pleases; and if the wound is small, or the vein is subtle and you doubt that it is not as much blood as you see, pierce in that same opening directly to the whole flame; and work a little gently, so that the limb is swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small. 
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place inflamed, do not begin the vein again, and put a little bit of oil on it, because it stops the blood from flowing to the body, and is mixed with this place the oil; and so administer the oil on each vein that you open the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing triacle and blister of those, when one puts it on the place; so subtle the blood and severs when it is too large. 
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, even when it has only been drained once, and the opening of the vein is small, you must hurry, and put on the place a sponge soaked in water and seal one hot, and restrain for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the discharge of blood from the vein, and if it remains in its place after some days no blackness or greenness, then it does not harm him; and if you see, put on anything of aloes or frankincense mixed with juice of calamine, monument stone, or similar.  
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and appearance occur at the saint's basilica: therefore put your hand upon it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, then that appearance is evil. 
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put on any of the things that we have said, because by chance it could be lacking in the artery; but make it a dry plaster to harden the place, then cure it with another cure, until it is healed. 
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood. 
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it ooze out until it is red; and if you see it swollen, let it be reduced until it is subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool. 
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for him who is strong and robust, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound for him, and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed him little and often, and one must bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding through a long or wide incision.  
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to him whose body needs to be bled, it is necessary to give moist bread in pomegranate juice; if it is warm, treat the blood three or four times. And if he is of a cold constitution, put moistened bread in front of the bleeding with honey syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-scented syrup. 
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it bleeds at the vein, after the issue of much blood, then it is necessary that he moisten broth of flesh, and fragrant syrup subtle, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of fainting, for the evacuation of the vein. 
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to drain his arm, and bleed another time, if it is necessary, when he is weakened by much bleeding, that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously. 
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to empty his arm after the first vein is opened, and he has a strong body, so it will heal seven hours after the first opening, or after the ninth hour.  
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed from another side, he must bleed on the second day or the third. 
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	Because there is much blood within the body that is already exhausted, and it brings fever; so it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the puncture until it flows in small streams; then when you have rewarded all the conditions of health, and place your hand on his pulse when he is healthy, so that death does not come in place of the stream, and this happens many times, when the healer is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see to untie his arm, and make blood flow a second time, and the puncture is closed, that you press strongly; but if it is curved, that he extends his arm as much as possible, because it would be bad; but let him rest until he heals for the second time; or you point at the tip of the flame, as long as the blood that is frozen to the vein's puncture has flowed out, and put on top a piece of silk placed in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not constrict it, until the abscess is appeased. 
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity is to draw blood a second time, if the vein in that same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm. 
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is bled in the place of the vein of the head because it is composed. 
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of bloodletting is that the patient puts their hand in hot water until the bone is red. Then it should be bound moderately so that the vein appears well, then let blood now through its center, not wide nor long; and let the wound be large, and let bloodletting be done near the joint of the hand, and if one cannot draw it out, put the hand back in hot water, and leave the blood in the water until you have enough. And if this is in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is put in more in winter than in summer; and the bloodletting of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve. 
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The vein of the savior of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: restrain the hand, and plunge it in hot water, until the vein is inflamed, if one sees it; and if the vein is out of place, and if you cut it completely through, it does not harm anything; and do not go too deep into it, for the nerves are below all skinless, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the wound is frozen in the wound, and it cannot leave.  
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put on the vein oil and wool to close it tightly, and do this with each one. 
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The vein of him in the left hand is as good for the disease of the mouse, and do all as I have told you towards the right. 
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the sophene is good for all illnesses that are below the body, such as diseases of the belly, and retention of flowers, and illness of the hips, and thighs and old legs, and similar illnesses. 
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of his wound are that the patient plunges his foot into hot water, and rubs on the vein until it aches, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot go many veins; heal then either a wider vein, or at the ankle, which is better.  
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you are healing it on the foot, guard the nerves that are underneath, and heal it by passing through as in cutting; and let the flames be gentle. 
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the vein cannot be issued forth, put the foot in water again, and let it bleed well. 
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the veins need to be opened the first time, it is restarted a second time above a bit, because the places are salted; do not doubt the nerves, as we have said, and thus make of the sophene of the other foot equally.  
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The veins of the sciatic nerve are at the ankle of the leg, and its pain reaches to the hip when it is hot with blood.  
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the qualities of his vein are that the patient enters into hot water, and is strained above the ankle IV by twisting, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, you seize the vein in all the ways that you can, and across; and better to let it bleed than to cut it, because the wound is dry, and it is much redrawn by hand. 
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, look for any pain in the hip or back of the foot, and towards the small toe, and guard the nerves; and make as much bloodletting as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put cotton on top and bind it; she is now healed. 
des sainies de ventouse	of the suction cups  
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suctions are made of horns, or metal, or glass; and suction is done in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.  
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventilation which is felt by fire is according to II manners: or it is with all fire, or without fire; and ventilation which is done by striking and by the extraction of blood is done in XIV parts of the body, so that one is entirely in the head; and the other is in the neck; and II others in II ribs of the neck; and the ventouse below the chin; and the ventouse on the II shoulders; and the ventouse above the hips; and the ventouses between the II arms; and the ventouses of the II legs; and the ventouses of the II ankles; and ventilation does not deal with blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not weaken one as much as one does from bloodletting of a vein; and it is not necessary that it should be administered, neither with all fire nor without fire, in any disease which comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied. 
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of diseases it is necessary to bleed, or by customs, let us administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in each time; for there are those who, when they have need to bleed, have a heavy head; and some who feel fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who feel a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen tongue, and spit out blood; and there are those who dream, and see by their blood and navels and death and similar things.  
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and even when it is gone for one month, we order them to vomit after three hours of the day.  
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The vein of the temple helps in the great pain of the head ... that comes to the eyes, and it is not fitting that this be done after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the cephalic vein, and it is not fitting for those who are of a cold complexion to use it, or who have catarrh, because this does much harm to them; and therefore it is not fitting for the elderly to use it, nor those who have or chief colds maladies.  
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured of it often become oblivious, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little lower down due to the doubt of oblivion.  
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The collimation of the wind removes the blood from the neck of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is good for the tightness of the belly, and for the cutting of the channel of the armpit, and all, and for repletion; and it is necessary to do little, because if it holds too tightly, it creates obstruction in the stomach and in the heart.  
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, and obtalmie and emigrainne, and a l’estranglement, and a la dolor as racines des dens, and est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; and covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, and ne veigne decorremens de sanc. 
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The ventilations under the chin are good for mouth disease, and for gum rot, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of the wounds of the two lips. 
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders is good for illnesses that come from heat and fullness.  
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The vein openings are as valuable as three veins in the arm, because they draw blood from those large veins; and instruct the patient not to prick them too much, because their skin is thin and near nerves and arteries. 
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The leech cup placed on the rump is good for hemorrhoids from the foundation, and for diseases below, and it should be large, and made of metal, because it needs to suck well; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and then it makes great wounds. 
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs are used quite openly because they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the hips, and knees, and bladder, and loosen up tumors; and are placed on the two shins, and the two ankles, but nonetheless, they weaken the body after prolonged use, and bring weakness in many conditions. 
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of placing the suction cup is that you place it first empty, and gently, and place it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease from doing so, until you see the skin red and inflamed, and appears the redness of blood; then apply firm pressure, and replace the suction cups, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are some who have fat flesh, and thin skin: therefore it is fitting to strike only once, and it is fitting to make wide wounds, and a deep poke; and suck gently.  
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is thick, it is necessary to strike it twice: the first time to subtly open the way of the thick blood. 
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very thick, it is necessary to prick it a third time; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, we only pierce it once. 
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish much blood, so often let us restart it; and if the vein is thin, then make it thicker with a fire (cautery), and the end is that the veins are pricked strongly, and it is necessary for one who has thick and hard skin, and who has rough pores, that you oil their leeches from the oil of appetizer and dissolvent: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or almond oil, or seed oil of gourd; and if it is in winter, of cress oil, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
