Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are large and cold, then take oil of wormwood, or of balm, or of anise, and similar things. 
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one whom one heals has tender flesh and large pores, there is no need to put any oil on it, but it should be washed after the inflation of rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar. 
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture, let him rise from ash, or myrtle water, and sumacs, and similar things. 
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or from water of the boil, or from decoction of anise or chamomile, or similar things; and it is not suitable to bleed with a cupping glass before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath one hour or II; and do not sleep after the cupping, and it is necessary that he should dress himself when he must be cupped and when he is cupped.  
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are healthy and have the temperament of choleric people; if their food is too dry and inflamed; then it befits them to eat cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce at meals, and similar things; and young pigeons, and roasted meat, and moist meats. 
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, should drink syrup of honey, and fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and quince, and plums, and small onions and pigeons; and the day that he will fast, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men once triacle or musk before fasting, or after, to comfort the principal members; and let it be subtle, but it is not necessary that those who are hot drink it. 
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are put without hurting are those that are put on the liver and the lungs and gout and on the belly and the back and the hips and the groin, because those members do not suffer well to be hurt on their own, and one does it only to attract blood from member to member, as we put on the breasts when the milk comes in; to remove the viscosity that is in the limb, as we put suction cups on the belly and on the back to lessen the limb; and to remove the pain, when there is an obstruction or a stone, as it removes by its attractive virtue perhaps the obstruction, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus does it when one puts it on the liver and the lungs when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty to suck only so much; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of warm water, as in diseases of pleurisy, and in that manner one fills the suction cup with hot water alone, or with water in which herbs suitable for it have been cooked. 
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup administered with fire is here:  
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two of wide and half a palm in length, and has or cost on the middle of its small opening, as for putting a needle, and be of iron, so that before she doesn't burn the patient when put upon the member; and has in the middle a rod across of iron or steel, to put a candle embraced, and be both great and small according to the illnesses and the age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are other than those of the old, and of the thin than the fat. 
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must thus put this suction cup on the limb: grasp the candle of wax or the linen cloth, and put it inside the suction cup through the rod which is inside the suction cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and the place must be on the wound as we have said, so that when one wants, one can go into the vapor, and one removes the suction cup; and grasp the linen cloth as before, and begin again often, if you have need. 
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup therefore which is administered in disease of pleurisy, to all acute, it has no rod nor point, and is not administered further than when it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb only so much. And this is the form:  
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leech are not applied except to members where it is not possible to put leeches because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar ones; and in the exposed flesh, such as the thigh or calves, and others; and the qualities of the user are that when you find leeches that are in clear sweet water without dirt, take them; and put them in a nut in fresh water until they are plump, and have nothing in their bellies; and then cleanse the member with bloodletting and leeching, then rub the member as much as it is red, and put the leeches on top; and when they will be full, and fall off, if it is the place where one can put a leech, put one there, because it does good afterwards. 
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this is not the case, lift the wound of ash, and then with water, well, and then bind it; and if the wound hurts too much after the body of the wounds, then moisten I the cloth of linen in cold water, and put on top, as long as the pain is extended; and if the pain is multiplied, then put on crushed vitriol, or galls, and similar things, as long as it is extended; or you put on the wound half of peeled beans, and let them dry on the wound, so will it stop now; and if you need more from this, then take other wounds. 
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the sutures do not want to be taken, then rub the place with fresh blood, or you put a needle there until the suture comes out, and then you put them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will flare up; and when you see that they are receding, sprinkle on a little bit of aloe and wheat bran, or ashes, they will now stick.  
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures 
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and dislocation.  
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know this, dear son, that the fool look at it from this chapter, that they never saw in any of the ancient books, nor read a letter; and for this reason is estranged the science in our land, because I have never found one good; and know nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, where I studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life; and I have you have described in this chapter what is contained, and have shortened it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of instruments that are used, as I have done in these II chapters before. 
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the sages put their understanding, and remain on the truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and learn it to others. 
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or torsion or sprain comes to anyone, it is necessary that you hasten to heal the patient on one side and the other, if any thing does not help him, such as weakness of body, or child, or old man; or if his heat is not very warm, or too cold; and avoid cold things, namely cold meats, and flesh of sheep and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meat which fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt of a hot abscess, or expansion of matter in the limb; so that the patient returns to his first governance that he has used. 
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make a thick nourishment, or there is viscosity, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and testes, and pies, and belly of calf, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with such nourishment they recover strength and the fracture heals more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the bones broken of the old and the decrepit do not well regain nor solder according to their nature because of the dryness of the members, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of little children; but nevertheless, care, reset the broken bone on the thick tendons which hold it together and join the limb together, so that it enforces like it was before; and not at all point of its work, and for this you should nourish them with large meats, as we have said.  
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the leg or hip, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes into a groove, and another in sharpening, like the edge of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if with fracture and wound, and fracture to a small crack all around.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in every manner it has its engine and its proper instrument in the restoration, according to what the remembrance comes in its place; and is known the fracture of the bone by that which its parts are twisted, and well open by outward, and feels at the pressure of the hand; and when there is no tortuosity nor feeling upon touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, if there is no point of fracture; but it can well have tortuosity, or fissure, or small fracture. 
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you must not move it by hand, but put on the medicines that come after here, and then restrain it subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And knows that the fracture that goes in arch, and are the II parts disjointed, it is necessary now to put them to point equally, so that abscesses may come; and if abscesses chaulz come, let him leave any day, as long as the abscesses be appeased; then put it equally to the move that you can lightly and wisely, and knows that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration of this one where it has pieces; then restrain, as it is necessary after. 
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is of two parts, whether it be hands or feet, or to your hand if it is a small limb, or to two tendons, or to one tendon and to your hand; and put the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you reset with all means the additions in their places as much as you can, and keep that through your work no lesion or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms. 
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels it well by the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if he arranges it well and does not restrain it too much, nor press as those do who bring it by their work abscess hot and contraction to the limb, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, carefully instruct the patient that he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other manner; and watch well that the limb is so secure that he feels no pain. 
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, except at a point, and it is necessary to put it in such a position that he feels no pain; and guard yourself that it be placed straightly, so that tortuosity does not come into it when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you. 
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are diverse in smallness and in greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones; it is necessary to wrap them in soft and fine linen cloths; and those which are large, such as the hips and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages embrace the whole large limb, and restrain it from all sides evenly, so that there is no gap; then tie lighter bandages, III tours or IIII according to the limb, and tighten your hand a little on the whole bandage, then go to the top of the fracture and tighten less, than the fracture thus distances a little the fracture; and soften the bandage little by little, until you reach a large part of its healthy place, then take the other bandage, and turn it back straight up onto the fractured place; then return to the bottom of the fracture, and tighten moderately, neither too hard nor too loosely, as we have said in the first section above; then put between the bandages linen or cloths, until they are all equal, then tie everything together with a band, and then put your well-made dressings on top, if there is no abscess or inflammation.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is a swelling or abscess, put on it a soothing poultice for the abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it so for some days; then strain onto its stitches, and be half an inch wide and carefully sawed, or from wood with which they make lances, or palm branches, and be according to this figure: 
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but it is necessary that the splint that one puts upon the fracture be a little bigger and wider than the others; and also as long as it is convenient to the limb of smallness or greatness; then restrain on the splints as you have done at the first hour, then tie above a thread evenly, as in the first hour on the fracture; tighter is above, less; and it is necessary that the threads be medium, neither too thick nor too fine, and be of soft linen; for if the threads are thick, as I want works from fools who make their bandages with cords of twisted linen, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not behoove that there be between each splint less than two fingers' width of space. 
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is sore at the sites of the stitches after the tightening in their healthy parts, put under them poultices of linen, or wool felt, so that it does not become blistered.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will say its cure here after.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not behoove to straighten all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, it should not be put in splints for after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of abscess appearing; and here's the way of the ancient plasters to restore fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and that you take flour that holds at the walls of the mill, and confuse it with an abundance of egg, and put this confection, not too clear nor too thick, and in use, and that is the common manner of the plaster restoring the fracture to more dispositions, and also to women and to small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold. 
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of plaster restoring fracture and dislocation and torsion: take  three ounces of barberry, ladane, and rue, and asafetida, and gum arabic, ana .x.  oz.; myrrh and aloes, ana .v. oz.; alechil .viiij. oz.; and make it into powder, and mix it with the white of an egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to make a poultice that is good for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, ana X  ʒ; myrrh and aloes, ana VIIII ʒ; acacia VI ʒ; Armenian bole X ʒ, and grind well, and confit with water or the white of an egg, and administer. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another manner of emplastering joints and bones that are out of place, and appeases the pain occurring, and the size uses of the bone, and the fracture: take new linen, and moisten it in oil and boiled in hot water, and put it on the wound. 
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing a hot abscess, and removes pain properly.  
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of ointment that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another manner of emplastering for the restoration of a broken bone and to lessen the remainder of the abscess. 
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wormwood, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of verbena, one part each; and grind it, and boil it with wine, and if the limb is frozen, boil it with moist coriander water, or water, and apply it. 
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way of setting a bone more forcefully than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.  
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of eyebright, and seeds of flax, balm, melilot, and wormwood, and flowers of violets and camomile, each one part; and grind, and confit with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest. 
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ipocras says in his book that one should not put on the broken limb for restoration other than a certain one made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, and he says that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen one must put on the broken member, to restore, things dry and a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is good for the wound and pain: take mugwort and  chevolz of sheep decocted, or feathers of an owl, and vismalve, and equal parts of these, and grind them up, and make a poultice of it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care if the patient feels no pain, or if the bones have not moved from their place; if no pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry, and untie it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge of moist sea, and plunge in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry linen, moistened in water or rose oil, and tie it with a nut, until you are sure of a hot abscess; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and be removed the pain, then begin again the ligature subtle, and a little plaster, and do not bind it as tightly as before; and subtilize until it is healed. 
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red, and the pain and swelling are all gone, and you need emplastrum and binding, then begin it again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb any of what we have said, then do not release it except after III days or IIII or V or VII; and no time leave it XX days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and approaches the adjustment of the bone above; then restrain him more than before, and make his flesh grow thicker, as I said before; and if you see him drying out more than necessary, know that nursing cannot come there; arose then with hot water, all times that you release it, and this be each third day, and wash a little the wound; by this work then shortens the nursing of the limb, and amends immediately what do the foolish mire, who left the limb crooked: this is evil, and so is dangerous work, and I see no other thing than to leave and work directly. 
des diverses manieres de brisure	of diverse ways of breaking (bones)
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of fractures are, and diverse figures, and the causes are destined; for there are fractures that are made by percussion of sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the surface which is below the bone, as it is done with a hatchet or spindle; and for this reason this manner of fracture is called "haichure".  
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this kind of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an enmeshed percussion, or a split or of the bone's neck, or of the head on a bone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture penetrating, which approaches up to the skin that is below the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that is put back in the bone as subtly as a hair, and the fracture is small, and for this reason this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound that is made by striking with stone, or by falling, or by similar thing, and makes the piece of bone enter inward, and are the pieces like those of the blacksmith when they forge on the cauldrons; so between the stones within. 
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or head with wet bones, such as the heads of children; and it happens in all these manners of fracture that small pieces are dislodged from them such as stars; and I will speak of it in its place. 
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of fractures by retracting upon them, and by probing with probes, and by the corrupted flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The seeming capillary is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone, and rubs upon it, the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure of a fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of understanding, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and eyes becoming inflamed and red, and other similar things in more dispositions, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an escapable accident, and you hope for salvation, so commence the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fracture comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day as much as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue under the bone does not rot, and comes the accident that we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes up to the membrane that covers the brain, it is necessary that you split the broken part thus: and that you prick the head of the sick person deeply, and uncover over the bone in all the ways that you can, and on the figure of the wound more softly than you can, and if bleeding comes out when uncovering the bone, put an abscess poultice, if it helps as much as it is necessary, and fill the place with cloths moistened in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the poultice is calmed, and be assured of the stoppage of blood; then begin to remove around the bone, and this is done according to II ways of work: one manner is that you cut at the narrow cutting in front, and this is the form:  
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of diverse incisions, some narrow and others wide, and pointed, and made of iron; and in work lightly, so that you do not bruise the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and stiff, then it is necessary that you pierce it around, so that you administer splints with tarers, not so deeply that they go beyond the bone of the test, and it must have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and it behooves you to have more than one, so that each comes in its place from the thickness of the bone, so that you have tarers for all tests; and this is the form of the three kinds of tarers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one tarer on the bone, and turn to your two hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the tarer elsewhere a little after, and thus do all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the pertu, and make them more subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments that you have such as tongs, pliers; and guard that you do not touch the marrow nor the sifac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you will have the bone pierced and treated, it is necessary that you reset the apparatus which is removed from the bone to all other instruments seeming like a chisel, but it is necessary that it be more solid and more subtle than the other chisel; and if there remain nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, then lightly cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.  
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other manner of work is that which Galen says, which is drier; and the load very strong, and that is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture appears to move, so that when you have uncovered that part, then place under the head of this lentil-shaped incisional instrument, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and is the part acute in II sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly chop the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is below; if it is adhering to the bone, gently lift the bone, because we well know without pain, and without fear. 
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not reach the skin, and the bone is broken only from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to first apply this asperity, and remove the scales with a fine rasp which you must have in various quantities, to administer in each place the most suitable one, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you begin with coarse rasps, and afterwards with finer ones, and do not cease doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other capillary cuts and subtle fractures, it is necessary that you administer  cause according to its place; and this thing is not replied to by him who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the abscess is uncovered, then it behooves you to take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it upon the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and put it on top of the first cloth; and do this more lightly than you can, so that you do not burden the abscess, then administer by means of a bandage above, and do not bind it more forcefully than so long as it holds the wound alone; and let it remain thus for a day or two, until the swelling has subsided, then untie it, and administer medicines such as roots of lilies, and flour of chickpeas, and powder of frankincense, and aristolochia, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and put it on the wound, and administer further medicines mixed without mordant; and guard that the wound be always clean, that you do not leave any ointment there, nor let any boil gather, for when a boil gathers upon the brain’s cloth, it will corrupt and pus-fill, and bring great evils to the patient; for when one puts on the abscess something biting, it will blister upwards. 
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take ward then, if no bad accidents come to the patient, as we have said, so it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blackness does not come forth except for the medicine that has been placed upon it, which has virtue, then you should take a part of honey, and III parts of rose oil and glue one cloth, and place it on the syfac; then cure in manners of cures as it is necessary, until it is healed. 
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the lower jaw are broken, or one by the other alone, because they are two bones; and this one below is cartilaginous, and does not break unless forced to bend or twist, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it behooves you to put your little finger or point of the two, and place the breakage inside your index finger, and to the palm outside, until the bone returns according to its natural figure; and do this gently, and guard that the patient does not feel pain from your work. 
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the nose, and it cannot come to its place, then you should put it even on top of a rail a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the fracture is of two parts, make another splint, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess is calmed, then bind with linen bandages of ten layers, if the fracture is in one part. 
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you put one on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the sheets be so thick that they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they said any restorer one must moisten the tents in butter, and change each day. 
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem to me that this is good, but it is necessary that they be softened in the making of auburn of an egg, and of mill powder; then leave the tent, as long as the bone is hard, and the cartilages hardened.  
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes one puts goose feathers in their place, and so i.e., one sheet of drape around it, and it holds the blister, and blows the patient among; do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess comes to the new while you work on it, put cerote or cotton moistened in rose oil, or in i. p. of diaquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to it, put a plaster from outside, of sesame flour and incense powder, mixed with yolk of egg, then put light bandages on top, and do not bind them too tightly; and if the fracture of the bone is small and broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then sew together the break, and treat it with proper dressings of flesh and support, like plasters and ointments as appropriate; and if there is no wound inside the bones, treat it with tents and put splints inside them until it is healed. 
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken below, and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only outside, and is not broken in two, except for a bulge inside, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, that you put your left index finger in the mouth of the sick person; and if the fracture is on the left jawbone, put your right index finger, and push the fracture inside lightly, and make it with the other hand outside, and put it straight.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is broken in two, it is necessary that you administer an extension of two parts, until it is straight.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth happens, or breakage, so restrain with a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place upon the broken jaw carefully, and place one double cloth; and place upon the cloth a great star well made, or a piece of leather equal, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up on the as much as you can, and command the patient that he rests himself, and eats light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, so untie it on the third day, and then re-apply what has changed; and place a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with plenty of egg or sesame flour, after that you have removed the cerote; and place a light cloth over the plaster, and if the plasters adheres, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward no piece of the bone is removed; so subtly of the removing with instruments suitable to that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you will have removed all these pieces, and there is none remaining, then cover the wound, if it is wide, and put upon it one plaster suitable to that, in order to hinder flesh, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fracture breaks many times in front, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three ways: or it is broken and severed in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is like this when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder that feels the broken bone; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put equal the fracture with your hands, so that the form is as it should be, and there is neither appearance nor misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, put under the shoulder of the patient a round sphere of cloth or wool, and be it large according to your necessity; and being and lightly raising the bone, and restraining the sphere with your hand, so that you put equal the fracture, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder with force because it comes back in place, then it is necessary that the patient lie prone on his arm and place below the shoulder 1 hour glass, and push the ministers' shoulder down until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two, and if you find it fragmented, it is necessary that you split further; and treat the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join by any elevation, so cut to one of the incisors that you have; but that you put under the shoulder this instrument, in order to guard the shaft:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and seems like a spoon, and is not too heavy, and be also wide as it is convenient, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have it two ends, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as is the rupture of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, so sew the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt hot abscess, so dress the wound with bandages and tents, according to its quantity. 
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes, then moisten one bandage in rose oil and in honey and in wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is without wounds and without incisions, is that you put upon the bone the plaster of the powder of the mill and of albumen of egg, and put light bandages above, and put a spear under the shoulder, if you have need; then take a very great bandage of one palm wide, then put I drapeil double above the bandages, and the plaster; then take a splint subtle of III fingers wide and long, and enwrap it around that bandaged one, so that the chief of the bandage be hanging; and put the splint upon the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the healthy shoulder, and under the diseased shoulder; and tighten each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the splint does not move above the broken bone, so you reward each day, and when the bandages loosen, so restrain it; and make the sick person lie upon his back, and put him when he sleeps the small cushion under the shoulder, to raise the shoulder upward; so will lighten the fracture of the forcele by the alleviation of the shoulder, or you tie his arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless evil accident comes to it, until XX days; then renew the plaster, if you see that he needs it, and restrain and leave it thus, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most at XXVIII days, and in less in some men. 
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens sometimes that the shoulder breaks or its length is misplaced, and one can only know it by touch; then prepare the apparatus according to the figure of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form in all the ways you can; then put on the place powder from the mill with an abundance of egg, and light bandages, and put above a double cloth; then put on a wide and subtle splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint is uneven in any place on the shoulder, then use that hair of linen bandages so that the splint be even; and then tighten it with a very strong bandage firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the joint every day; and whenever it softens, tighten it again, and put the splint back in place if it is out of place, and lay the patient on his side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25, and when this number is fulfilled, then untie it, and be sure because it is not bone that comes out easily.  
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of bone protrudes forward, and not below the joint, so do it above, and the bone, and do what we have said in the fracture of the collarbone to soothe the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture of the leg
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens little; but it often breaks at the end. 
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in its marrow, it sinks to the lower part, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of strength, and all things, and perhaps vomits blood, and opens the passages within the broken bone, and it smells quite bad. 
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies often on his back, and he puts 1 cushion between the shoulder blades, then presses the shoulder blades, and he assembles the ribs of the 2 ribs with your hands, and subtly does put it equal in all ways that you can, until the figure of the bone is as it ought; then puts above plasters and bandages above the subtle layer of salt, or another light husk, and enwraps it in 1 drape, and lays it on top of the broken bone, so that it doesn't move; and turn the bandage round to the back, and strain it well, and reward each hour the bond, and if it softens, then strain it; and if it comes to him to loosen, for corrosion or for itch that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, then hasten, and loose it, and wipe the plaster, and address what has come there by ways of cures; then put back the plaster, and strain it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breakage of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breakage of the ribs comes only in their thickest parts after the back, and at the head inside, and they bend only for that reason because they are brittle; and one feels it well at the examination of the two sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is that you set the fracture equal, as it is right. 
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put the splint on it, and restrain it with a stick, if you need it.  
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breakage of the ribs is leaning inwards, the patient feels very great pain, and sharpness, as well as from pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and besides pains, and coughing, and vomiting a large quantity of blood, and this is a serious illness, and the ancients have put much care into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say it is necessary to administer meats that swell the belly, to expel the wind outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, except for hot abscesses, if they have not yet come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, then treat it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of us say that one should put suction cups on the area to draw out fluids strongly, and this seems reasonable; nonetheless, there is doubt that the suction cup draws the superfluities to the area for the sake of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say any one of you should cover the place with a woolen cloth in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make equal the lying wound, then be cured of the plague of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot suffer because of the bone which points to the skin, and there is doubt for the patient, then it is necessary to cut above the place of the broken rib, and it is necessary to put under it an instrument to guard the sifac; and then one must trench the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with plasters, until it is healed. 
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, put on it soft cloths in rose oil, and put on top of it; and cure while the place of that which is necessary for the abscess, and lie flat lying on the ribs or where it should, until it is healed. 
de la brisure dou col	of the breaking of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes comes a break of bones of the neck, and sometimes it happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, then take note if you see his hands softened and swollen and dead, and he cannot move them nor extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, he feels nothing. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is mortal in many dispositions, and if they move and feel well when they are pulled and held still, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if one puts care to it. 
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if these similar things happen to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it is healthy or not, if you take care if the legs are soft, and if the accidents there are in hand, and on the back there is windiness and emission without will; and when one places it on its belly, there is emission without will.  
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is set on its back and he wants to sit up, he cannot. 
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is mortal: if it does not labor in its cure. 
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to him, then the thing is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward it if there is an abscess hot, so put on the spine rose oil or egg yolk of an egg, until it is appeased; then put on a comforting and drying plaster, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is broken, it is necessary to cover the wound; and remove the bone, then assemble the two edges of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment that promotes healing, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," put your thumb of your left hand in it, and place it equal to the other hand at your power, then put the plaster and splint on top, if you need it; then restrain it, and if there are bones that have been displaced, do this again, remove the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, it should not have been for a little weakening at the top; and making long, and declining to the sides, and coming to the patient pain in the place, and prickling, and swelling that breaks.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are on the fracture; and know which is the fracture and its figure; and if the fracture is at the top only, so put equal the fracture, as long as it is to a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inward, so make the patient lie on his belly, as long as the restoration of that fracture be apparent to you.
