Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have put it even, place it on the emplasters, then place a splint of wood or of horn, and restrain the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the plaster below the ribs, as long as the limb is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient that he sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears there, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and restrain it as appropriate, if there is no bad accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the fracture of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjuitor is that which is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take one staff of medium thickness, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of .two. strings together, and lift them up, and place the patient on one seat; then put his broken arm upon the staff, until it comes to the armpit, and has a curve of staff in the middle, then put upon any heavy thing or minister its extension down; then put the hands of the fracture equal together, as long as the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one supports the patient on his bed, and ties his hand to his neck, then commands two ministers that one holds what is above the fracture in their hands, and the other holds below at all .i. point, and extends each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too far, restrain the limb below the fracture and above the fracture, and extend each minister to its side.  
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the shoulder head, it is necessary that you put one linen in the middle under the armpit, and the other towards the outside, under the fracture; and also if the fracture is toward the outside, then it is necessary to put the bandage lightly, without labor, until the fracture is equal on the top, and on the outside; then set the fracture straight, as it is necessary, and restrain it, if an abscess does not come.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes to the place, do not constrain it until seven days, and put on linen moistened in oil of roses, as long as the abscess is appeased; then constrain it, and the manner of constraining it is that you put the bandage on the bruise, then assemble the arm upon the shoulder, and put your hand upon the shoulder or upon the breast; and put the cloth, and constrain upon the shoulder, and upon the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless anything prevents you, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moved, use splints, and put on the bruise a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint one digit of space, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the bruise three digits on each side; then constrain upon the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the bruise, more strongly and less widely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the stars, and the constriction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess hot, so leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days the bond, that itching or swelling comes not to the place, or the dressings cannot come to the limb because it is too strained.  
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said. 
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not dislocate him until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and have his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder one cushion full of wool evenly, and watch every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or become softer the ligaments; if it advances by the virtue of medicine, and give him the food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the first food is subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick. 
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be taken back in forty days from all; and therefore one must unbind it and administer baths and medicines of emollient for the place to heal.  
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is bad and obstructed, it remains for 1 day or 2 months to loosen.  
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of .ij. bones, which are called the two "fosciles", because one is small, and that is the one that follows the pouch; and the other is large, and that is the one that is below, towards the little joint; by chance breaks the large foscile alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are broken together. 
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then it should be gently extended and made even. 
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great hip bone, then it should be strained more strongly; and the patient lies upon the cushion, and hold the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the small toes lower than the other toes, and let the patient lie crossed upon himself, and the cushion before him higher, that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers' arms to the part below his hand, or at the groin, and one other minister on the other side above. 
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the mirrors equal, according to its best form. 
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the fracture there are pieces, put each one in its place, and if there is any detached that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then do as and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken of it in the singular chapter; so take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration sores abscesses appear, then glue the drapery of cerote made of rose oil and white wax so that it is not too hard nor too soft; and tie the drapery above subtly until the abscesses are appeased. 
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the surgeon removes the cerote, and he puts on the plaster of the powder of the mill with plenty of egg, then put the splints, and let the splint be on the outside more further, and one little bit wider than the others; and know that it must have VI splints or arms in more dispositions: whether the splint is in one of the bones, or in II; and restrain more above the splint than elsewhere, and every day less moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the splint be soft and moist, and not be hard nor rough; and let the thread, with which it is restrained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. 
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the limb and the ligament after some days. 
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is necessary that you raise the limb in hot water, until the itching is calmed; and let the limb not be allowed to rest at all.  
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again the tightening, and if the ligaments are loosened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, so the bandage. 
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it happens that the numbing cannot come to the limb, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you soften it a little, and leave it so for some days, until the numbness passes, and then restrain it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, do not loosen him until 20 days.  
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when it has twisted, then he puts his hands on his neck, and let his neck be equal, and guard against movement and agitation, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in XXX days or in XXXV, and perhaps in XX days, according to the compositions and the complexities of the virtues. 
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and on us there are few fractures, and it comes but rather often a sprain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, it befits that the patient sit cross-legged and be straight in front of him equally; then put his hand on the table outstretched, and extend the ministers the broken bones, and put them equal to the sides, so long as they are well joined; and put the plaster and the bandages, if an abscess does not come, then put a splint according to the quantity of the place; and be enveloped in one cloth of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the palm towards the belly of the hand, make a sphere of cloths, and command the patient that he grasp it to his broken palm; then strain it with a long cloth, and let the splint be of hard wood as large as the palm of the hand, and strain it, as it befits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is at the forearm, it is necessary that you put a splint on top, and another below in the palm, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie it tightly around the hand, and seal the linen between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of the bones of the arms, if it is the arm, put it straight as it should; and restrain it with the palm, and if you see fit, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture, and do not move it. And if the fracture is in another finger, such as the index or one of the others, put it straight, and tie it with the healthy finger that follows; or tie them all together in one band, which is better, or put on top a splint, like the pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the hot and dry abscess, and cure those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken hip
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the hip is often broken, and it is well seen when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is by one ligament above the fracture, and one below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister stretches his limb to his equal part; and this is when the fracture is committed into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the hip, so one of the ligaments towards the groin, and the other ligaments below the fracture. 
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And also if it is near the knee, and then be the ligaments close to the knee, and be the extension down; then put the hands on the bone equal with their two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put the splint, and the bandage, if an abscess does not come. 
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, then let it be calmed and then return to your work and your care; the ligation is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap on the fracture I with a hard bandage doubled in II or III, and keep the superfluities then turn the leg until the heels come to the root of the thigh, and put I long thread between the hip and the leg, below the knee, and make the head of the thread go above; then turn up the leg and up the hip the bandage, then put on the fracture splints, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the place VIII between the leg and the hip of cloths soft for to put equal tightness, then begin to tie firmly III turns or IIII on the fracture; and as you go higher above the fracture, and less tighten; then take as II heads of the thread that you have put between the leg and the hip, and in tie III splints that are above, then return down to the head of the thread, until you come near the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that it does not come an abscess or swelling nor any other kind. 
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, untie it, and address what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that catch, it is necessary to remove them, if one can; and if one cannot, it is necessary to split the place, and drain pus; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And no time is the hip broken in this way if one puts splints on it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration made this way, the patient does not complain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the fracture is healed in one day, or a little less or a little more, according to the varieties of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the rue of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the area of the knee there are few fractures, but it bends many times. 
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is no longer than a fissure, or opening, and it happens to all wounds, and without wounds, and this everyone feels well. 
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done this way: one puts it straight what is rounded to its sides, as much as it can be assembled before moving it; then one applies a splint, and puts a round staff over it, if you have need of it, and restrains it as is fitting; then restore all the arrangements that we have said in other fractures, such as hot poultice and similar things; put to each accident what is necessary for it, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called "tibia" and the other "fibula"; and all fractures come as it comes to the arm, and for that reason the restoration is like that of the arm equally, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in every direction. 
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is clearly seen; and it turns downward.  
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore administer extension and make it even, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is bad and there are many pieces, that the extension be less and lighter; and the splint according to your virtue.  
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of woolen cloth that support the leg on both sides, and be the length of the leg from the knee down; then wrap in two lengths one bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle also, and at this juncture, the leg cannot decline to the right or to the left, and thus is well; and none administer one stick along the leg, and if it is of wood, and put on the leg to ward off movement, and properly made one's in the fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident; so treat until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no fracture, but the bones of the foot come at any time fracture and to two places, and there is not there been other than that which causes in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there comes fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlap each other, put now the patient's foot on the ground, just as if he would walk, and then put your foot upon his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they return to their places; then put plaster and bandages above, and put under the belly of the foot a small board to two fingers wide, then restrain the foot well, then that you have enveloped bandages, and other things which you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four will have passed, undo the bandage, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the bones broken, restore them, as we have said about the bones of the hand; then put on the broken bone a splint according to the length of the bone, and be a little more wide, then put under the foot that table that I have said, and restrain it well; and if there are .ij. or .iij., or more, broken, put on each bone a splint according to its quantity, enveloped in one cloth of linen, and restrain the table under the foot; and let it be standing on the head of the table further from the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and support each accident as it is necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the woman's nature is broken, then make her sit enlarged, then incline her to the back part, and be held by behind; then fill the vagina of the patient with cotton, and put in as large as the stick; then turn the woman over, and lift her back little by little, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and returns the bone with the stick; and when she wants to urinate, take out the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and so do for VII days or more: thus will be restored the fracture, and if you see, take a sheep bladder, and tie a rope to its opening, and put the whole bladder into nature; then blow into the rope form, until the bladder is inflated inside: nature will return the fracture; then be filled with cotton, and leave it so for some days, until it is healed. 
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the arm of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the bone of the hip; and these fractures near are not hidden from him who puts his study and use to them, and understands my book. 
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture signifies in more positions the right way of restoration; therefore, listen. 
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the member, when it is broken, take a goose's throat and put it into the member; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until healed, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It behooves him who has a fracture with wound, even if it is great, like the bone of the hip or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healings that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, then let the restraint of vitriol remain, if you have nothing else, and then begin to restore the fracture in that same hour, or on that same day, if an abscess does not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess does come, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, as long as the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the uncovered heart, then it behooves you to put it in place gently with your hands, by small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not readily available to put it in place with your hands, then resort to this instrument which is of iron, which has .vij. or .viij. finger-lengths long, and the width according to the quantity of the wound; and for this, it is necessary for the one who makes it to engrave .iii. or iiij., according to what he needs in each cure of a fracture; and let it be round and a little thick so that it does not bend under compression on the member during your work, and let it be pointed at the front, and thicker from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palainche," for which it is necessary that the shoulder bone be placed on top of the apparent bone; and to push once, as long as it returns, and be equal one against the other.  
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then it is necessary that you cut the head of the bone, until the instruments have purchase. 
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone, as we have said, so cut it with a suitable instrument, either incisor or saw, to your power; then clean those which remain in the bone of roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. 
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is so that it is in its place, then moisten the drape with black styptic wine, and properly set it; and do not put on the wound any sort of ointment or anything else where there is oil, lest it cause rot and corruption; then administer splints when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cut the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and tell the patient well that the wound should not be strained with the fracture; and many times fools have done this, and have brought upon the patient either death or corruption at any time; and let the strapping be softer and more slack than other fractures. 
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it does not behoove to put on stars; but surround the area, in place of stars, with hard cloths, and tie them. 
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one day or two that the wound is bowing, remove what you have put on top and put healing ointment for wounds, such as ointment tetra-formation and similar things.  
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you untie the limb two times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is united and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in such a manner that the bone goes down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the next day, and it cannot unite anymore but returns back bone, know that there are small pieces of bone, so it is necessary that you cover the wound with a bandage, and remove all these loose pieces which bring that pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter before. 
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, like the bone of the hip or the shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, do not treat it, because many times death comes from it, but let it be until it decays; perhaps it will heal itself after XX days or XXX, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it. 
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the boils that come from the swelling
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the bruise, even when it is near the joint, and it is a bad thing to see the figure of the limb; and perhaps it cannot make the member its natural works.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take ward then if it is fresh: if it has administered medicines styptic, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, in such a way that you take any of these things, or all together, and you concoct them with styptic wine or with white of egg or with oil; and put it on the bruise in poultices, and restrain it well, and do not loosen it in the hands for days; and then unloosen it, and begin another one, until the swelling is gone; or you restrain it on a piece of plank that is well made; because the properties of the plank are such that it removes all the swellings from the limbs; and if the swelling is already converted into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut above it, and make the superfluity apparent; or you return it to any razor, until it is removed, and the cure until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is set, and afterward the limb remains weak and subtle, it happens for many reasons: one of which is because it was bound too tight, and not tied as it should; or because there were too many ligatures, and it cannot come to the nourishment of the member; or due to too much rubbing; or because of too great movements, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and to make the body tender, as long as the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths to him, and give him joy and leisure; then put poultices on the limb, so that the poultice draws to great nourishment, and the rub often with a wet cloth, until the nourishment comes to the member; and returns to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb after the healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the broken bones are open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: so do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb anew, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and this work is blamed, and comes great harm, and perhaps death; nevertheless, if the nodules and the torments are fresh, then it befits that they be raised with hot water, or softening herbs are cooked, such as leaves of marsh mallow, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and the one makes a softening poultice, such as diaquilon well made, and you take the vismalve fleece, and confit it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a poultice on top; or you take figs and grease them, and grind them with flaxseed, and similar medicines that lessen the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes dislocation is removed by rubbing continuously and lengthwise with wet hands. 
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And make the member move each hour.  
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is ingrained and hardened, as with stone, and need is to remove it with iron, then it befits to cut up to the bone, with a subtle incisor lightly; and put cussing and study into the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation is an exit from any joint from its place, for which it cannot move, and the limb is badly shaped, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, it should now be brought back without splinting.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, then the limb swells, and by chance if one sets it back to its place; for this reason it is not fitting that one moves it while it is swollen: many times brings pain and other pains; however, when this happens, make the patient bleed, then let him, until the abscesses are all calmed; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then reset it gently, and treat each member as you would bring the wound to its place.  
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters of dislocations of the head to the foot.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jawbones are dislocated and the dislocations of both are according to .ij. manners: or they are a little removed from their places, and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, and hang towards the cheek, and cut off saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by the many more dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, it behooves you to reset it carefully, and not grudge at all; and in such a manner that the ministers hold the head of the patient, and puts the tips of his thumbs into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are outside, to put them equal; and command the patient that he soften it, its jaws, and move them in all directions. 
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the finger puts it straight, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is brought back with pain, even if it is the two jaws together, then apply hot water and oil, as long as you gently reset them; do not be afraid to bring them back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient is well closed without softening, it puts on soft cloths in a cerote made of rose oil and wax, then ties it lightly with soft bandages; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders be between two cushions, so that he does not move them neither to the right nor to the left, nor does he try to open his mouth, but eat light food as long as the pains are gone, and the jaws are healed; and then chew what he wants lightly, and do not work at all to open his mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well healed and healthy.   
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be set back in an hour, and are not brought back to their places, then come fevers and accustomed swellings, and perhaps a solution of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of cold phlegm.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a deadly sign; and many times those who have it die within eight days.
de la forcelle	Of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate from within the side of the rib and from the hip, and it is dislocated no time at the outside, and well one feels it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back, and extends his arms; and then presses the place firmly with his palm, and it will return; then puts on the splint and bandage, and restrains it; and the head which is towards the outside cannot dislocate; if so, and if it dislocates any time, then reset it in its place, as we have said; then puts on the splint and bandage, and restrains it, and commands the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus likewise is restored the head of the shoulder, when it is dislocated from its place.  
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one of which is that it dislocates to the side of the hip; and the second is to the side of the breast; and sometimes it dislocates to the top part, which happens little; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and many times dislocated below towards the hip, especially to those who have little flesh, because on these it goes easily; to those who have enough flesh, it goes with difficulty, and enters with difficulty. 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men percussion or fracture, and swells the shoulder with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore it is necessary that you prove it, until you are certain; and then begin the cure.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocation when it is down towards the hip, and puts difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their variety manifest; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a hollow, and under the hip to touch the head of the shoulder, as if it were one bone; and the patient cannot bring back his hand to his hip, nor move from any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly at the touch; and this manner of dislocation is not much except to be brought back, when it is new, or when the child is sick. 
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift the hand of the sick person upwards, then put their thumbs under the armpit, and lift the joint with force upwards to its place; and the ministers lift the hand and extend it upwards, then put it downwards; so it will come back gradually.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in a few days after, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and administer emollient and soothing, such as decoction of althea and fennel and melilot in water, and let him be administered; then let the patient be laid on his back, and put under the buttock a piece of wool equal, neither too soft nor too hard, then put the foot of the sick person's heel on the wool, and raise the head of the shoulder virtuously, and draw the hand of the sick person; and another minister holds the head of the sick person, so that he does not move down; this shoulder returns now, and if you see it, reset it in this manner: and it is that you make a man present who is taller than the patient; and let him be straight towards the rib cage, and put his shoulder under the buttock of the patient, and raise the buttock upwards, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister draws the hand of the sick person down towards the belly. 
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can lift anything heavy with him, and the dislocation returns now. 
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And it is set in another manner: and there is put a long piece of wood into the earth, on which the shoulder is as if it were a bed, and neither too large nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but he must have blankets above him, and the patient should lie on the length of the staff; then the hand is stretched out on the other side, forming the joint, and it will return to its place immediately; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stick from the arm of great size and four spans wide, which has the head round so as to fit in between the shoulder blades, according to this form: 
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie on top of the staff cloth above, that the staff does not sting the patient, then place it under the buttocks of the patient; and extend his arm on the staff of the long, and tie the shoulder to the staff, and the arm to the head of the hand, then put the arm onto one rung of a ladder wide, and let the hands be extended down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in, in whatever manner that it is, it behoves you to put under the saddle a sphere of wool even, then put the emplasters prepared powder from the mill, with incense and auburn of egg, on all the shoulder and around, then restrain it under the saddle evenly, and turn the linen on the emplasters, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it behoves that he move little, as long as the limbs are strengthened, because it will heal faster; and then move more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is hardened and it is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another cause, then you must administer cautery to III places, as it is shown in front of or chapter of cautery. 
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all these things, and he unties after .vii. days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is severed or extended or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the hip, and the breasts, or behind, is made by impulse, and extension of hands, and it administers in another place; and cure until it be healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes pain to the limb, and slowness of movement, then use the patient baths many times, until that pain is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated to many places, and returns to many places; and it is dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not replaced, because one sees it well and feels it well; and dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased knife with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.  
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch his shoulder at all. 
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it thus as if abscesses come from there, because if abscesses came from there, it would be grievous to bring it back; and by chance, it may not be able to be brought back completely at all, even when it is behind; so it is worse than the other dislocations, and it is of greater pain, and by chance death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is thus, when it is such that one can bring it back, that you extend your hand to its two hands; and its arms should be spread out, and the hands touch according to the blade around, above and below, and push the joint to its breast together, or to the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and fire of the root of the palm the blade which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and let two ministers extend the arm, and they hold it so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm in each direction, then when you have enveloped a double, long and wide cloth; and when the minister joins the joint with his hand, he puts oil on any oil to soften the joint, then pushes the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, put a dry plaster on top with egg white, and bind it tightly, and place the arm on the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then untie it. 
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, untie the bandage and leave it; and if you see that the joint isn't well set, begin again with the plaster and bandage, and leave it so for some days, until it is firmly placed; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after resetting the joint, and it moves, bathe him and rub him well, and press until he is soothed; or put on the joint a lambskin fleece, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the fleece back on, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until he is healed; and if you see that, put on a moist chaff fin with butter, and strain it on; it will return to its place. 
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is lighter than the other joints. However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place immediately when it is dislocated, so that the joint does not swell or become inflamed with heat.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the setting back is that you put the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and he places his hand equal, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns to its place; it is necessary that you look if it is well in place; then put the sick one's back of his hand on a table at extension and setting back.  
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient puts the back of their hand on the table, and the healer places their hand above the appearance of the joint. 
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, it is well
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you are unable to put it back in place after some days, the joint remains twisted; and does no harm to the patient except that as long as his hand is numbed, and cannot exert anything: therefore know that the nerves are cut, or the artery; there is no other remedy but to constrain by cautery according to the case, and perhaps it is not worth any other thing.  
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the splint that we have said, then restrain it and leave it for 5 days, then untie it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is no wound, then moisten it with hot water, and rub it until it is sound.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the bones of the hand are dislocated to each side, sometimes on the back of the palm or on the belly; then is the bone and push the dislocation to your pockets until it comes back, then support the head of the bone, and the bend towards the side where it is disjoined; and let him rest two days, and then put it straight that day; and don't tie it, as we have said, and untie it day by day, and make it move, and tie it again tight; and do this often, until it is tight, and just as well, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healthy; and just as well, when it is dislocated from another side. 
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or the neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, if there is no cure, because death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs of this are that the gesticulations jump without will, and he cannot hold them, and many times they are softened any limb, or the two thighs or the two arms or one. And many times the spine moves in four parts; that which moves to the back is called "gilbositez": the cure of this is that you return it if the gilbositez came from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing at all. 
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or percussion or similar things, the ancients said methods of cures by great words, in which there is no great profit at all; but I have abridged it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways. 
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the inflammation that comes to the breast in front, there is nothing healing; and also the one that comes straight into II sides, and one can cure only the one properly that comes on the back, as I said; and it is that the patient is extended on his face in the place equal, and has strain under him so that he does not move; then put the stick to the chief in earth formed, and the other at the feet, and tie a linen around the sides of the sick person, and the other at the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two ministers hold the ligatures, one at the head and the others at the feet, among the II sticks; and be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the mire puts its palms on the spine formed, until it returns. 
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, then take a board of three arms long, and place it under the armpit, and the patient should be on his side, and put the head of the board under the armpit, then put the middle of the board on the spine; and put the patient's feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, then do it with the turn that turns by hand. 
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And is that you put II sticks to the chief of the sick person's arm from great, and towards the feet II others, and have between each stick, desoure and desoz, a palm of space long; and have in each stick I pertu, or the turning, correct, and be the sticks firmly in earth, so that they do not move; and between each II sticks have I tison turning, over which the lien turn, and have in II turning II small sticks from a palm long, to return the turning; and then tie the linen which is among the assels to the turning towards the chief, and the other linen towards the feet to the other turning, and each of the ministers turns his turning all of the linen, and the master puts the spine equal as we have said.
