Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, he places a drying plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the bandages, and then the splint of a tablet of III fingers long, that holds the place of the vertebra and the part of the spine straight, then tie it with a linen band, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle nursing, until he is healed; and if any thing comes at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and assuaging medicines, with the splint that we have said before; and sometimes one administers a piece of wood, and sometimes the appearance comes in the back vertebra of the back, and one thinks that it is dislocations; and it is the bone that opens, so one must not have presumption: by chance it might bring death. 
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come out only dislocations, not as other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated into .iiij. parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and less dislocated front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and opens more the patient's knee than the healthy one, and the patient cannot double his knee at all; and it is the thigh which is below swollen with a hot abscess, because the head of the hip comes there. 
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes on the outward side, is that this accident is contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it happens in front, is that his leg is well aligned according to its completion; nonetheless, he does not double his knee without pain, and if one wants him to go forward, he cannot before, and he retains his urine, and swells his anger, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it happens behind, is that he cannot spread his knee or double it, and his leg is more twisted than the other, and his anger is softened, and his hip is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this kind of dislocation is that you examine if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no need for any treatment; and he must not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those whose dislocation is fresh, and there are .iiij. ways of dislocation, so haste that you return the joint, and the extension inside and outside, and the movement to right and left; by chance it will return, and needs no other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must set the minister strongly, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or to the ligature that is tied above the knee; and another minister extends his hand upwards in such a manner that he pushes his hands beneath his shoulders, then tightens with a ligature on the hip; and another holds the head of the limb; and extend both up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.  
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, then it is necessary to take care of its appearance. When a dislocation is in the back, you must lie down the patient on his healthy side, then place the linen on the root of the hip, and the part that is below the angle, then extend the linen upwards towards the angle, and towards the thigh; then grasp other ministers with his arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased hip, and extend it outwards: now it will return to its place; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others. 
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen bandage above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then hang it on the top of a pole, and let it be two arms length above the ground; then command to the minister that he embrace the head of the hip, and let there be other ministers hanging with the sick person, who embrace firmly the hips, because the joint now returns readily. 
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is at the rear, he lies the patient, as we have said in the one who has gout, and restricts the linen on the leg wounded properly, and on the foot also; then puts II sticks, I at the head and I other at the foot, then puts I stick between the hips of the wounded man in the form; and a planchette of moist cloths around, that he does not sweat the wounded one, then extend each minister towards him, and the mire puts equal to his hand the dislocation. 
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good. 
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If this is not so, put him on a table,  and press him as we have said in the glossary, and lay the patient on his healthy side. 
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the injured leg as far as possible and according to what I have said; and put his pain on the suffering angle, then press with the other hand, and guide it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is at the hip, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards, nor raise him up on the ground, but rather he should be as if his hip had been dislocated outwards, as we have said about the couching on the two hips; and be on his face, and the bandage extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint to the table; and it will be right when the patient extends his legs, and they will be equal; therefore adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and the strain of a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three days or four, then untie it, and put the splint on top; and if you see that they are equal, strain them, as before, and leave it for three days; then untie it, and let him walk well, until the limb is strengthened. 
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg to his hip, and if it does not rest on his hip, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit straight, and extend his leg as far as he can, and you put your back on his thigh, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and retract between your two hands, then bend the two bones that form the knee; and other assistants extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he will rest his leg on his hip lightly; and put the plaster on, and make him hold his leg to his hip, and tie them together firmly for III days or IIII, then untie it; and do not let the patient work at all, as long as the limb is strengthened. 
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not in place, administer a strong stretching, as we have said in the cure of the hip, until it is healed. 
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely dislocated, inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs of it are that the ankle is swollen, and tender before the part where it is dislocated: the resetting of it is light, and one must extend it gently with their hands when it is only bruised.  
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, it is necessary that you make the patient sit straight, and hold him with ministers except by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot to you with your right hand, and then with the left two times, then the end up, and push the foot well upwards; and do this two times, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is well; if not, begin the work again, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and put a stick firmly into the ground between his hips, and tie bandages around it so that it does not move the patient; then hold the ministers the hip, and others extend the foot to their hands or at the ankle, so that they lie on the collar of the foot; then extend each minister equally, and the sticks be well between the hips of the patient to hold the patient when we extend him; then put the healers equal dislocation in his hands, and other ministers hold the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return easily.  
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is pointed, put the plaster and dressings on it, and strain it firmly, and tie its foot to the leg, and guard the nerves which are above the heel behind, so that the bandages be not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages soften, tighten them again; then untie it on the third day or fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.  
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to it then you must soothe it as we have said elsewhere until it is healed.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the hips are dislocated, it is necessary to extend them well without effort, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a table totally straight, and put your foot on what opens of these joints, then press with your foot firmly, until it returns; and when it is aligned, and there is nothing open, then put under the sole of the foot a board at the shoulder, then strain it firmly, and leave it for III days, then untie it; and let him rest, until he is healed. 
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wants to restore it, many times happens that the patient dies: so be not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and tardy, nor bold; and use at the beginning of soothing things abscess hot, and let the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscesses warm come; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing things abscess hot, and cure the wound, as it befits, with dry dressings; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones broken, set them, and do what we have said in simple ailments; and guard yourself from entering into a way of fear, according to what I have said, for this will cause you death according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapon and body. 
Amen	Amen
